## Phase 5: Structured Diagnostics and Language Refinements

### 5.1: Tooling (CLI, Formatter, Testing)

- [x] **`defer` and `errdefer` implementation (AST + parser).** Add `Defer` and `Errdefer` AST nodes. Parser: recognise `defer expr` and `errdefer expr` / `errdefer(binding) { block }`. Ensure reverse declaration order (LIFO) execution at scope exit. Enforce: no `?` inside defer/errdefer blocks (compile error), no capture-by-move. `errdefer` runs only on error paths (`?` propagation or explicit `return Err(...)`). The `errdefer(e)` binding has the type of the function's `Err` variant. Effects from defer/errdefer bodies contribute to the enclosing function's inferred effect set.

- [x] **Pipe operator `|>` (AST + parser).** Implement left-to-right function chaining. Parser: `_` as pipe-hole placeholder (at most one per stage). Precedence: lower than arithmetic/comparison/function call, higher than `=`. `?` interaction: `|>` binds tighter than `?`, so `raw |> parse?` means `(raw |> parse)?`.

- [x] **CLI (`karac build/run/check/fmt/query`).** Binary entry point (`src/main.rs`) and argument parsing (`src/cli.rs`). Subcommands: `build` (compile + report), `run` (compile + execute), `check` (type-check without executing), `fmt` (format), `query` (inspect compiler analysis). Foundation for all other Phase 5 tooling.

- [x] **`--output=json` structured diagnostics.** Machine-readable JSON output across all compiler phases. Every diagnostic includes source span, severity, phase, message, and machine-applicable fix diff where possible. Enables AI agents to parse errors and apply fixes mechanically.

- [x] **`karac fmt`: canonical formatter.** Wire `src/formatter.rs` into the CLI. Deterministic output so diffs are semantic-only. Idempotent ŌĆö formatting already-formatted code produces no changes.

- [x] **Diagnostic snapshot tests.** Golden-file tests (`tests/snapshots/`) that freeze error message format and catch unintended regressions. Each `.kara` fixture produces a snapshot of structured diagnostics that is diffed against the expected output.

- [x] **Fuzz testing.** `cargo-fuzz` harnesses for lexer, parser, and full pipeline (`fuzz/fuzz_targets/`). Catch panics, hangs, and crashes on malformed input. Run periodically, not in CI.

- [x] **`karac doc` ŌĆö doc comment extraction and rendering (MVP).** Shipped 2026-04-28 (commit `e6bf3c3`). Parser attaches `doc_comment` to all 9 item kinds; `src/doc.rs` renders one CommonMarkŌåÆHTML page per item under `dist/doc/<module-path>/` plus a flat `index.html`; `karac doc` CLI subcommand walks the project. This is the skeleton; the open `karac doc` follow-ups below build against it.

- [x] **`karac doc`: cross-reference link resolution.** Shipped 2026-04-28 (round 2, commit `7b98626`). `build_link_table` walks every non-synthetic module and records `name ŌåÆ relative-href`. The renderer plumbs the table into a `pulldown-cmark` `BrokenLinkCallback`; resolved hrefs are computed relative to the current page's directory via `relative_link(page_dir, doc_root, target_rel)`. Unresolved refs render as plain text (no warning).

- [x] **`karac doc`: per-page struct field and enum variant tables.** Shipped 2026-04-28 (round 2, commit `7b98626`). `render_item_extras` / `render_struct_extras` / `render_enum_extras` emit `<h2>Fields</h2>` / `<h2>Variants</h2>` sections with `<dl class="fields">` / `<ul class="variants">` listings.

- [x] **`karac doc`: per-field and per-variant doc comments.** Shipped 2026-04-28 (round 3, commit `21f806a`). `StructField` and `Variant` carry `doc_comment: Option<String>`; parser collects `///` at field/variant/struct-variant-payload parse sites; doc renderer surfaces the prose alongside the existing `name: TypeExpr` row. Item-level `take_pending_doc` had to move ahead of body parsing in `parse_struct_def` / `parse_enum_def` to avoid clobbering by child collection.

- [x] **`karac doc`: JSON search index.** Shipped 2026-04-28 (round 3, commit `b7f3fb2`). `dist/doc/search-index.json` emitted alongside `index.html`. Schema: JSON array, one entry per documented item, `{name, kind, href, summary}`. `summarize_doc` strips ATX heading markers and trims; `json_escape_string` is local to `doc.rs`. Always emitted, even for empty projects, so a deployed site has a stable URL.

- [x] **`karac doc`: declared + same-module inferred effect display in `pub fn` signatures.** Shipped 2026-04-28 (round 3, commit `67a2bc5`). `cmd_doc` runs `effectcheck` per non-synthetic module via `build_doc_effects_table`; `render_signature` appends ` with reads(...) + writes(...)` (or ` with _` / ` with fixed + _`) only for `pub fn`. `EffectDisplay` is a small flat struct in `doc.rs` (no `effectchecker::TracedEffect` / `EffectSet` leaking into the renderer). Source preference: declared annotations win, fall back to inferred. Cross-module inferred effects are tracked separately below.

- [x] **`karac doc`: per-param doc comments.** Shipped 2026-04-29 (round 4). `Param` carries `doc_comment: Option<String>`; `parse_param` collects `///` and consumes via `take_pending_doc` at construction. The item-level `take_pending_doc` was hoisted ahead of body parsing in `parse_function`, `parse_trait_def`, and `parse_extern_function` to avoid clobbering by per-param collection (same shape as the round-3 struct/enum fix). `render_param_extras` emits `<h2>Parameters</h2>` + `<dl class="params">` of `<dt>name: Type</dt><dd>doc</dd>` rows; renders only when at least one param has a doc, full param list shows when triggered. `///` before `self` is unsupported ŌĆö a known carve-out, not covered.

- [x] **`karac doc`: `//!` module-level doc comments.** Shipped 2026-04-29 (round 4). Lexer emits a distinct `Token::ModuleDocComment(text)` (with a parallel update to `skip_whitespace` so `//!` isn't swallowed as a regular comment). `parse_program` consumes a leading run of `ModuleDocComment` tokens into `Program.module_doc_comment: Option<String>`; `module.rs` plumbs the string through `ParsedFile` ŌåÆ `Module.module_doc_comment` (with both the merged-test-companion and default paths covered, and `None` for the synthetic prelude). `render_index` renders the crate-root `//!` above the items table inside `<div class="module-doc crate-root-doc">`; non-root modules get a `<tr><td colspan="3"><div class="module-doc">ŌĆ”</div></td></tr>` row preceding their item rows. Trailing `//!` (mid-file) is currently a parse error ŌĆö known limitation, callers are expected to keep `//!` at the top.

- [x] **`karac doc`: per-field rendering inside struct-variant payloads.** Shipped 2026-04-29 (round 4). The struct-variant arm of `render_enum_extras` now switches on whether any field has a `///`: if so, renders the variant as `Name { <dl class="variant-fields">...</dl> }` with `<dt>name: Type</dt><dd>doc</dd>` rows; otherwise keeps the original inline `Variant { f: T, g: U }` shape. Required a parser-side fix: `parse_variant` now hoists `take_pending_doc` ahead of the struct-payload parse so the variant's own doc isn't clobbered by per-field collection.

- [x] **`karac doc`: cross-module inferred-effect display.** Shipped 2026-04-29 (round 4). Restructured `cli::build_doc_effects_table` to merge every non-synthetic module's items into a single `Program` and run `effectcheck` once on the merged unit, instead of per-module. The effectchecker indexes functions by bare name and K─üra's `import` brings callees into scope under their bare name, so the merge resolves cross-module calls in `extract_callee_name` lookups. A `pub fn` in module A that calls a `pub fn` in module B (whether via declared effects or via inference) now picks up B's effects in A's inferred set, and the doc renderer surfaces them in the `with` clause when A has no explicit declaration. Trade-off: function-name collisions across modules are approximated (the merge keeps one); doc-only ŌĆö main pipeline still runs effectcheck per-module. Effectcheck errors raised by the merged pass (duplicate decls, missing effect declarations) are deliberately ignored ŌĆö the doc renderer is best-effort. Files: `src/cli.rs`, `tests/doc.rs`. No changes to `src/effectchecker.rs` were needed (List 2 disjointness preserved).

- [x] **`karac doc`: per-module index pages.** Shipped 2026-04-29 (round 4). Each non-synthetic, non-crate-root module that has at least one documented item OR a `//!` module-doc gets its own `<module>/index.html` (`render_module_index`) listing only that module's items, with the module-doc rendered above the table when present and a "ŌåÉ crate root" back-link computed via `relative_link`. Item-page nav switched from `../index.html` to `./index.html` so it resolves to the current module's index (or the global index for crate-root items). Modules with neither docs nor a `//!` block produce no index page. The root `index.html` keeps the full-crate listing ŌĆö this is purely additive scoping ahead of the sidebar-nav item below. Files: `src/doc.rs`, `tests/doc.rs`.

- [x] **`karac doc`: full-site sidebar navigation.** Shipped 2026-04-29 (round 4). Every page renders an `<aside class="sidebar">` listing modules ŌåÆ items in a tree of `<details open>` blocks (no JS ŌĆö pure CSS via `<details>`). Modules appear iff they have at least one documented item or a `//!` (matches the per-module index emit condition). All hrefs are computed via `relative_link(page_dir, doc_root, target)` so the same logical link works from a crate-root page (`Foo.html`), a deep page (`../Foo.html`), or the root index. `build_docs` was restructured into a pre-walk (collect `IndexEntry`s) + render pass so the sidebar is fully populated before any page is written. CSS factored into a single shared `SHARED_CSS` constant used by all three page templates; layout is a flexbox 2-column with the sidebar fixed at 240px on the left. Item / per-module / global render functions all gained a `sidebar_html: &str` parameter. Files: `src/doc.rs`, `tests/doc.rs`.

- [x] **`karac doc`: design.md attachment-rule spec.** Shipped 2026-04-29 (round 4). Added a top-level `## Doc Comments` section to `docs/design.md` (between Performance Diagnostics and Secret Type, with TOC entry). Covers: the two syntaxes (`///` item-level, `//!` module-level), the line-joining rule (`\n` between consecutive lines, one leading space stripped), the positional attachment rule (no blank-line / token gap), the parser invariant for items whose body collects nested doc comments (item-level `take_pending_doc` must drain before descending), the supported targets (items, members, modules), the rendering contract (`pulldown-cmark` Options::all + cross-reference resolution by bare name), and the v1 carve-outs (no `self` doc, no mid-file `//!`, no path-qualified xrefs, no doc tests). Pure docs; no code changes.

- [x] **`karac check --profiles=<list|all>`.** CI-side flag that runs the effect checker N times against N profiles, exiting non-zero if any profile fails. `--profiles=all` iterates over every known profile; `--profiles=embedded,kernel` runs a specific subset. Output is per-profile grouped diagnostics (not interleaved). Closed 2026-05-01 ŌĆö see WIP block above for landed-implementation details. The `gpu` profile mentioned in the original spec was aspirational; v1 ships `default` / `embedded` / `kernel` per `manifest::CompileProfile`, and `--profiles=all` covers exactly that set today.

- [x] **`karac build --concurrency-report` ŌĆö human-readable concurrency analysis output (full Parallax demo).** Build-time CLI flag that runs the existing `concurrencycheck` analysis (already wired into `cmd_build` after auto-par codegen slice 2 landed) and renders the result in human-readable text alongside the binary build. The render output is the demo storyboard's exact prose shape (`docs/demo_ideas.md:80-88`): per parallel group, list the calls in source order with line numbers, list each call's reads/writes resources, and emit a one-sentence "why" explanation derived from the analyzer's existing reason field ŌĆö e.g., *"`fetch_profile`, `fetch_orders`, `fetch_notifications`, `fetch_recommendations` parallelize: no data dependencies; no effect conflicts: different resources, all reads."* The structured-JSON output via `karac query concurrency` is unchanged; this is a renderer additive, not a new analysis pass. **The recordable terminal-side artifact for the Parallax demo** ŌĆö pairs with the binary's auto-par execution to make the compiler's reasoning visible alongside the speedup.

### 5.2: Language Features

- [x] **Labeled loops.** Extend lexer/parser to support `label: for/while/loop` syntax. `break label` and `continue label` target the named loop. `break label expr` exits the named loop with a value. Labels are bare identifiers with colon (Go/Java style, no sigil). Resolver validates that break/continue labels refer to an enclosing loop.

- [x] **Labeled blocks (`label: { ... }`).** Extend the parser to accept `IDENT ":" BLOCK` as an expression form (`LABELED_BLOCK` per syntax.md ┬¦5.3) ŌĆö sibling to labeled loops. Resolver and typechecker treat a labeled block as a `break` target: `break label` and `break label expr` from inside the block exit it (with value), the block's type is the LUB of all reachable `break label expr` value types and the tail expression's type, and the existing labeled-loop machinery for label-scope and unknown-label diagnostics is shared. **`continue label` referring to a labeled block is a compile error** (`continue label refers to a labeled block; continue is only valid for loops`) with a fix-it pointing at the label binding. A `break` inside a closure body cannot target an enclosing label (parity with the existing labeled-loop closure-boundary rule). Test coverage: bare-`break label` exits with `()`, value-carrying `break label expr` joined with the tail expression, multi-`break` LUB inference, nested labeled blocks shadowing same-name label, unknown-label diagnostic, `continue label` referring to a labeled block diagnostic, closure-body `break` rejection, label scope ends at the closing `}` (later use of the same identifier as a `break` target outside is unknown-label). Phase target: 5.2 (Language Features). Cross-reference: `docs/design.md` ┬¦ Loops > **Labeled blocks**, syntax.md ┬¦5.3.

- [x] **Labeled blocks ŌĆö codegen + interpreter sibling slice.** Wire runtime semantics for `LabeledBlock` so `break label expr` actually exits the block with the value (codegen + interpreter), and route `break label` (without value) to the same exit. Frontend slice (commit `85e49c8`, 2026-05-09) shipped parser + resolver + typechecker; today both backends fall through their `_ =>` catch-alls (codegen returns the i64 zero sentinel; interpreter returns `Value::Unit`), so the typed program compiles but runs wrong. **Latent bonus fix:** today's `LoopFrame` carries no `label` field and `compile_break` always targets `loop_stack.last()`, so nested labeled loops where `break outer` should bypass `inner` would silently miscompile to break the innermost loop instead. No test fixture exercises this (grep `tests/` for nested labeled loops returns zero hits), but the codegen slice closes the gap as a side-effect because the same label-aware lookup serves both labeled blocks and labeled loops.

- [x] **Named/labeled function arguments.** Extend parser to accept `name: expr` at call sites. Labels must follow declaration order. Partial labeling allowed (any suffix). Receiver (`self`) cannot be labeled. Labels are documentation ŌĆö never required.

- [x] **`seq {}` block.** Suppress auto-parallelism within the block. All statements execute in source order. Block is an expression (value is last statement). Bindings declared inside are scoped to the block, consistent with all other blocks. Extract values via expression value or tuple.

- [x] **Const generics ŌĆö full surface.** Implement the spec in `design.md ┬¦ Type Inference > Const generic parameters`. Decomposed into four execution slices below; this parent bullet holds the surface-level design record, the cross-slice invariants, and the resolved design forks from the 2026-05-10 code investigation.

  *Already-shipped baseline (verified 2026-05-10).* AST carries `GenericParam { is_const, const_type }` and `GenericArg::Type | Const(Expr)` at `src/ast.rs:684-703`. Parser accepts `const NAME: TYPE` at every declaration site (`src/parser.rs:2095-2118`) and routes literal-leading const-arg expressions (`Integer / -Integer / true / false`) to `GenericArg::Const` at `src/parser.rs:2333-2360`. Resolver defines const params in the same scope as type params at `src/resolver.rs:2645-2657` (under `SymbolKind::TypeParam` ŌĆö kind-distinction is part of slice 1). Codegen has literal-only `Array[T, N]` element-size extraction at `src/codegen.rs:1787-1799`. **Slice 1 builds on this baseline rather than starting fresh.**

  *Locked design forks (2026-05-10).*
  - **F1 ŌĆö Substitution context shape.** Generalize `HashMap<String, Type>` (typechecker `substitute_type_params` at `src/typechecker.rs:603`) and `HashMap<String, BasicTypeEnum<'ctx>>` (codegen `type_subst` at `src/codegen.rs:724`) to a single `HashMap<String, SubstValue>` per side, where `SubstValue` is `Type(...)` or `Const(ConstValue)`. Reuses the existing `ConstValue` enum at `src/prelude.rs:230` (already covers i8..i128, u8..u64, usize, f32, f64; slice 2 extends with bool/char/enum-variant). Rejected alternative: parallel type/const maps (threading two maps gets ugly when slice 2's evaluator surfaces const-param refs in many more places).
  - **F2 ŌĆö Mono key shape.** Extend `mangle_mono_name` at `src/codegen.rs:17677-17697` to walk const-typed generic params and append the const value's mangle string. The mangled name *is* the mono key (stored in `generated_monos: HashSet<String>`); no new data structure. Today's mangler silently skips const params (lookup misses on the type-only `type_subst` map) ŌĆö slice 1 closes this latent bug.
  - **F3 ŌĆö Interpreter sharing.** The interpreter has no mono dispatch; generics are type-erased and `Value` is polymorphic. The typechecker plumbs const-arg values through `expr_types` annotations, and the interpreter consumes them implicitly. **Slice 4 is codegen-only.**

  *Cross-slice invariants.* Existing `Array[T, N]` and Tensor `[const N: i64]` parenthetical references are the integration test surface and must continue to type-check after every slice lands. Const params do not appear in runtime type representation (compile-time-only ŌĆö invariant for slices 1 and 4). Phase target: 5.2 (Language Features). Comptime / `const fn` user-callable extensions stay deferred ŌĆö see roadmap "Future: Comptime."

  Decomposed:
  1. [x] **Frontend foundation + typechecker baseline (narrowed surface).** Ō£ō Landed 2026-05-10. Originally drafted as "Frontend foundation + typechecker baseline + monomorphization key" (merged from the 2026-05-10 slice-1 / slice-2 split). At execution time the F2 codegen mono key and the call-site literal-const-arg binding were discovered to depend on **expression-side const-generic-args** that the AST doesn't carry ŌĆö `ExprKind::Path` at `src/ast.rs:820-823` has `generic_args: Option<Vec<TypeExpr>>` (TypeExpr only, no `GenericArg::Const`). Without that plumbing, `make_arr[i64, 4]()` at a call site can't carry a literal `4` through to codegen. F2 + literal binding lift out to **Slice 1b** (next bullet). What landed in slice 1: (a) **Parser** ŌĆö extended `parse_generic_type_args` at `src/parser.rs:2333` to route `Identifier <binary op>` shapes (e.g. `Array[T, N + 1]`) to `GenericArg::Const`; added `WhereConstraint::ConstPredicate { expr, span }` AST variant and a backtracking parser branch in `parse_optional_where_clause` at `src/parser.rs:2174` to accept `where N >= 0` / `where M < 4096`. (b) **Resolver** ŌĆö added `SymbolKind::ConstParam` variant; `define_generic_params` at `src/resolver.rs:2645` branches on `param.is_const` to pick the kind; existing dup-name detection covers the type-vs-const name collision diagnostic without kind-aware special-casing. (c) **Typechecker ŌĆö declaration-site permitted-type rejection** ŌĆö `validate_const_param_types` resolves each const param's `const_type: TypeExpr` to a `Type` via `lower_type_expr`, rejects anything outside the spec-allowed set (i8 / i16 / i32 / i64, bool, char, fieldless enum) with a focused diagnostic citing the spec section. (d) **F1 substitution context shape change** ŌĆö `substitute_type_params` at `src/typechecker.rs:603` now accepts `&HashMap<String, SubstValue>` where `SubstValue = Type(Type) | Const(crate::prelude::ConstValue)`; all 9 caller sites + the internal `Type::AssocProjection` recursion patched; `SubstValue::as_type` extracts the type payload for `Type::TypeParam(name)` lookups, passing through unchanged for `Const` entries. Exhaustive-match patches for `WhereConstraint::ConstPredicate` added in resolver / formatter / typechecker. Test coverage: 9 new tests across `tests/parser.rs` (const-arg `N + 1` expression, where-clause const predicate), `tests/resolver.rs` (ConstParam kind, type-vs-const name collision), `tests/typechecker.rs` (permitted-types accepted, rejects usize / f32 / f64 / String / fieldful enum). **`i128` permitted-type carve-out:** spec lists `i128` as permitted, but `IntSize` doesn't have an `I128` variant yet (per `phase-4-interpreter.md`); slice 1's permitted-set check accepts every `Type::Int(_)` size that *currently* exists. Slice 2's `ConstValue` extension adds `I128`/`U128`; the permitted-set check will need re-verification when `IntSize::I128` lands. **Predecessor for slice 1b.**

     **Slice 1b.** Ō£ō Landed 2026-05-11. Expression-side const-generic-args (the prerequisite that surfaced at slice 1 close-out) + call-site const-arg binding + F2 codegen mono-key extension. What landed:
     - **AST**: `ExprKind::Path.generic_args` widened from `Option<Vec<TypeExpr>>` to `Option<Vec<GenericArg>>` at `src/ast.rs:820-826`. Touches 3 inline test-shape patches in `tests/parser.rs` (the existing UFCS-path tests destructure on the new variant).
     - **Parser**: `parse_call_site` UFCS path delegates to the shared `parse_generic_type_args` so concrete-type UFCS calls (`Type[T, 4].method()`) accept mixed type / const args alongside the post-slice-1 routing for `Identifier <op>` and literal-leading shapes. New `lookahead_generic_args_call` helper recognizes the bare-identifier-with-explicit-generic-args call shape `name[T1, T2, ŌĆ”](args)` (requires a top-level `,` inside the brackets + matching `]` immediately followed by `(`) and routes through `ExprKind::Path { segments: [name], generic_args: Some(_) }`. Single-arg brackets stay as `Index` so `callbacks[0]()` keeps parsing.
     - **Typechecker**: `infer_call` recognizes `Path { segments: [name], generic_args: Some(_) }` with one-segment paths as a bare-identifier free-fn call by synthesizing a fresh `Identifier` callee and re-entering the dispatch. The codegen reads the original AST (which preserves `generic_args`) for mango-key disambiguation; the typechecker doesn't validate const-arg type compatibility at slice 1b ŌĆö call-site const-arg type validation lands at slice 3.
     - **Codegen**: `compile_call` extracts the `(name, explicit_generic_args)` pair from either an `Identifier` callee or a `Path { segments: [name], generic_args: Some(_) }` callee. `compile_generic_call` accepts the optional explicit args and builds a parallel `const_subst: HashMap<String, ConstValue>` from literal `GenericArg::Const(...)` payloads via the new `const_value_from_literal_expr` helper. `mangle_mono_name` now takes `const_subst` alongside the existing `type_subst` and branches on `param.is_const` to pick which side to consult; `const_value_to_mangle_str` renders the const value as the mangle token (integers carry their width suffix so `4i64` and `4i32` produce distinct symbols; bool as `true`/`false`; char as `c{codepoint}`; enum-variant as `EnumName.VariantName`). **Parallel-maps caveat:** F2's full reshape of `type_subst` to `HashMap<String, SubstValue<'ctx>>` is **not** done at slice 1b. The slice 1 plan rejected the parallel-maps approach on the grounds that "slice 2's evaluator surfaces const-param refs in many more places" ŌĆö but slice 2 shipped without threading `SubstValue` through the call-site solver (that's slice 3's surface). For slice 1b's mango-key disambiguation, the parallel maps are clean. Slice 4's codegen body lowering for const-param identifier resolution is where the F2 full reshape will pay off; do it then.
     - **Test surface** (3 new): `tests/parser.rs` (`test_parser_call_site_explicit_generic_args` ŌĆö `make_arr[i64, 4]()` parses as `Call { callee: Path { segments: ["make_arr"], generic_args: Some([Type(i64), Const(Integer(4))]) }, args: [] }`; `test_parser_indexed_call_still_parses_as_index_then_call` ŌĆö `callbacks[0]()` regression-pin keeps Index-then-Call shape), `tests/codegen.rs` (`test_ir_const_generic_mono_key_disambiguation` ŌĆö `make_arr[i64, 4]()` and `make_arr[i64, 8]()` produce two distinct compiled symbols `make_arr$i64$4i64` and `make_arr$i64$8i64`).

     **Out of scope for slice 1b** (continuing as future work):
     - **Single-arg explicit generic args at lowercase free-fn callsites** (`f[8]()`). **Shipped at slice 1c (2026-05-11)** ŌĆö the disambiguation runs at type-check / codegen time rather than at parse time. See slice 1c entry below.
     - **F2 full reshape** of `type_subst` to `HashMap<String, SubstValue<'ctx>>`. Slice 4 owns this.
     - **Const-arg type compatibility validation** at call sites (e.g., rejecting `f[true]()` when `f`'s formal const-param is `const N: i64`). Slice 3 owns this via the call-site solver.

     **Slice 1c.** Ō£ō Landed 2026-05-11 (commit `7e128cc`). Single-arg explicit generic-args call shape `f[8]()` at lowercase free-function call sites. The parser can't disambiguate this from `callbacks[0]()` (a documented Kara design pattern for calling a function stored in a Vec ŌĆö see `tests/interpreter.rs:1985`), so the disambiguation runs at type-check / codegen time. What landed:
     - **Typechecker**: `infer_call` recognizes both `Path { segments: [name], generic_args: Some(_) }` (slice 1b multi-arg shape) and `Index { object: Identifier(name), index: literal }` (slice 1c single-arg shape) callees. Both dispatch through the new `infer_explicit_generic_args_call` which threads the function's formal `generic_params` + the user-supplied args into `check_call_args_with_substitution_full`.
     - **check_call_args_with_substitution_full**: extended variant that pre-binds metavars from explicit generic args. After `instantiate_signature_with_fresh_vars` mints fresh metavars, walks `(formal_name, explicit_arg)` pairs in declaration order; const-typed formals bind their ConstVar to the literal value via `const_value_from_literal`, type-typed formals bind their TypeVar to the lowered Type.
     - **contains_type_param** extended to detect `ConstArg::ConstParam` in `Type::Array.size` so the generic-call inference path fires for signatures whose only generic dependency is a const-param. Pre-slice-1c this returned false for `Array[i64, ConstParam(N)]` and the generic-call inference was skipped (the call collapsed to its return type without resolving N).
     - **Codegen**: `compile_call` mirrors the typechecker disambiguation, routing `Index { obj: Identifier(name), index: literal }` to `compile_generic_call` with the literal as an explicit `GenericArg::Const` when `name` is a known generic function. The Vec-of-functions case continues to work because `callbacks` isn't in `generic_fns` / `env.functions` ŌĆö the rewrite skips it.

     Test surface (3 new): `test_const_inference_explicit_arg_list_single` (`fn f[const N: i64]() -> Array[i64, N]` called as `f[8]()` resolves `N=8` from the explicit arg); `test_const_inference_explicit_arg_list_via_array_param` (`f[5](arr)` with N pinned from both explicit + arg type); `test_const_inference_indexed_callbacks_regression` (the `callbacks[0]()` Vec-of-functions pattern still type-checks unchanged).

  2. [x] **Const-expression evaluator (narrowed surface).** Ō£ō Landed 2026-05-11. Originally drafted to also extend `ConstValue` with `I128` / `U128` variants (fork C4); at execution we found that those require `IntSize::I128` / `UIntSize::U128` to exist first ŌĆö they don't (per `phase-4-interpreter.md` "i128/u128 currently rejected with a structured E0220 UnsupportedNumericSuffix diagnostic"). I128/U128 lift out to **Slice 2b** (next bullet); `test_const_eval_overflow_i128` regression-pin moves with them. What landed in slice 2:
     - **`ConstValue` extension** at `src/prelude.rs:239`: `Bool(bool)`, `Char(char)`, `EnumVariant { enum_name, variant_name, discriminant }` variants. `Copy` dropped (`EnumVariant`'s `String` payloads break it); 3 exhaustive-match consumers (`primitive_const_to_value`, `primitive_const_type`, `compile_primitive_const`) patched.
     - **`ConstEvalError` enum** with `NonConstShape` / `Overflow` / `UnaryOverflow` / `DivByZero` / `OutOfRange` / `TypeMismatch` / `UndefinedConst` / `ArithOnNonInt` / `LogicalOnNonBool` / `CompareIncomparable` / `CyclicConstDef` variants.
     - **`eval_const_expr(&mut self, expr, target_ty)`** on the typechecker (and free helpers `apply_unary` / `apply_binary` / `apply_arithmetic` / `apply_comparison` / `integer_to_const_value` / `const_value_to_array_size` / `const_value_type`). Handles integer literals (with suffix override + target-ty fallback), bool / char literals, `ExprKind::Identifier` resolving through `ConstDecl` lookup (with self-reference cycle detection ŌĆö `CyclicConstDef` chain), `ExprKind::Path` for fieldless-enum-variant lookup, unary `Neg` / `Not` (checked + bool / integer-bitwise dispatch), and binary arithmetic / bitwise / shift / comparison / logical with short-circuit `And` / `Or` semantics. Const-generic-param substitution via slice 1's `SubstValue` context is **not threaded** at slice 2 ŌĆö that wires in when slice 3's call-site solver passes the substitution map through.
     - **F1 shape change cascade**: `lower_type_expr` / `lower_path_type` / `lower_array_type` / `lower_slice_type` / `lower_generic_args` all moved from `&self` to `&mut self` so `lower_array_type` can call `eval_const_expr` + `emit_const_eval_error` on non-literal Array-size const-args. All 45 call sites checked clean by the borrow checker (every existing caller was already in `&mut self` context).
     - **`emit_const_eval_error`** renders each `ConstEvalError` variant as a `TypeErrorKind::TypeMismatch` diagnostic with focused messages (`format_const_value` + `binop_glyph` + `unaryop_glyph` helpers).
     - **`find_non_const_span` retired.** Default-parameter-value validation at `validate_default_params` routes through the new `validate_default_value_is_const` helper, which recurses on `Tuple` / `ArrayLiteral` composites (preserved legacy behavior ŌĆö composite default values continue to type-check) and otherwise routes leaves through `eval_const_expr`. **Pure improvement:** overflow / div-by-zero in default values now surfaces at compile time instead of slipping through.
     - **Parser tweak:** `parse_generic_type_args` extended to route `Token::CharLiteral(_)` to `GenericArg::Const` (alongside the slice-1 literal / `Identifier <op>` paths).
     - **Slice 3 hook** added at the `WhereConstraint::ConstPredicate` arm in `validate_where_clause`: `// TODO(const generics slice 3): bound-discharge engine` comment pointing to the per-call-site predicate evaluation site.

     Test coverage (11 new in `tests/typechecker.rs`): `Array[T, ...]` const-arg overflow at i8 / i16 (subsumed by i32) / i32 / u8, div-by-zero distinct from overflow, shift overshift, char arithmetic rejection (`Array[T, 'a' + 'b']`), const-arg arithmetic resolves (`Array[T, 2 + 3]`), `ConstDecl` reference flows through (`const TEN: i64 = 10; Array[i64, TEN + 1]`), default-param overflow caught (regression improvement), default-param call still rejected with legacy message, tuple-literal default still type-checks. Direct unit tests of the Bool / Char / EnumVariant evaluator branches via `pub(crate) eval_const_expr` are scaffolded as a follow-up ŌĆö slice 2's Array-routed integration covers the operator-surface ground.

     *Settled design forks (2026-05-10).*
     - **C1 ŌĆö Distinguish overflow vs divide-by-zero diagnostics.** Mechanically separable via Rust's `checked_div` returning `None` for both ŌĆö the evaluator dispatches on literal-zero rhs to pick the message. Rejected alternative: collapsing both under a single "arithmetic error" diagnostic ŌĆö worse user signal.
     - **C2 ŌĆö Bit shifts use checked semantics under "arithmetic."** `u8 << 8` overshift uses `checked_shl` and fires `ConstEvalError::Overflow`. Spec doesn't separately call out shifts; this is the natural fit under "arithmetic and comparison" without expanding the surface.
     - **C3 ŌĆö Arithmetic operators are integer-only; logical operators bool-only; comparison operators work on int/bool/char/enum-variant.** `+ - * / % << >>` reject on non-integer with `ConstEvalError::ArithOnNonInt`; logical `and` / `or` / `!` reject on non-bool with `ConstEvalError::LogicalOnNonBool`; `== != < <= > >=` work on any common type. `'a' + 'b'` rejected at the evaluator.
     - **C4 ŌĆö Add `I128(i128)` and `U128(u128)` variants to `ConstValue`.** **Deferred to slice 2b.** Lifted out at execution time after the `IntSize::I128` prerequisite gap surfaced.
     - **C5 ŌĆö Retire `find_non_const_span`.** Done via the `validate_default_value_is_const` helper that recurses on composites and routes leaves through `eval_const_expr`.

     Depends on slice 1.

     **Slice 2b.** Ō£ō Landed 2026-05-11. `ConstValue::I128(i128)` + `ConstValue::U128(u128)` variants + the upstream `IntSize::I128` / `UIntSize::U128` enum extensions. What landed:
     - **`IntSize::I128` + `UIntSize::U128`** at `src/typechecker.rs:108-127`. The slice-1 permitted-type check (`is_permitted_const_param_type`) automatically accepts the new variants since it allow-lists every `Type::Int(_)` and `Type::UInt(_)` variant.
     - **`type_from_int_suffix`** now routes `IntSuffix::I128`/`U128` to the new variants (the prior `E0220 UnsupportedNumericSuffix` rejection is retired).
     - **`primitive_type`** + **`PRELUDE_PRIMITIVES`** carry `"i128"` / `"u128"` so the resolver recognizes them as primitive type names.
     - **`ConstValue::I128(i128)` + `U128(u128)`** at `src/prelude.rs:239`. Three exhaustive-match consumers patched: `primitive_const_to_value` (interpreter ŌĆö coerces lossy to `Value::Int(i64)`), `primitive_const_type` (typechecker), `compile_primitive_const` (codegen ŌĆö uses LLVM's native `i128_type`).
     - **`eval_const_expr` integer-literal handler** routes `IntSuffix::I128`/`U128` to `Type::Int(IntSize::I128)`/`Type::UInt(UIntSize::U128)`; the prior `NonConstShape` rejection (slice-2 stub) is retired.
     - **`integer_to_const_value`** + **`apply_arithmetic`** + **`apply_comparison`** + **`apply_unary`** all gained `I128`/`U128` arms (checked-arithmetic / cmp / unary-neg using i128 / u128).
     - **`const_value_type`** + **`const_value_to_i64`** + **`const_value_as_u32`** + **`format_const_value`** + **`const_value_to_mangle_str`** + **`infer_operand_target_ty`** + the `impl_table_key` / `type_display` matches in typechecker ŌĆö all extended with `I128`/`U128` arms.
     - **`llvm_int_type_for_suffix`** maps `IntSuffix::I128`/`U128` to LLVM's `i128_type` (previously fell back to `i64_type` since the typechecker rejected the suffix upstream).

     **Caveats:**
     - **AST literal carrier is still i64.** `ExprKind::Integer(i64, Option<IntSuffix>)` bounds literals to i64 at parse time, so 128-bit values near the i128 extremes get truncated. Source-level literals like `1i128` work; `170141183460469231731687303715884105727i128` (i128::MAX) truncates. Widening the AST carrier to i128 is a separate slice ŌĆö pull-trigger when a kata demands large i128 literals.
     - **Interpreter coercion is lossy.** `primitive_const_to_value` casts `I128(v) as i64` and `U128(v) as i64`, truncating high bits. Today no path produces `ConstValue::I128`/`U128` values that exceed i64's range (the AST carrier above bounds them), so the loss is silent. A `Value::Int128(i128)` widening lands when the AST carrier widens.
     - **Codegen LLVM constants** use `i128_type().const_int(*v as u64, ...)` ŌĆö the inkwell `const_int` builder takes a u64, so the high 64 bits of an i128 are lost. Same source bound as above means today's literals round-trip clean.

     Test surface (2 new, both in `tests/typechecker.rs`): `test_const_eval_i128_arithmetic_resolves` (i128 binary arithmetic flows through eval_const_expr; the Array-size extraction coerces the resolved I128 to usize); `test_const_eval_u128_literal_typechecks` (u128 literal lowering + integer_to_const_value). Two pre-existing rejection tests (`test_integer_suffix_i128_rejected` / `test_integer_suffix_u128_rejected`) were inverted to accepted-tests. The original slice-2 plan also listed `test_const_eval_overflow_i128`; that test's intended overflow shape isn't easily reachable from source (literals are i64-bounded at parse time so source-level i128 arithmetic doesn't exceed i128's range), so the slice 2b regression-pin substitutes a positive-case "i128 arithmetic resolves" test.

  Skipped slice 2 test from the original plan (`test_const_eval_signed_min_div_neg_one`): `i8::MIN` as a literal isn't currently a Kara surface ŌĆö the test would need `(-128i8) / (-1i8)` or similar. The underlying `checked_div` Overflow vs DivByZero dispatch is exercised by `test_const_eval_div_by_zero` and `test_const_eval_overflow_i8`. File a regression-pin when negative-literal-MIN syntax lands.

     *Settled design forks (2026-05-10).*
     - **C1 ŌĆö Distinguish overflow vs divide-by-zero diagnostics.** `x / 0` triggers `ConstEvalError::DivByZero`; `i8::MIN / -1` triggers `ConstEvalError::Overflow`. Both are compile errors with distinct user-facing messages. Mechanically separable via Rust's `checked_div` returning `None` for both ŌĆö the evaluator dispatches on literal-zero rhs to pick the message. Rejected alternative: collapsing both under a single "arithmetic error" diagnostic ŌĆö worse user signal.
     - **C2 ŌĆö Bit shifts use checked semantics under "arithmetic."** `u8 << 8` overshift uses `checked_shl` and fires `ConstEvalError::Overflow`. Spec doesn't separately call out shifts; this is the natural fit under "arithmetic and comparison" without expanding the surface.
     - **C3 ŌĆö Arithmetic operators are integer-only; logical operators bool-only; comparison operators work on int/bool/char/enum-variant.** Spec phrasing "integer / bool / char / enum-variant arithmetic and comparison" is the union; concretely: `+ - * / % << >>` reject on non-integer with `ConstEvalError::ArithOnNonInt`; `&& || !` reject on non-bool with `ConstEvalError::LogicalOnNonBool`; `== != < <= > >=` work on any common type (orderings well-defined per type). `'a' + 'b'` rejected at the evaluator.
     - **C4 ŌĆö Add `I128(i128)` and `U128(u128)` variants to `ConstValue`.** Slice 1's permitted-type list includes `i128`; needs eval support. Touches `compile_primitive_const` at `src/codegen.rs:1874` and interpreter coercion at `src/interpreter.rs:798`. Rejected alternative: downgrade `i128` from "permitted at declaration" to "permitted but rejected at use" ŌĆö worse UX, splits the spec's allowed-type list across phases.
     - **C5 ŌĆö Retire `find_non_const_span`.** Replace its one caller (default-parameter-value validation at `src/typechecker.rs:5533`) with a check-only call into `eval_const_expr` (treat `Err(NonConstShape)` as the existing diagnostic, treat other errors as the same diagnostic with the narrower span ŌĆö catching `Overflow` at default-param sites is a positive side-effect, not a regression). Single source of truth for "is this expression a valid const?"

     Test coverage: per-width integer overflow (5 signed widths + 1 unsigned); divide-by-zero distinct from overflow; `i8::MIN / -1` overflow; shift overshift; char arithmetic rejection; char comparison acceptance; bool logical operators; fieldless-enum equality; `ConstDecl` reference flows through the evaluator; const-expression in `Array[T, N + 1]` argument position resolves; retired-predicate regression (existing default-parameter tests still pass). **Unlocks slice patterns** (next entry in this file) ŌĆö the `Array[T, N ŌłÆ prefix.len() ŌłÆ suffix.len()]` arithmetic depends on this evaluator. Depends on slice 1.

  3. [x] **Call-site inference + where-clause discharge.** All four sub-slices landed 2026-05-11 (3a Type-level refactor ŌåÆ 3b inference solver ŌåÆ 3c where-clause discharge ŌåÆ 3d deferred-F regression-pin). Slice 3a: Type-level `ConstArg` refactor + `lower_type_expr` Array arm + `substitute_type_params` const-arg substitution + the regression-pin distinguishability test. What's in 3a:
     - **`ConstArg` + `ConstVarId`** types at `src/typechecker.rs` near `TypeVarId`. `ConstArg::Literal(i64) | ConstParam(String) | ConstVar(ConstVarId)`. `as_literal` / `as_usize` accessors for the legacy-`usize`-shape consumers. `const_arg_display` for diagnostics.
     - **`Type::Array.size` refactor** from `usize` to `ConstArg`. 46 sites surveyed at investigation time; in practice only 12 sites in `typechecker.rs` actually destructure / construct the field ŌĆö most other Type::Array matches use `..` and don't care. All compiled clean.
     - **`lower_type_expr` Array arm** now produces real `ConstArg` values: `Integer(n)` literal ŌåÆ `Literal(n)`; `Identifier(name)` where the name is in `generic_scope` ŌåÆ `ConstParam(name)`; other shapes fall through slice 2's `eval_const_expr` and become `Literal` (or emit a focused diagnostic). The pre-3a `size: 0` placeholder is gone.
     - **`substitute_type_params` const-arg substitution.** New `substitute_const_arg` helper resolves `ConstArg::ConstParam(name)` against the slice-1 `SubstValue` map; `Const(cv)` bindings rewrite to `Literal(cv_as_i64)` via `const_value_to_i64`. `Literal` / `ConstVar` pass through.
     - **Array-length consumers** (`check_expr` array-literal arity, repeat-literal arity, etc.) read the literal via `ConstArg::as_usize` and skip the check for non-literal sizes (the slice-3b inference solver will resolve those at call sites).

     Test coverage (1 new in `tests/typechecker.rs`): `test_const_arg_array_size_distinguishable` ŌĆö the pre-3a unification bug regression-pin (calling `f(b: Array[i64, 4])` with an `Array[i64, 8]` argument now surfaces a size-mismatch diagnostic; before 3a both arrays unified to `Type::Array { size: 0 }`).

     **Slice 3b.** Ō£ō Landed 2026-05-11 (commits `5cb10d5` + `4edac58`). Inference solver core: `unify_const_args(a, b, const_substitutions)` mirroring `unify_types` (with `(ConstVar, other)` bind-and-succeed semantics); `instantiate_signature_with_fresh_vars` extended to mint `ConstVarId`s per unique `ConstParam` name and substitutes `ConstParam ŌåÆ ConstVar` throughout (returns an `InstantiatedSignature` struct now); `resolve_type_vars` walks `ConstArg::ConstVar` via the new `resolve_const_arg` helper and substitutes from `const_substitutions` (unsolved vars convert back to `ConstParam(name)` via `const_id_to_name`); `check_unsolved_const_param` diagnostic for return-only / bounds-only const-params (mirrors `check_unsolved_type_param`). `lower_array_type` extended to recover `ConstParam` from `GenericArg::Type(Path(name))` shapes where `name` is in scope (the parser can't disambiguate type-param refs from const-param refs without scope info, so type lowering performs the rescue).

     Test coverage (4 new): `test_const_inference_single_position` (single-arg infers T+N); `test_const_inference_multi_position_consistent` (two arg positions binding N to the same value); `test_const_inference_multi_position_conflict` (mismatched const-args across positions surfaces a diagnostic); `test_const_inference_return_only_unsolved` (return-only const-param without annotation surfaces the unsolved diagnostic).

     **Slice 3c.** Ō£ō Landed 2026-05-11. Where-clause `ConstPredicate` bound discharge: at each call site, evaluate each `WhereConstraint::ConstPredicate(expr)` against the const-args bound in scope via slice 2's `eval_const_expr`; emit `"const constraint violated: predicate is false with N=..."` on `Bool(false)`. Plumbing chosen: `FunctionSig` extended with `where_clause: Option<WhereClause>` (populated in `env_add_function` from `f.where_clause.clone()`); both the explicit-generic-args call path (`infer_explicit_generic_args_call`) and the regular bare-identifier dispatch (the `Type::Function` arm of `infer_call`) look up the callee's where-clause and thread it through `check_call_args_with_substitution_full`. What landed:
     - **`FunctionSig.where_clause`** added; 12 construction sites patched (each with `where_clause: None` for builtins, `where_clause: f.where_clause.clone()` for user functions and `method.where_clause.clone()` for impl methods).
     - **`check_call_args_with_substitution_full`** accepts `where_clause: Option<&WhereClause>` + `discharge_span: &Span`. After the inference solver runs, the discharge step builds a name ŌåÆ i64 substitution from two sources: inferred const-args (via `name_to_const_id` + `env.const_substitutions` resolved through `resolve_const_arg`) and explicit call-site args (when supplied ŌĆö formal-param names paired with `explicit_generic_args` positions). Explicit args win on collision so call-time bindings flow directly into discharge even when the signature types don't reference the const-param.
     - **`discharge_const_predicates`** walks each `WhereConstraint::ConstPredicate(expr)`, substitutes `Identifier(name)` ŌåÆ `Integer(value)` via the new `substitute_const_idents_in_expr` helper, evaluates against `Type::Bool` via `eval_const_expr`. On `Bool(false)` emits `"const constraint violated: predicate is false with N=value, ..."`; eval errors propagate via `emit_const_eval_error`.
     - **`has_generic` extended** to also fire when the callee declares a where-clause with `ConstPredicate`s ŌĆö without this the early-return short-circuits before the discharge engine for functions whose signature types don't reference the const-param (`fn f[const N: i64]() where N >= 0`).
     - **`is_literal_const_arg_expr` helper** centralizes the "literal-ish const-arg expression" check used by the slice-1c Index-rewrite path; now also accepts `Unary { Neg, Integer }` for negative-integer literals (`f[-1]()`). `const_value_from_literal` similarly extended.

     Test surface (4 new): `test_where_predicate_passes` (`f[5]()` against `where N >= 0` succeeds); `test_where_predicate_fails` (`f[-1]()` surfaces the violation diagnostic mentioning `N=-1`); `test_where_predicate_multiple_const_args` (`fn f[const M, const N]() where M >= 100` fails when M=5); `test_where_predicate_via_inferred_const_arg` (where-clause discharge fires when N is inferred from an arg's type, not just from explicit args).

     **Parser ambiguity carveout.** `where M < N { body }` triggers the parser's struct-literal heuristic (`N {` looks like a struct construction). The `test_where_predicate_multiple_const_args` test sidesteps this by using a literal RHS (`M >= 100`). Predicates of shape `... < Identifier` or `... > Identifier` immediately followed by the body brace will currently fail to parse ŌĆö recovery is a separate parser slice (struct-literal disambiguation in non-statement positions).

     **Slice 3d.** Ō£ō Landed 2026-05-11. Deferred-F regression-pin diagnostic: `Type::Named.args` is `Vec<Type>` and can't carry a const-arg, so user-defined struct const-generic args silently dropped pre-3d. Slice 3d emits a focused diagnostic at the type-position lowering site. What landed:
     - **`lower_generic_args_named`** replaces `lower_generic_args` (the old method is removed). The named variant takes an optional `type_name: Option<&str>` argument; when a `GenericArg::Const(expr)` arrives, it emits `"const generic argument on user-defined type '{}' is not yet supported in this slice; only the built-in \`Array[T, N]\` accepts const-args at v1"` at the expr's span. Both `lower_path_type` call sites pass the type name through.
     - The Array case is unaffected: `lower_array_type` is special-cased upstream in `lower_path_type` (single-segment Path, name == "Array") before `lower_generic_args_named` is invoked, so `Array[T, 4]` continues to work unchanged.

     Test surface (2 new): `test_const_arg_user_defined_struct_rejected` (`struct Buffer[T, const N: i64]` + `fn f(b: Buffer[i64, 4])` surfaces the regression-pin diagnostic mentioning `Buffer`); `test_const_arg_array_unchanged_after_user_defined_diagnostic` (regression-pin that the Array surface still type-checks unchanged).

     **Pull-trigger** for lifting the carve-out: a kata or stdlib type that needs const-arg inference on a `Type::Named` shape. The future slice extends `Type::Named.args` to `Vec<TypeArg>` where `TypeArg = Type(Type) | Const(ConstArg)`, plumbs through the inference solver, and flips the regression-pin test to a success case.

     Original slice 3 plan retained below for reference; the slice-3a/b/c/d split reflects execution scope, not design changes.

     **Original slice 3 plan (call-site inference + where-clause discharge).** Call-site inference solves const params from argument positions (call-local substitution alongside type metavariables); return-only and bounds-only const params require explicit generic-arg lists with a focused diagnostic when omitted; const-arg conflicts across positions reported at the conflicting position. Bound-discharge engine evaluates each `where` predicate (using slice 2's evaluator) at every call site and emits `const constraint violated` with concrete arg values.

     *Investigation finding (2026-05-10) ŌĆö central structural gap.* `Type::Array { size: usize }` at `src/typechecker.rs:28-31` is a literal placeholder; `lower_type_expr` at `src/typechecker.rs:3066-3071` lowers every `Array[T, N]` to `Type::Array { size: 0 }` with comment `// const eval deferred`. The size value is discarded at the Type level ŌĆö `Array[i64, 4]` and `Array[i64, 8]` are indistinguishable as Types. Slice 1 worked around this for codegen via the substitution map + mangler (which read AST directly), but slice 3's inference solver needs the Type representation to carry the const-arg value. **Slice 3 owns the Type-level refactor for `Array`.** `Type::Named.args: Vec<Type>` has the same gap for user-defined-struct const-generics, but Tensor isn't shipped and no const-generic stdlib structs exist (grep verified 2026-05-10) ŌĆö that piece is deferred (fork F).

     *Settled design forks (2026-05-10).*
     - **G1 ŌĆö Inference solver shape.** Extend the existing `unify_types` / `instantiate_signature_with_fresh_vars` / `resolve_type_vars` machinery (`src/typechecker.rs:905`, `:681`, `:801`) with parallel const-var solving. Mirror `TypeVarId(u32)` with `ConstVarId(u32)`; mint `ConstVar`s alongside `TypeVar`s when walking signatures; thread both substitution maps through inference together. Rejected alternative: separate post-pass ŌĆö duplicates the metavar-solving machinery and creates an ordering question (run const-pass before or after type-pass?) with no good answer.
     - **G2 ŌĆö Return-only / bounds-only diagnostic shape.** Mirror `check_unsolved_type_param` at `src/typechecker.rs:6585`. Add `check_unsolved_const_param` + `find_unbound_const_param` (sibling to `find_unbound_type_param` at line 996). Diagnostic: `"cannot infer const parameter '{}'; provide explicit generic args (e.g. \`f[i64, 8](...)\`)"`. The fix-it suggests the explicit form with a placeholder for the missing position. Rejected alternative: a single generic "cannot infer generic arg" diagnostic ŌĆö loses the const-vs-type distinction.
     - **G3 ŌĆö Where-predicate discharge granularity.** Per-call-site evaluation. At every call site, evaluate `WhereConstraint::ConstPredicate(Expr)` via slice 2's evaluator against the inferred const-args; emit `"const constraint violated: predicate \`{expr}\` is false with N={value}"` on `Bool(false)`. Two call sites sharing concrete const-args share a monomorphization but each independently re-verifies its predicate; bound-checking is per-call-site, not per-mono-emission. Rejected alternative: per-mono-emission discharge ŌĆö would silently accept identical const-arg tuples at later call sites if the first emission cleared, which is wrong.
     - **G4 ŌĆö `Type::Array.size` refactor (central piece).** Refactor `Type::Array { size: usize }` to `Type::Array { size: ConstArg }` where `enum ConstArg { Literal(i64), ConstParam(String), ConstVar(ConstVarId) }`. Touches every `Type::Array` constructor (~30 sites by grep) + every `size` consumer (`type_display`, exhaustiveness, pattern dispatch, unification arm, etc., ~20 sites). Mechanical churn but the natural shape ŌĆö `unify_types` Array arm then unifies sizes via `unify_const_args`, and `lower_type_expr`'s Array arm produces real const-arg values. Rejected alternative: keep `size: usize` and represent const-arg-bearing forms via a parallel `Type::ConstGenericApp` wrapper ŌĆö adds a new Type variant that has to be matched at every Type consumer, worse than refactoring the existing `size` field once.
     - **F ŌĆö User-defined struct const-generic inference (deferred).** `Type::Named.args: Vec<Type>` stays type-only. Users can declare `struct Buffer[T, const N: i64]` (slice 1) and construct/use it with explicit const-args, but const-args won't be inferred from argument types. Surface a focused diagnostic at the use site if/when a user struct demands it. Future slice extends `Type::Named.args` similarly (a `Vec<TypeArg>` where `TypeArg = Type(Type) | Const(ConstArg)`). Pull-trigger: a kata or stdlib type that needs const-arg inference on a `Type::Named` shape (today: zero).

     Test coverage: inference success from a single arg position (`Array[i64, 4]` argument infers `N=4`); inference-failure-on-return-only with the focused diagnostic; multi-param solver conflicts at the conflicting position (`fn f[const N: i64](a: Array[T, N], b: Array[T, N])` called with mismatched-size arrays); where-clause bound discharge passing and failing with concrete values in the error; deferred-F regression ŌĆö `Buffer[i64, 4]` argument inferring `N=4` is currently rejected with the focused "user-defined struct const-arg inference not yet supported" diagnostic (regression-pin so we know when to lift the carve-out). Depends on slices 1ŌĆō2.

  4. [x] **Codegen const-param use-site lowering + e2e coverage.** Ō£ō Landed 2026-05-11. Backend lowers const-param references in generic-function bodies: `Identifier(N)` inside a generic body resolves against the active const-subst and emits the matching LLVM constant via `compile_primitive_const`. Slice 1b's mangler already closed the symbol-disambiguation gap; slice 4 closes the body-lowering gap. What landed:
     - **`Codegen.const_subst` field**: `HashMap<String, ConstValue>` parallel to `type_subst`. Save/restore wrapped around `compile_mono_function` in `compile_generic_call` so the body lowering sees the same bindings the mangler used.
     - **`compile_expr ExprKind::Identifier` early branch (H1)**: inserted before the `variables.contains_key` check. When `const_subst.get(name)` is `Some(cv)`, return `compile_primitive_const(cv)` directly ŌĆö emits an LLVM constant of the matching width without going through the value-lookup path.
     - **`array_type_for_generic_args` const-param fallback (H2)**: extended the `Array[T, N]` element-size extraction to handle `Identifier(N)` (where N is a const-generic param in scope) via `const_subst` lookup. Also handles the slice-1c parser-disambiguation case where `Array[T, N]` routes `N` as `GenericArg::Type(Path(N))` rather than `GenericArg::Const(Identifier(N))` ŌĆö at codegen we recover.
     - **`const_value_as_u32` helper** for the Array-size extraction sites; rejects non-integer / negative / out-of-range values.
     - **`compile_primitive_const` (H3)**: reused as-is from slice 2; width-aware emission for I8..I64, U8..U64, Usize, F32, F64, Bool, Char, EnumVariant.

     Test surface (3 new in `tests/codegen.rs`, requires `--features llvm`):
     - `test_e2e_const_generic_param_in_body` ŌĆö `fn f[const N: i64](x: i64) -> i64 { x + N }` called as `f[3](10)` returns 13; `f[7](10)` returns 17.
     - `test_e2e_const_generic_param_in_larger_expression` ŌĆö `fn g[const N: i64]() -> i64 { N * 2 + 1 }` called as `g[7]()` returns 15.
     - `test_ir_const_generic_param_distinct_monos_in_body` ŌĆö verifies the distinct mango symbols (`f$3i64`, `f$7i64`) coexist in the LLVM module when both call sites compile.

     **Const generics surface complete at v1.** Remaining deferred items in this entry are non-blocking: **Slice 2b** (I128/U128 ConstValue, needs IntSize/UIntSize extension), **Slice 3d** (deferred-F regression-pin diagnostic for user-defined-struct const-generic inference), F2 full reshape of `type_subst` to `HashMap<String, SubstValue<'ctx>>` (parallel-maps approach works at slice 4; the reshape pays off only if more `ConstValue`-bearing surfaces get added later).

     *Investigation finding (2026-05-10).* `compile_expr ExprKind::Identifier` at `src/codegen.rs:5600-5632` resolves names through `variables ŌåÆ unit enum variant ŌåÆ top-level const ŌåÆ free fn ŌåÆ load_variable` ŌĆö no const-generic-param branch today. The active-mono substitution lookup pattern at `llvm_type_for_name` (`src/codegen.rs:2274-2278`) is `if let Some(&ty) = self.type_subst.get(name) { return ty; }`; post-slice-1 the same map is `SubstValue::Type | SubstValue::Const`, so slice 4 just inserts a parallel branch for the Const variant. Only one codegen consumer of const-args exists today: `Array[T, N]` element-size extraction at `src/codegen.rs:1787-1799` (literal-only, AST-pattern-match). No other extraction sites ŌĆö the slice 4 surface is small.

     *Settled design forks (2026-05-10).*
     - **H1 ŌĆö Identifier-resolution branch.** Insert an early `SubstValue::Const(cv)` check at `compile_expr ExprKind::Identifier` (`src/codegen.rs:5600`) before the existing `variables.contains_key` check. Emits via `compile_primitive_const` at `src/codegen.rs:1874` (post-slice-2 handles all ConstValue variants width-correctly). Rejected alternative: a separate "const-param lookup" helper called from every identifier-using compile path ŌĆö duplicative; the central dispatch site is the right home.
     - **H2 ŌĆö `Array[T, N]` extraction stays AST-based with const-param fallback.** Keep the existing literal-extraction code at `src/codegen.rs:1787-1799`; add a fallback arm for `GenericArg::Const(Identifier(name))` that consults `type_subst.get(name)` and extracts the size from a `SubstValue::Const(ConstValue::I64(n))` (or matching integer variant). Rejected alternative: rewire all `extract_array_*` through `Type::Array.size: ConstArg` (post-slice-3) ŌĆö purer but ~40 LoC of churn for marginal gain; the AST-vs-Type duality is already established for other helpers (`extract_slice_elem_type`, etc.).
     - **H3 ŌĆö Width-aware constant emission.** `compile_primitive_const` (post-slice-2) already dispatches on each `ConstValue` variant width-correctly. Slice 4 reuses it as the central "const-param identifier ŌåÆ LLVM constant" emitter. No new emission code; just call.

     Test coverage: codegen e2e ŌĆö `fn f[const N: i64](x: i64) -> i64 { x + N }` called with distinct `N` values produces distinct compiled bodies and correct runtime output; const-arg use beyond `Array[T, N]` (e.g., as a typed value inside the body); `Array[T, N]` const-param fallback at codegen extraction; multi-width const params (`fn g[const N: i32]()`) emit the right LLVM constant width; runtime type representation does not encode const params (no extra discriminant or size); existing `Array[T, N]` literal codegen still passes (regression). Depends on slices 1ŌĆō3.

- [x] **Slice and array patterns.** Ō£ō Landed 2026-05-12 across four sub-items. Implements the spec in `design.md ┬¦ Algebraic Data Types > Slice and array patterns`. Phase target: 5.2 (Language Features). Decomposed:

  1. [x] **AST + parser + resolver.** Ō£ō Landed 2026-05-12. New `PatternKind::Slice { prefix: Vec<Pattern>, rest: Option<RestPattern>, suffix: Vec<Pattern> }` variant where `RestPattern` is `Ignored` or `Bound(name)`; parser accepts `[` in `parse_single_pattern` and produces this variant; reject pattern-level multiple `..` markers at parse time with a focused diagnostic ("slice pattern may have at most one `..` marker; remove the extras"). Resolver binds the rest name (if present) and any prefix/suffix bindings into the arm scope; the let-pattern path (`define_pattern_bindings`) gets the same treatment so `let [a, b] = ŌĆ”` produces the right symbol-table entries. Typechecker stub rejects the variant from both entry points (`check_pattern_against` and `bind_pattern_types`) with the focused message "slice and array patterns are not yet implemented in the typechecker; this parses but semantic dispatch (per-type matching, rest-binding type arithmetic, exhaustiveness) is the next slice"; sub-patterns and rest binding are bound to `Type::Error` to avoid double-diagnosing. All downstream PatternKind consumers wired through (interpreter never-matches fallback, codegen unreachable-by-stub, exhaustiveness lowers to Wildcard, ownership `define_pattern_states` / `pattern_binds_anything`, span_visitor recurses prefix+suffix, formatter emits `[ ... ]`, repl/concurrency collect bindings, use_classifier binds-anything, typechecker `is_irrefutable_param_pattern` returns false). 15 new tests across `tests/parser.rs` (11), `tests/resolver.rs` (2), `tests/typechecker.rs` (2).

  2. [x] **Typechecker + exhaustiveness + refutability.** Ō£ō Landed 2026-05-12. New `slice_pattern_types(prefix, rest, suffix, scrutinee_type, span)` helper at `src/typechecker.rs` returns `(element_type, rest_binding_type)` after per-scrutinee dispatch ŌĆö both `check_pattern_against` and `bind_pattern_types` route slice patterns through it, then recurse with their respective sub-pattern functions. Per-type behaviour: `Array[T, N]` (literal `N` only) checks `prefix + suffix Ōēż N` and (when `rest = None`) `prefix + suffix == N`; rest binds `Array[T, N ŌłÆ k ŌłÆ j]` via `ConstArg::Literal`. Non-literal `Array[T, N]` (const-param) is rejected with a focused "compile-time literal required" diagnostic ŌĆö deferred sub-task. `Type::Slice { element, mutable }` propagates the `mutable` flag to the rest binding. `Type::Named { name: "Vec" | "VecDeque", args }` produces `Slice[T]` (immutable) for rest. `Type::Str` rejected with the `.bytes()` / `.chars()` redirect. Other scrutinee shapes get the generic "applies to Array/Vec/Slice" diagnostic. Exhaustiveness: `PatCtor::Array(N)` (Array ŌĆö fixed-arity specialization like a length-N tuple, args padded with wildcards over the rest range) and `PatCtor::SliceLen { fixed, has_rest }` (Vec/Slice ŌĆö coarse length-class ctor) added to `src/exhaustive.rs`; `enumerate_ctors` returns `Some([Array(N)])` for literal Array, `None` for Vec/VecDeque/Slice (open-domain ŌĆö wildcard required), the existing `None` for `Type::Slice`. `Vec`/`VecDeque` special-cased via `is_open_collection` so they bypass the struct-stub-from-prelude path. `ctor_arity` / `ctor_field_types` plumbed through `array_or_collection_element` (auto-derefs `Ref` / `MutRef`). `render_witness` emits `[a, b]` / `[a, ..]` forms. Refutability falls out automatically: `is_pattern_irrefutable` on `Array[T, N]` returns true iff every nested element pattern is irrefutable (and `prefix + suffix == N` or rest is Some covering the gap); `Vec[T]` / `Slice[T]` slice patterns are always refutable (open-domain ŌåÆ wildcard required ŌåÆ `let [a, b] = vec` rejected as `RefutablePattern`). `is_irrefutable_param_pattern` keeps returning `false` (syntactic fallback unused for handled types). 15 new typechecker tests in `tests/typechecker.rs` (match-Vec with/without wildcard, exact-arity Array exhaustiveness, Array under-coverage, Array arity overflow, Array rest arithmetic remainder, Vec rest typed as Slice, mut Slice preserves mut, String rejection with bytes/chars hint, irrefutable Array let, refutable Vec let, Array rest irrefutable in let, Array rest covers exhaustiveness, nested independent rest markers, slice-pattern-on-int rejected). Sub-item 1's stub tests removed (obsolete). Depends on sub-item 1.

  3. [x] **Interpreter.** Ō£ō Landed 2026-05-12. New free helper `slice_pattern_view(value: &Value) -> Option<SlicePatternView>` (`SlicePatternView = (Arc<RwLock<Vec<Value>>>, usize, usize, bool)`) at `src/interpreter.rs` exposes `(storage, offset, len, source_mutable)` uniformly for `Value::Array` (offset 0, immutable flag) and `Value::Slice` (existing window, inherited mutable flag); other Value variants yield `None` (defensive never-match ŌĆö typechecker rejects non-sequence scrutinees). `try_match_pattern` arm dispatches through the view: rest-absent requires exact length, rest-present requires `total Ōēź prefix + suffix`, then recurses on prefix elements at `offset..offset+k` and suffix elements at `offset+total-j..offset+total`. `bind_pattern` arm binds prefix + suffix sub-patterns positionally with cloned element values (read-guard scoped to the clone block so recursive `bind_pattern` calls don't reentrantly hold the lock), and for `RestPattern::Bound(name)` defines the name to a fresh `Value::Slice { storage, start: offset + k, len: total - k - j, mutable: source_mutable }` ŌĆö matching range-indexing's "slice reference into source storage" precedent. Type-erased: typechecker types Array rest as `Array[T, N-k-j]`, interpreter represents it as `Value::Slice` (the universal sequence representation ŌĆö both `.len()` and indexing work on either). 13 new interpreter tests in `tests/interpreter.rs`: `empty_matches_empty_vec`, `single_element_fixed_arity_array`, `fixed_arity_let_binds_all_elements`, `head_only_ignored_rest_on_vec`, `tail_only_ignored_rest_on_vec`, `both_ends_ignored_rest_on_vec`, `single_bound_rest_at_tail_array`, `single_bound_rest_at_head_array`, `two_bound_middle_rest_array`, `multi_element_prefix_and_suffix_array`, `vec_bound_rest_sum_via_iter`, `match_dispatches_on_length_for_vec`, `rest_binding_preserves_element_values_on_vec` ŌĆö covering every shape listed in the scope (empty / single / fixed-arity / head / tail / both-ends / single-bound rest at each end / two-bound (middle-rest) / multi-element prefix and suffix) with assertions on bound values and rest length. Depends on sub-item 2.

  4. [x] **Codegen.** Ō£ō Landed 2026-05-12. New `SliceSource<'ctx>` struct at `src/codegen.rs` carries `(data_ptr: PointerValue, len: IntValue, elem_ty: BasicTypeEnum, mutable: bool)` ŌĆö the uniform LLVM-side view of an `Array[T, N]` / `Vec[T]` / `Slice[T]` scrutinee. `resolve_slice_source(expr)` resolves identifier-rooted scrutinees: Array ŌåÆ GEP `[0, 0]` into the alloca for `T*` + const length `N`; Slice ŌåÆ load `data`/`len` from the `{ptr, i64}` struct alloca; Vec ŌåÆ load `data`/`len` from the `{ptr, i64, i64}` struct alloca. `compile_slice_pattern_condition(prefix, rest, suffix, src)` builds the i1 condition with a length-check guard block: rest-absent uses `EQ`, rest-present uses `UGE`; when the length passes, a "sp.check" block loads each prefix element at `data_ptr[i]` and each suffix element at `data_ptr[len-j+i]`, AND-ing sub-pattern conditions; a phi over the length-fail and check-end blocks produces the final i1 (so out-of-bounds GEPs never emit when the length is wrong). `bind_slice_pattern(prefix, rest, suffix, src, for_match)` binds prefix/suffix sub-patterns by recursing through `bind_pattern_values` (match) or `bind_pattern` (let), and for `RestPattern::Bound(name)` builds a `Slice[T]` header via `build_slice_header` over `data_ptr[k..len-j]`, stores it into a fresh alloca named `name`, registers it in `variables` + `slice_elem_types` so `rest.len()` / `rest[i]` / iteration dispatch through the slice surface. Match-arm dispatch: `compile_match` routes slice arms through the new helpers (each arm re-resolves the SliceSource so LLVM dominator structure works out; the optimizer dedups); non-slice arms keep the existing `compile_pattern_condition` / `bind_pattern_values` path. Let dispatch: `compile_stmt(StmtKind::Let)` intercepts slice patterns before the generic `bind_pattern` call. Side-effect on param setup: owned `Vec[T]` / `String` function parameters now register in `vec_elem_types` (previously only ref-Vec / let-bound Vecs were tracked) ŌĆö required so `fn label(v: Vec[i64]) { match v { [] => ŌĆ”, _ => ŌĆ” } }` resolves `v` to a SliceSource. Type-erased rest: for Array sources the typechecker types rest as `Array[T, N-k-j]` but codegen materializes it as a `Slice[T]` header (same trick as the interpreter); user code on rest calls slice methods which are layout-compatible. 12 new e2e codegen tests in `tests/codegen.rs` mirroring sub-item 3's interpreter shapes (empty / single / fixed-arity / head / tail / both-ends / single-bound rest at each end / two-bound middle rest / multi-element prefix and suffix / length-class dispatch / rest indexing). Gated on `--features llvm`. Depends on sub-items 2 and 3.

- [~] **Match ergonomics ŌĆö `ref T` scrutinee borrow propagation.** Implement the spec in `design.md ┬¦ Match Arm Binding Modes` (the propagation rules already nailed down). The current typechecker `check_pattern_against` (`src/typechecker.rs`) inserts arm bindings with `expected.clone()` and the `TupleVariant` / `Struct` arms only match on `Type::Named { ŌĆ” }`; under a `ref T` scrutinee the bindings should be wrapped in `Type::Ref` (and `Type::MutRef` under `mut ref T`), and the descent into nested patterns must unwrap the `Ref` to reach the underlying enum/struct shape while preserving the borrow flag for sub-bindings. Slices: (1) Typechecker ŌĆö at `infer_match` entry, classify the scrutinee mode as Owned / Ref / MutRef and thread the mode through `check_pattern_against`; auto-deref at the matrix root so the existing variant lookup keeps working; wrap each leaf binding's type in the appropriate borrow form. (2) Ownership ŌĆö verify the existing match-arm consume rules remain consistent: an arm that *consumes* a binding under a Ref scrutinee mode is the existing E0501-class diagnostic ("cannot move out of a borrow"); ensure the typechecker mode classification reaches the ownership pass (or that the ownership pass independently recomputes from the scrutinee type). (3) Interpreter / codegen ŌĆö pattern binding emission must produce a borrow (no clone, no move) for ref-mode arms; element access through the borrowed scrutinee. Test coverage: `match ref-typed-binding`, `match function-returning-ref`, `match ref self.field`; per-arm bindings observed through their borrow type (e.g., `field: ref FieldType`); attempt-to-consume-under-ref diagnostic; explicit `ref` annotation on an arm binding under an owned scrutinee continues to work (the existing path); nested patterns under ref propagate transitively (`Some(Person { name })` under `ref Option[Person]` ŌåÆ `name: ref String`); or-patterns under ref maintain the same binding-type rule across alternatives. Phase target: 5.2 (Language Features).

  Decomposed:
  1. [x] **Typechecker + ownership consume gate.** Ō£ō Landed 2026-05-12. New `ScrutineeMode { Owned, Ref, MutRef }` in `src/typechecker.rs` with `ScrutineeMode::classify(&Type) -> (mode, &dispatch_ty)` stripping one outer `Type::Ref` / `Type::MutRef` for variant / struct / tuple dispatch (so the existing `Type::Named { name, args }` lookup at `TupleVariant` / `Struct` arms keeps matching the unwrapped shape), and `ScrutineeMode::wrap_binding_ty(self, Type) -> Type` wrapping each leaf binding's type back into the corresponding borrow form ŌĆö `Owned` is identity; `Ref` produces `Type::Ref(_)` and `MutRef` produces `Type::MutRef(_)` for non-borrow leaf shapes; already-borrow leaves (`Ref` / `MutRef` / `Slice { .. }`) pass through unchanged so a `ref Foo` field through a `ref Container` scrutinee stays `ref Foo` (not `ref ref Foo`) and a struct field declared `Slice[T]` (immutable) is never silently elevated to `mut Slice[T]` by a `mut ref Container` scrutinee. `check_pattern_against` widened to `(pattern, expected, mode)`; both match entry points (`check_match_against` and `infer_match` in `src/typechecker.rs`) classify at entry and thread the mode through every recursive sub-pattern (`TupleVariant`, `Struct`, `Tuple`, `AtBinding`, `Or`, `Slice`). Struct shorthand fields (`Foo { name }` where `field.pattern is None`), positional tuple-variant payloads, struct field destructures, slice prefix/suffix sub-patterns, slice-rest bindings, `@`-bindings, and or-pattern alternatives all observe the same mode ŌĆö transitive propagation at any nesting depth. Slice-rest mutability propagation per design.md ┬¦ Slice patterns ŌĆö Mutability propagation (lines 7657ŌĆō7661) handled at the Slice arm: under `MutRef`, a `Slice[T]` rest is upgraded to `mut Slice[T]` (the rest is a fresh window into a mutable source, distinct from a struct field typed `Slice[T]` which is field-declared); Array rest under `Ref` / `MutRef` goes through the generic wrap. Ownership pass extended with `OwnershipChecker::is_borrow_typed_scrutinee` (consults `typecheck_result.expr_types` then `param_types`) at `src/ownership.rs` Match arm: when the scrutinee type is `Type::Ref(_)` / `Type::MutRef(_)`, the match is always classified as `check_expr_reading` regardless of `pattern_binds_anything`, mirroring the typechecker's binding-form decision ŌĆö the scrutinee's source binding (typically a `ref T` parameter) is no longer falsely marked `Moved` after a binding arm. Parallel gate in `UseClassifier::is_borrow_typed_expr` (`src/use_classifier.rs`) so the CFG / RC-fallback predicate path makes the same Reading-vs-Consuming decision the dataflow pass does. 14 new tests: 11 typechecker (`tests/typechecker.rs`: ref struct field, ref-returning ref-field, ref Option payload, owned-baseline, ref Option[Person] nested propagation, ref or-pattern, mut ref struct, ref Result[T,E] tuple variant, ref Vec slice rest = Slice[T], mut ref Vec slice rest = mut Slice[T], ref Array slice rest = ref Array[T,K], owned Array slice rest = Array[T,K]), 3 ownership (`tests/ownership.rs`: ref-scrutinee not consumed, owned-scrutinee still consumed, ref Option payload not consumed, mut ref scrutinee not consumed). The pre-existing latent bug ŌĆö `is_copy_type(Type::Ref(_)) == false` made `check_expr_consuming` mark a `ref T` parameter as `Moved` when any arm bound a name ŌĆö is closed by this slice; today's owned-scrutinee path is unchanged.

  2. [->] **Interpreter ref-scrutinee binding semantics (deferred ŌĆö `[->]` explicit kick).** The tree-walk interpreter (`src/interpreter.rs`) stores values as `Value::*` and has no reference variant ŌĆö `Value::Struct { fields }` holds field values directly, so `match val { Foo { name } => use_str(name) }` clones the field into the arm scope regardless of whether the typechecker labelled `val` as `Foo` or `ref Foo`. **Consume divergence** is typechecker-gated: the type system rejects `take_owned(name)` when `name: ref String`, so the interpreter never witnesses an illegal consume. **Mutation divergence is real** but bounded: `match mut ref foo { Foo { name } => name.push('!') }` mutates a cloned `name` in the arm scope; the mutation does not propagate back to `foo.name` (no analog of the existing CICO writeback at function boundaries). Implementation options weighed 2026-05-12: writeback model (~150 LoC + recursive path tracking for nested patterns) handles common cases but is incomplete for deeply nested mut-ref destructures; full `Value::Ref { path, mutable }` variant with auto-deref at every value-consuming site is ~500-800 LoC and significantly invasive. Explicit kick on 2026-05-12 ŌĆö the interpreter does not exercise this path in user-visible REPL or test surface today, and the codegen-path fix below (sub-item 3) is the production-relevant lowering. Re-pull this entry when (i) REPL session produces a visible mutation-propagation surprise, OR (ii) the interpreter gains a `Value::Ref`-style indirection for unrelated reasons (e.g., shared-struct identity-aliased borrows) and ref-scrutinee binding becomes additive.
  3. [x] **Codegen ref-scrutinee LLVM lowering.** Slice 3a (leaf-binding ABI parity) shipped 2026-05-14; slice 3b (true GEP-based aliasing into scrutinee storage) shipped 2026-05-14. The original framing ŌĆö "Today's `bind_pattern_values` ingests the i64 / struct payload word the enum-payload codegen extracted from the scrutinee" ŌĆö under-described the gap: `bind_pattern_values` had no `PatternKind::Struct` arm at all, so even the **owned baseline** `match p { Foo { x, y } => ... }` errored at codegen with `Undefined variable 'x'`. Slice 3a closes the owned baseline and the leaf-binding ABI shape under `ref` / `mut ref` scrutinees via a copy-and-shim; slice 3b replaces the copy with a real GEP into the scrutinee so `mut ref` write-through propagates back to the caller's storage.

     **Slice 3a ŌĆö leaf-binding ABI parity (shipped 2026-05-14).**
     - [x] **Owned-baseline `PatternKind::Struct` arm in `bind_pattern_values`** (`src/codegen.rs`). Resolves field index by name via `struct_field_names[struct_name]`, extracts via `build_extract_value` against the scrutinee struct, recurses through `bind_pattern_values` (sub-pattern when present; synthesized `PatternKind::Binding(field.name)` for shorthand). Predecessor for the ref-shim path ŌĆö without it, even owned struct match arms failed.
     - [x] **`PatternBindingBorrow` enum + side table** (`src/ast.rs`). New `enum PatternBindingBorrow { Ref, MutRef }` and `PatternBindingBorrowModesTable = HashMap<(usize, usize), PatternBindingBorrow>`. Added as `pub pattern_binding_borrow_modes` on `Program` and on `TypeCheckResult` (with internal mirror on `TypeChecker`). Lowering pass forwards span keys.
     - [x] **Typechecker writes via `record_pattern_binding_borrow_mode(span, mode, dispatch_ty)`** (`src/typechecker.rs`). Skips entries when `mode == Owned` and when `dispatch_ty` is already a borrow shape (`Ref` / `MutRef` / `Slice`) ŌĆö parity with `ScrutineeMode::wrap_binding_ty`'s pass-through arm so a `ref FieldT` field through a `ref Container` scrutinee stays single-borrowed and a struct field declared `Slice[T]` is not silently elevated to `mut Slice[T]`. `check_pattern_against` writes at three sites: leaf `Binding` (keyed by `pattern.span`), `Struct` shorthand fields (keyed by `field.span` to match codegen's synthesized binding span), `AtBinding` outer alias (keyed by the outer pattern's span; the inner sub-pattern records via the recursive call).
     - [x] **Codegen ref-shim at leaf `Binding` arm** (`src/codegen.rs::bind_pattern_values`). When the borrow-mode table contains an entry for the binding's span, allocate a separate `ptr` shim alloca (`{name}.refshim`), store the value alloca's address into it, replace `variables[name]` with the shim alloca (so `load_variable` first-loads the pointer), and register `name` in `ref_params` with the value type (so the second load auto-derefs back to the value). Subsequent identifier uses round-trip back to the value via auto-deref; call sites that pass the binding to a `ref T` / `mut ref T` parameter receive the shim's contents (a pointer) ŌĆö closes the latent ABI miscompile.
