Test coverage: external `match` on `#[non_exhaustive]` enum without wildcard rejected with the typed diagnostic; same with wildcard accepted; same-package `match` on the same enum without wildcard rejected via the normal exhaustiveness rule (not the `#[non_exhaustive]` rule); external struct literal on `#[non_exhaustive]` struct rejected with the constructor-fix-it; external struct pattern without `..` rejected; external struct pattern with `..` accepted; same-package literal and exhaustive pattern accepted; attribute on a private type rejected; attribute on a trait rejected; attribute on a function rejected; new error-variant additions on a stdlib `#[non_exhaustive]` enum compile cleanly across a cross-package consumer that uses a wildcard arm; `missing_non_exhaustive` lint fires on a stdlib `pub enum FooError` lacking the attribute and is silent on a user-package `pub enum BarError` lacking it. Phase target: 5.2 (Language Features).

  - [x] **Slice 4 ŌĆö literal half (2026-05-17) + pattern half with `..` rest-pattern enabling change (2026-05-17) both shipped.** Spec sentence honoured for the literal half: *"Typechecker ŌĆö for struct literal expressions ... where the struct's defining package differs from the current package and the struct is `#[non_exhaustive]`, emit a focused error with a fix-it: literal ŌåÆ `Struct.new(...)` (named-arg call) when a `pub fn new` exists."* **`StructInfo` extension** in `src/typechecker/env.rs`: two new fields ŌĆö `is_non_exhaustive: bool` (mirrors `StructDef.is_non_exhaustive`) and `defining_stdlib_origin: bool` (mirrors `StructDef.stdlib_origin`). Populated in every `StructInfo` construction site in `src/typechecker/env_build.rs`: the regular `env_add_struct` reads both flags from the `StructDef`, the slice-1 prelude-bake pre-pass in `register_builtin_types` and the type-method scaffolding site default `is_non_exhaustive: false, defining_stdlib_origin: true` (built-in / range types are stdlib-internal scaffolding and never reach the cross-package check). **`current_fn_stdlib_origin: bool`** on `TypeChecker` (`src/typechecker.rs`): defaults `false` at construction; saved/restored across every `check_function` call (`src/typechecker/items.rs`) based on `f.stdlib_origin`. Save/restore is symmetric with the existing `current_return_type` / `current_self_type` / `enclosing_bounds` patterns ŌĆö nested item walks (impl methods inside a stdlib impl block, trait default-body synthesized functions) propagate the inner function's origin during body checking and unwind to the outer on return. **Cross-package check** in `infer_struct_literal` (`src/typechecker/fields.rs`): after the existing field-validation pass, if `info.is_non_exhaustive && info.defining_stdlib_origin && !self.current_fn_stdlib_origin`, emit `error[E_NON_EXHAUSTIVE_CROSS_PACKAGE_LITERAL]` naming the struct and suggesting the `<Name>.new(...)` constructor fix-it. The diagnostic message links to design.md ┬¦ `#[non_exhaustive]` for Evolvable Public Types so a first-time reader sees the rationale. **New `TypeErrorKind::NonExhaustiveCrossPackageLiteral`** in `src/typechecker.rs`; mapped to `E0241` in `src/cli.rs`'s typechecker error-code table (the slot following `ConflictingImpl: E0240`). **Test surface (6 typechecker tests in `tests/typechecker.rs::non_exhaustive_slice4_*`)**: `cross_package_literal_rejected` (the headline negative ŌĆö stdlib-origin `#[non_exhaustive] pub struct Config` constructed via literal in user code fires the slice-4 diagnostic, with the symbolic code, the struct name, and the `Config.new(...)` constructor fix-it all surfaced in the message), `same_package_literal_accepted` (positive pin ŌĆö both decl and call user-origin ŌåÆ no diagnostic), `non_exhaustive_off_no_diagnostic` (rejection keys on the attribute, not the cross-package boundary alone ŌĆö a stdlib-origin `pub struct` without `#[non_exhaustive]` is fine), `stdlib_internal_use_accepted` (defining-package internal use ŌĆö both decl and constructor are stdlib-origin ŌåÆ no diagnostic; the defining package keeps exhaustive literal access), `struct_info_carries_flag` (plumbing pin ŌĆö `StructInfo.is_non_exhaustive` and `defining_stdlib_origin` round-trip from the AST through env-building; pins both flags on two distinct structs in one Program), `cross_package_error_code_is_e0241` (pins the `TypeErrorKind::NonExhaustiveCrossPackageLiteral` discriminant is produced under the rule conditions ŌĆö `cli.rs`'s match exhaustiveness check guarantees the `E0241` code surfaces in JSON output). **Test helper `typecheck_with_stdlib_origin_on_structs`**: flips `stdlib_origin = true` on every `StructDef` after parse, leaving `Function`s user-origin, mirroring the baked-stdlib + user-code mix the actual stdlib path produces. The same shape `src/prelude.rs::baked_item_for` uses; the test helper keeps the construction inline so each test reads top-to-bottom. **Pattern half (shipped 2026-05-17).** Enabling change: `PatternKind::Struct` gains a `has_rest: bool` field at `src/ast/patterns.rs`, populated by the parser when `..` appears in the field list. New parser helper `parse_struct_pattern_fields` in `src/parser/patterns.rs` walks the field list, accepting `..` once at any position (preferred: last) and emitting `E_REST_PATTERN_DUPLICATE` on a second occurrence and `E_REST_PATTERN_NOT_LAST` on a field-after-rest. Both struct-pattern parse sites (single-segment `Name { ... }` and qualified `Path.Name { ... }`) route through the helper; the third site (parameter-pattern grammar in `src/parser/items.rs`) keeps `has_rest: false` since params are irrefutable and `..` is meaningless there. **Cross-package pattern check** in `src/typechecker/patterns.rs`: BOTH `check_pattern_against` (match-arm route) AND `bind_pattern_types` (let-binding route) emit `error[E_NON_EXHAUSTIVE_CROSS_PACKAGE_PATTERN]` (new `TypeErrorKind::NonExhaustiveCrossPackagePattern`, mapped to `E0243` in `src/cli.rs`) when `is_non_exhaustive && defining_stdlib_origin && !current_fn_stdlib_origin && !has_rest`. Both routes are exercised ŌĆö `let Config { x } = c;` and `match c { Config { x } => ... }` both fire the rule, mirroring the slice-4 literal half's invariant that the cross-package check fires wherever exhaustive-shape destructuring happens. **Formatter / lowering** (`src/formatter/patterns.rs`, `src/exhaustive.rs`, `src/interpreter/pattern_match.rs`, `src/resolver/resolve_refs.rs`): all sites that destructure `PatternKind::Struct` updated to thread `has_rest` through. Formatter round-trips the `..` marker so `karac fmt` preserves rest-patterns. Exhaustiveness lowering already treated missing-field shorthand as `Pat::Wildcard`, so `..` produces an identical lowering ŌĆö no semantic change to the existing Maranget machinery. Interpreter pattern-matcher never required all fields to be enumerated, so the runtime check is `has_rest`-independent. **Test surface (7 parser tests in `tests/parser.rs::rest_pattern_struct_*` + 6 typechecker tests in `tests/typechecker.rs::non_exhaustive_slice4_pattern_*`).** Parser: bare `{ .. }`, field + rest, field + rest + trailing comma, no-rest sets flag false, field-after-rest rejected with `E_REST_PATTERN_NOT_LAST`, duplicate-rest rejected, qualified-path struct pattern with `..`. Typechecker: cross-package without `..` rejected (let-binding route), cross-package with `..` accepted, same-package without `..` accepted, no-attribute + cross-package accepted, match-arm route also rejected (pins both check sites fire), stdlib-internal use accepted. **Cross-package today.** The only inter-package boundary the compiler currently tracks is stdlib-vs-user (`stdlib_origin`); the slice-4 check leverages this as the v1 cross-package proxy. When richer per-package boundaries land (cross-user-package isolation), the comparison at `infer_struct_literal` widens to `defining_package_id != current_package_id` without re-flowing through `StructInfo` or the fn-context plumbing. Phase target: 5.2 (Language Features). **Blocks slice 5** (enum exhaustiveness ŌĆö same fn-stdlib-origin context will be consulted on the match scrutinee's type) **[Resolved by slice 5 below ŌĆö shipped 2026-05-17.]** **and slice 6** (stdlib hygiene lint ŌĆö once the lint registry lands, the lint reads `is_non_exhaustive` to flag stdlib `pub enum` lacking the attribute).

  - [x] **Slice 5 ŌĆö cross-package enum exhaustiveness wildcard rule shipped 2026-05-17.** Spec sentence honoured: *"Exhaustiveness checker ŌĆö when matching on a value whose enum type is `#[non_exhaustive]` and defined in a different package, the wildcard requirement is unconditional regardless of which variants are covered; emit the existing non-exhaustive-match diagnostic with a fix-it inserting `_ => todo!(\"handle new variant\")`. The check is package-relative: same-package matches are checked normally."* Builds directly on slice 4's `current_fn_stdlib_origin` plumbing ŌĆö the `EnumInfo` side of the same plumbing replicates the `StructInfo` extension. **`EnumInfo` extension** in `src/typechecker/env.rs`: `is_non_exhaustive: bool` + `defining_stdlib_origin: bool`, mirroring the `StructInfo` shape from slice 4. Populated in both `EnumInfo` construction sites in `src/typechecker/env_build.rs`: the prelude-bake pre-pass and `env_add_enum`. **Check site** in `src/typechecker/patterns.rs::check_exhaustiveness`: before invoking the existing `check_match_exhaustive`, if the scrutinee is a `Type::Named` of a `#[non_exhaustive]` enum from another package AND the user is in a non-stdlib fn AND the arms contain no catch-all, emit `error[E_NON_EXHAUSTIVE_CROSS_PACKAGE_MATCH]` naming the enum and surfacing the `_ => todo!("handle new variant")` fix-it. The check fires BEFORE the strict-rule `check_match_exhaustive` so a missing wildcard surfaces as the slice-5 diagnostic, not as a generic "missing variant Vn" tail (which would mislead the author into adding the listed variant rather than `_`). `return` after the slice-5 emission to skip the strict rule for the same match (the cross-package rule subsumes it). **Catch-all detection** via two new free functions at the bottom of `patterns.rs`: `arms_contain_catchall(arms, &variant_names)` walks each arm's pattern under the no-guard predicate and dispatches to `pattern_is_catchall`. **Variant-aware catch-all classification**: `PatternKind::Binding(name)` is the surface for BOTH a fresh binding (`other => ...`, a catch-all) AND a unit-variant constructor (`Read => ...`, NOT a catch-all ŌĆö the parser can't distinguish at parse time). The helper threads the scrutinee enum's variant-name set so `Binding(name)` counts as catch-all iff `name` is NOT a known variant. `Or` patterns and `AtBinding` chains recurse. Guarded arms (`x if cond =>`) are never catch-alls because the guard can fail. **New `TypeErrorKind::NonExhaustiveCrossPackageMatch`** mapped to `E0242` in `src/cli.rs` (the slot following `NonExhaustiveCrossPackageLiteral: E0241`). **Test surface (8 typechecker tests in `tests/typechecker.rs::non_exhaustive_slice5_*`)**: `cross_package_match_without_wildcard_rejected` (headline negative ŌĆö every variant listed but no `_` arm fires `E_NON_EXHAUSTIVE_CROSS_PACKAGE_MATCH` with the symbolic code, the enum name, the `_ =>` fix-it, AND the `todo!(...)` placeholder), `cross_package_match_with_wildcard_accepted` (positive twin ŌĆö same match with `_ => 0` added typechecks cleanly), `same_package_match_uses_strict_rule` (covers all variants without `_` ŌåÆ fine, the strict rule doesn't fire because all variants are listed), `same_package_strict_rule_fires_on_missing_variant` (missing variant + no wildcard ŌåÆ the EXISTING `NonExhaustiveMatch` fires, NOT the new cross-package rule ŌĆö local code catches "you added a variant and forgot to handle it"), `cross_package_match_without_attribute_uses_strict_rule` (plain `pub enum` without `#[non_exhaustive]` continues to use the strict rule even when defining-package and use-site differ), `stdlib_internal_match_accepted` (the defining package retains exhaustive-match access ŌĆö both enum and fn `stdlib_origin = true`), `bare_binding_arm_counts_as_catchall` (the variant-aware classification ŌĆö `other => ...` is a catch-all because `other` is not a variant), `enum_info_carries_flag` (plumbing pin ŌĆö both flags round-trip from AST through env-building on two distinct enums). **Test helper `typecheck_with_stdlib_origin_on_enums`** mirrors the slice-4 struct helper: flips `EnumDef.stdlib_origin = true` after parse, leaves `Function`s user-origin. **What slice 5 does *not* do.** No `NonExhaustiveMatch` deprecation ŌĆö the strict rule continues to fire same-package (the slice-5 rule is package-relative, layered on top). No support for enum pattern-position wildcard (still surfaced via the existing `_` mechanism). No machine-applicable fix-it `replacement` field ŌĆö slice 7 polish covers fix-it text rendering. Phase target: 5.2 (Language Features). **Unblocks** the broader same-fn-stdlib-origin design ŌĆö slices 4 and 5 share the same `current_fn_stdlib_origin` context, validating the design for slice 4's deferred pattern half.

  - [x] **Slice 6 ŌĆö stdlib hygiene lint `missing_non_exhaustive` shipped 2026-05-17.** Spec sentence honoured: *"Stdlib hygiene lint (new) ŌĆö `missing_non_exhaustive` warning that fires on a stdlib `pub enum` whose name ends in `Error` or whose declared role is 'stdlib error enum' and which lacks `#[non_exhaustive]`; the lint is `deny`-by-default for stdlib crates and `allow` for user code."* The "declared role" half is reviewer judgement (not a hard rule baked into the compiler, per the spec); the lint heuristic is the name suffix. **Lint registry entry** in `src/lints.rs`: `missing_non_exhaustive` with `default_level: LintLevel::Deny`. Registry-coverage test gets the name pinned. **New `TypeErrorKind::MissingNonExhaustive`** in `src/typechecker.rs`; mapped to `W0246` in both `src/cli.rs` code tables (the W prefix reflects the underlying lint carrier; the deny-by-default level surfaces it as an error under `severity: "error"` by way of the error-loop emit path, mirroring how `Deprecated` is routed). **Emission pre-pass** in `src/typechecker.rs::emit_missing_non_exhaustive_warnings`: walks `program.items`, for each `Item::EnumDef(e)` where `e.stdlib_origin && e.is_pub && e.name.ends_with("Error") && !e.is_non_exhaustive` pushes the enum's `lint_overrides` as the innermost cascade frame and emits via `type_lint_warning` so `#[allow(missing_non_exhaustive)]` on the enum self-suppresses (same pattern as `emit_unknown_lint_warnings` from slice 4b follow-up, where the warning's natural span sits outside the item's body and a span-based cascade walker would otherwise miss it). Wired into `check()` immediately after `emit_unknown_lint_warnings()`. **Spec-correct "allow for user code"** comes free from the check site's `stdlib_origin` gate: the rule does not examine user enums at all, so no build-wide CLI default is needed (CLI build-wide defaults `-A` / `-W` / `-D NAME` land in slice 4b polish). **Test surface (8 typechecker tests in `tests/typechecker.rs::non_exhaustive_slice6_*`)**: `stdlib_error_enum_without_attr_fires` (headline negative ŌĆö stdlib `pub enum FooError` without the attribute fires `MissingNonExhaustive` with symbolic code, enum name, and attribute mention), `stdlib_error_enum_with_attr_silent` (positive twin), `user_error_enum_silent` (the "allow for user code" surface ŌĆö user-package `FooError` is not examined), `stdlib_non_error_name_silent` (the name-suffix heuristic ŌĆö `BarConfig` is silent), `private_enum_silent` (non-pub gating ŌĆö meaningless without a cross-package boundary), `allow_suppresses_at_enum` (`#[allow(missing_non_exhaustive)]` on the enum routes through the slice-4b cascade and self-suppresses), `warn_demotes_to_warning` (`#[warn(missing_non_exhaustive)]` overrides the deny default and routes to `warnings` instead of `errors`, pinning that the lint goes through `type_lint_warning` rather than `type_error` directly), `lint_is_registered` (registry pin ŌĆö adding the lint without wiring the check, or vice versa, breaks loudly). **What slice 6 does *not* do.** No `Display` / `Debug` exemption ŌĆö the rule applies uniformly across all stdlib `Error`-suffixed enums. No build-wide CLI default (slice 4b polish). No fix-it `replacement` text (slice 7 polish). Phase target: 5.2 (Language Features).

  - [x] **Slice 7 ŌĆö machine-applicable fix-it `replacement` text for pattern + match diagnostics shipped 2026-05-17.** Spec sentence honoured: *"diagnostic polish (slice 7 ŌĆö machine-applicable fix-it `replacement` text for the literal/pattern/match diagnostics)"*. **New `FixIt { span: Span, replacement: String }`** in `src/typechecker.rs` ŌĆö minimal one-edit surface (a zero-`length` span represents an insertion). **`TypeError` gains `fix_it: Option<FixIt>`** wired through every existing construction site (`type_error` / warning-loop `TypeError {...}` blocks ŌåÆ `None`; new `type_error_with_fix_it` helper threads the edit when the emitter knows one). **CLI JSON wiring** in `src/cli.rs::DiagnosticJson::add`: `DiagEntry` carries `fix_it: Option<&FixIt>`, surfaced as a nested `"fix_it":{"span":{...,"offset":N,"length":N},"replacement":"..."}` object so IDE / formatter consumers can apply the edit without re-parsing the message text. The byte-level `offset` + `length` are included alongside line/column (the existing span shape) so consumers can distinguish insertion (length=0) from replacement uniformly. **Pattern fix-it** in `src/typechecker/patterns.rs::non_exhaustive_pattern_fix_it` (free helper at the bottom of the file, alongside `arms_contain_catchall` from slice 5): empty field list ŌåÆ insert `..` at `pattern.span.end - 1` (position of `}`); non-empty ŌåÆ insert `, ..` at `last_field.span.end` (chains onto the existing last field whether or not the source carried a trailing comma). Wired into both pattern emission sites ŌĆö `check_pattern_against` (match-arm route) and `bind_pattern_types` (let-binding route) ŌĆö so every cross-package pattern diagnostic carries the fix-it. **Match fix-it** in `non_exhaustive_match_fix_it`: empty arms ŌåÆ insert `_ => panic("handle new variant")` at `match.span.end - 1`; non-empty ŌåÆ insert `, _ => panic("handle new variant")` at `last_arm.span.end`. Wired into the slice-5 emission site in `check_exhaustiveness`. **K─üra-valid placeholder.** The spec's `todo!(...)` rendering (Rust syntax) is replaced by `panic("handle new variant")` ŌĆö K─üra has no `todo!()` macro, so a machine-applicable fix-it must use the actual stdlib panic-emitter. The slice-5 message text and its pinning test are updated to match; the spec's intent ("placeholder the user fills in with the real handler") is preserved. **Test surface (7 typechecker tests in `tests/typechecker.rs::non_exhaustive_slice7_*`)**: `pattern_fix_it_present_with_fields` (headline pin ŌĆö non-empty pattern ŌåÆ replacement = `, ..`, zero-length span), `pattern_fix_it_empty_field_list_emits_dot_dot` (empty `Foo {}` ŌåÆ `..`), `pattern_fix_it_anchors_after_last_field` (round-trip ŌĆö splicing the fix-it in produces a parser-valid program containing `, ..`), `match_fix_it_inserts_wildcard_arm` (replacement contains `_ => panic("handle new variant")`), `match_fix_it_anchors_after_last_arm` (round-trip ŌĆö splicing into a non-empty match produces a parser-valid program), `unrelated_diagnostics_carry_no_fix_it` (channel hygiene ŌĆö non-slice-7 diagnostics have `fix_it: None`), `fix_it_type_is_public` (compile-time pin on `karac::typechecker::FixIt` accessibility for IDE consumers). **What slice 7 does *not* do ŌĆö literal-half fix-it.** The literal site (`E_NON_EXHAUSTIVE_CROSS_PACKAGE_LITERAL`) keeps its descriptive message but emits no machine-applicable fix-it: rewriting `Foo { a: 1, b: 2 }` to `Foo.new(a: 1, b: 2)` requires either source-text access (which the typechecker doesn't have) or a multi-edit shape with per-brace spans (which `StructLiteral` AST doesn't carry ŌĆö only the whole-literal span and per-field spans are available). When richer multi-edit fix-its land (or `StructLiteral` gains `lbrace_span` / `rbrace_span`), the literal-half lands as a two-edit `FixIt` rewriting `{` ŌåÆ `.new(` and `}` ŌåÆ `)`; the surface is forward-compatible (`fix_it` becomes `fix_its: Vec<FixIt>` without touching existing producers). The descriptive message at the literal site still steers to `<Name>.new(...)`. Phase target: 5.2 (Language Features). **Closes the `#[non_exhaustive]` epic** ŌĆö the parent `[~]` flips to `[x]`.

- [~] **`#[deprecated]` attribute + `deprecated` lint.** Parser surface + AST `Deprecation` payload on all attribute-bearing item kinds + resolver placement-rejection for `impl` blocks and struct fields (slices 1+2+3a) + resolver symbol-table flag-recording (slice 3b) + typechecker use-site warning emission with cascade integration (slice 4) shipped 2026-05-16 / 2026-05-17; stdlib-canonical-deprecations (slice 6) remains.

  - [x] **Slices 1+2+3a ŌĆö parser, AST payload, resolver placement-rejection shipped 2026-05-16.** Spec sentences honoured: *"Attribute parser ŌĆö recognise `#[deprecated]`, the `#[deprecated = \"note\"]` shorthand, and the long form `#[deprecated(note: \"...\", since: \"...\")]`. Both fields optional; `since` is a free string (advisory; not validated against `kara.toml`). Reject unknown keys with `error[E_DEPRECATED_UNKNOWN_FIELD]` enumerating the accepted set."* + *"AST ŌĆö new `Deprecation { since: Option<String>, note: Option<String>, span: Span }` payload attached to function / struct / enum / ... item nodes; reject the attribute on `impl` blocks (`error[E_DEPRECATED_ON_IMPL]`) and on individual struct fields (`error[E_DEPRECATED_ON_FIELD]` ŌĆö field-level deprecation is post-v1)."* **AST payload** in `src/ast/items.rs`: new `Deprecation { span, since: Option<String>, note: Option<String> }` struct. New `deprecation: Option<Deprecation>` field on every attribute-bearing item kind: `Function`, `StructDef`, `EnumDef`, `TraitDef`, `TraitAliasDef`, `MarkerTraitDef`, `DistinctTypeDef`. Defaulted to `None` at every construction site (parser sets from attribute presence; `prelude.rs`'s stubs default `None`; `typechecker/items.rs`'s synthesized trait-method stub defaults `None`; `effectchecker.rs` and `effectchecker/bounds.rs` synthesized trait-method stubs default `None`). **Parser wiring** in `src/parser/items.rs`: new `scan_deprecated_attr(&attributes) -> Option<Deprecation>` helper recognises all three forms ŌĆö bare `#[deprecated]` (both fields `None`), shorthand `#[deprecated = "note"]` (populates `note`), and long form `#[deprecated(since: "...", note: "...")]` (populates either or both fields per their named-arg presence). Both `name: value` and `name = value` arg-shapes accepted because the underlying attribute parser already produces uniform `AttrArg { name, value }` records. Helper called from every item constructor: `parse_function`, `parse_struct_def`, `parse_enum_def`, `parse_trait_or_alias` (the trait-def tail), `parse_trait_alias_tail`, `parse_marker_trait`, `parse_distinct_type`. **Four parse-time diagnostics**: `E_DEPRECATED_UNKNOWN_FIELD` (per the spec ŌĆö enumerates the accepted set `since`/`note` in the message body); `E_DEPRECATED_FIELD_NOT_STRING` (non-string value on `since`/`note`); `E_DEPRECATED_POSITIONAL_ARG` (positional arg in the long form ŌĆö the shorthand `= "string"` is the only legal unnamed shape); `E_DEPRECATED_DUPLICATE` (multiple `#[deprecated]` on one item ŌĆö first one wins, rest skipped, matches Rust's idempotency). **Resolver placement validation** in `src/resolver/collect.rs`: two new helpers `reject_deprecated_on_impl(attrs)` and `reject_deprecated_on_field(attrs)`, wired into `collect_impl` (block-level) and the `for field in &s.fields` loop inside `collect_struct`. Each emits one diagnostic per offending attribute occurrence. **New `ResolveErrorKind::DeprecatedOnImpl` and `DeprecatedOnField`** in `src/resolver.rs`; mapped to `E0241` and `E0242` in both `src/cli.rs` error-code tables (the diagnostic-emit path and the legacy `resolve_error_code` map ŌĆö both must stay in sync). **Test surface (19 parser tests in `tests/parser.rs`)**: positive form coverage ŌĆö `deprecated_slice1_bare_form_on_function`, `..._shorthand_populates_note`, `..._long_form_with_since_only`, `..._long_form_with_note_only`, `..._long_form_with_both_fields`, `..._long_form_with_equals_separator` (`name = value` shape); per-item-kind coverage ŌĆö `..._struct_captures_payload`, `..._enum_captures_payload`, `..._trait_captures_payload`, `..._marker_trait_captures_payload`, `..._trait_alias_captures_payload`, `..._distinct_type_captures_payload`; regression pin ŌĆö `..._without_attribute_leaves_field_none`; negative form coverage ŌĆö `..._rejects_unknown_field`, `..._rejects_non_string_value`, `..._rejects_positional_arg`, `..._rejects_duplicate_attribute`, `..._first_attribute_wins_when_duplicate`, `..._set_on_impl_block_parser_does_not_reject` (parser captures uniformly; the resolver does placement validation). **Test surface (4 resolver tests in `tests/resolver.rs`)**: `deprecated_slice3_accepted_on_function` (positive pin); `deprecated_slice3_rejected_on_impl_block` (the spec's E_DEPRECATED_ON_IMPL); `deprecated_slice3_rejected_on_struct_field` (the spec's E_DEPRECATED_ON_FIELD); `deprecated_slice3_accepted_on_struct_enum_trait` (negative pin ŌĆö none of these legal placements produce DeprecatedOnImpl/Field diagnostics). **What slices 1+2+3a do *not* do.** No symbol-table flag recording (slice 3b ŌĆö the resolver doesn't yet thread `Deprecation` into the per-symbol metadata, so use-site lookup can't read it cross-module). **[Resolved by slice 3b below ŌĆö shipped 2026-05-17.]** No use-site warning emission (slice 4 ŌĆö blocked on lint registry at line 383: the lint must be registered, suppressible, and dispatchable per the cascade rule); no stdlib annotations (slice 6). The payload is structurally complete at every parsed item; slice 4 will read it back through the resolver's symbol-table extension. **Sub-opens.** Per the spec, `#[deprecated]` is also legal on **enum variants**, **trait methods**, **associated functions** (impl methods, already covered by `Function`), **type aliases**, and **module-level consts**. The first three need attribute support added to `Variant` and `TraitMethod` AST nodes (no `attributes` field today); `TypeAliasDef` and `ConstDecl` need attribute support added too. These are the same enabling change flagged by the `#[track_caller]` slice 1 sub-open (line 389) ŌĆö adding `attributes: Vec<Attribute>` and `deprecation: Option<Deprecation>` to those four AST nodes unblocks both features simultaneously. Tracked as a follow-up because it touches every existing pass that walks `Variant` / `TraitMethod` / `TypeAliasDef` / `ConstDecl` (resolver, typechecker, formatter, span_visitor) ŌĆö a single enabling commit lets the parser side fan out cleanly. The slice 1 surface here is structurally complete for the seven item kinds it covers. (4) Typechecker / use-site check ŌĆö at every reference resolution that lands on a deprecated item (call, type name, variant constructor, pattern, trait-bound, method dispatch), emit the `deprecated` lint (warning level by default) with the focused diagnostic shape from the spec ŌĆö note string surfaced if present, `deprecated since: "..."` line if present, `help: suppress with #[allow(deprecated)]` always present, defining-package note when the deprecated item is `pub`. The lint name is `deprecated`, registered in the central lint registry from the lint-level-attributes entry below. (5) Non-transitivity ŌĆö deprecating a function does not mark its callers, deprecating a struct does not mark its methods unless each method also carries the attribute. Test coverage: bare `#[deprecated]` produces default-message warning; shorthand `#[deprecated = "use X"]` surfaces the note; long form with both fields includes the `since:` line; defining-package internal use produces the same warning (and `#[allow(deprecated)]` at module level suppresses it); reference at every kind of use site (call, type-name, variant constructor, pattern, method dispatch, trait bound) fires the warning; `#[deprecated]` on `impl` rejected; on struct field rejected; unknown field rejected. Phase target: 5.2 (Language Features). Cross-reference: lint-level-attributes entry below for the `#[allow(deprecated)]` / `#[expect(deprecated)]` suppression machinery.

  - [x] **Slice 3b ŌĆö resolver symbol-table flag-recording shipped 2026-05-17.** Closes the slice-1+2+3a sub-open: the resolver now threads each parser-captured `Deprecation` payload into the symbol table so slice-4's use-site lookup pass (once the lint emission infrastructure lands at line 419 slice 4) can read it without re-walking the AST. **Sidecar HashMap** in `src/resolver.rs::SymbolTable`: new `pub deprecations: HashMap<SymbolId, Deprecation>`, keyed by the defined-symbol's id. Mirrors the existing `generic_param_bounds` shape ŌĆö sidecar is preferred over a field on `Symbol` because most symbols are not deprecated (space-efficient + cheaper match arms). **Two helpers** on `SymbolTable`: `record_deprecation(id, dep)` (insertion site) and `deprecation_for(id) -> Option<&Deprecation>` (lookup site for slice 4). **Per-collect-site wiring** in `src/resolver/collect.rs`: each of the eight `collect_*` helpers that registers a top-level symbol with an attribute-bearing item kind now switches from `if let Err(e) = ...` to a `match` on the `define` result, calling `self.record_deprecation_if_present(id, &item.deprecation)` on the Ok arm. Sites wired: `collect_function` (free fns), `collect_struct`, `collect_enum` (top-level + per-variant payload recording for variant-level `#[deprecated]`), `collect_trait`, `collect_trait_alias`, `collect_marker_trait`, `collect_distinct_type`, `collect_const`, `collect_type_alias`. **Impl-method special case** in `collect_impl`: methods bypass `table.define` (they live in `type_methods`, not the global scope) and are pushed directly onto `table.symbols`; slice 3b records the per-method payload via `record_deprecation_if_present(method_id, &method.deprecation)` after the push. **New private helper** `Resolver::record_deprecation_if_present(id, &Option<Deprecation>)` centralises the dispatch so each call-site stays one line. **Trait-method `#[deprecated]` carry-forward.** Trait method declarations carry the `deprecation` payload at the AST level (per the line-431 enabling change), but v1 does not register trait methods as top-level symbols (they're looked up via the trait's method-names list). Slice 3b therefore records the per-trait-method payload only at the impl-block side (where each impl-method gets its own SymbolId); the trait-decl side stays AST-only until slice 4's use-site lookup pass decides whether to consult the trait's method-names list or the impl table. The carry-forward is one-line comment in `collect_trait`. **Test surface (8 new tests in `tests/resolver.rs::deprecated_slice3b_*`)**: `records_payload_on_function` (basic ŌĆö bare `#[deprecated]` produces a recorded payload with both fields `None`); `preserves_since_and_note` (long-form `#[deprecated(since, note)]` round-trips both fields verbatim); `shorthand_populates_note` (`#[deprecated = "..."]` shorthand populates `note` only); `undecorated_symbol_has_no_entry` (regression ŌĆö a plain `fn` does not appear in the sidecar); `per_item_kind_coverage` (one entry per legal target kind ŌĆö fn / struct / enum / trait / marker_trait / pub const / type alias ŌĆö each with a distinct note string so a misrouting would surface as a mismatched assertion); `records_on_enum_variant` (variant-level `#[deprecated]` records against the variant's own SymbolId, not the parent enum's; pins that the parent enum and an undecorated sibling variant both lack entries); `records_on_impl_method` (the bypass-define impl-method path records correctly; pins the sibling-undecorated-method-absent invariant via a `type_methods["S"]` walk); `lookup_returns_distinct_payloads_for_two_items` (two deprecated fns hold distinct payloads ŌĆö pins that the sidecar is keyed by id, not by name). Helper `lookup_deprecation(result, name)` factored at the top of the new test block to keep the per-test assertions concise. **What slice 3b does *not* do.** No use-site emission (slice 4 ŌĆö that's where the lookup helper becomes load-bearing). No cross-module visibility filter (use-sites in a different package querying a deprecated `pub` item see the recorded payload identically to defining-package use-sites ŌĆö visibility filtering is a slice-4 concern when the lint cascade reads the override). No trait-method-decl payload recording into a top-level symbol (the v1 surface only records trait methods at impl-block instantiation; if slice 4 needs trait-decl-side metadata it can extend the helper). Phase target: 5.2 (Language Features).

  - [x] **Slice 4 ŌĆö typechecker use-site warning emission shipped 2026-05-17.** Unblocked by lint-level slice 4b core (the cascade walker landed earlier the same day). Spec sentence honoured: *"Typechecker / use-site check ŌĆö at every reference resolution that lands on a deprecated item (call, type name, variant constructor, pattern, trait-bound, method dispatch), emit the `deprecated` lint (warning level by default) with the focused diagnostic shape from the spec ŌĆö note string surfaced if present, `deprecated since: "..."` line if present, `help: suppress with #[allow(deprecated)]` always present."* **New `TypeErrorKind::Deprecated`** in `src/typechecker.rs`; mapped to `E0245` (errors path under `#[deny(deprecated)]`) / `W0245` (warnings path) in `src/cli.rs` (slot `E0244`/`W0244` is the `unknown_lint` follow-up landed on top of slice 4b core). **`check_deprecated_use_at(span, display_name)` helper** at `src/typechecker.rs:~1062`: queries the resolver's per-span `resolutions` map first; falls back to a global-scope name lookup so call sites where the typechecker resolves via its own env (rather than threading the SpanKey) still surface the warning. Reads `SymbolTable.deprecation_for(sym_id)` (slice-3b plumbing); if `Some(dep)`, builds a message like `"warning[deprecated]: use of deprecated item `name`: <note> (since X) ŌĆö suppress with `#[allow(deprecated)]` on the enclosing item"`, omitting the `note` / `since` clauses when the payload's optional fields are absent. Emits via `type_lint_warning("deprecated", ...)`, routing through the cascade so `#[allow(deprecated)]` / `#[warn(deprecated)]` / `#[deny(deprecated)]` on the enclosing scope take effect (slice 4b core). **Wired at three reference sites** (the most common surfaces; trait-bound and pattern sites are carry-forwards): (1) `resolve_identifier_type` in `src/typechecker/expr_ops.rs:~180` ŌĆö emits when a bare-name reference resolves to a `Function` or `Constant` in the env. (2) `infer_struct_literal` in `src/typechecker/fields.rs` ŌĆö emits when a struct literal's name resolves to a deprecated struct. (3) `lower_path_type` in `src/typechecker/lowering.rs:~349` ŌĆö emits when a type-position reference (`var: OldStruct`) resolves to a known deprecated struct / enum / trait. The borrow-checker required cloning the env lookups (`functions` / `constants`) before the `&mut self` emission call; clones the small `FunctionSig` fields (`params` / `return_type`) and the const's `Type` directly. **Non-transitivity** (spec sentence: *"deprecating a function does not mark its callers"*) is a natural consequence ŌĆö the warning fires at the USE site, not the definition site, so a deprecated fn calling another deprecated fn still produces a warning for the inner call. **Test surface (9 typechecker tests in `tests/typechecker.rs::deprecated_slice4_*`).** Headline: `call_to_deprecated_fn_emits_warning` (positive ŌĆö calling a `#[deprecated]` fn fires the warning with the expected message components: fn name, `deprecated`, suppression hint). `long_form_surfaces_note_and_since` (`#[deprecated(since, note)]` round-trips the note string and the since version into the diagnostic). Cascade integration: `allow_suppresses_at_caller` (the slice-4b cascade silences the warning when the caller is `#[allow(deprecated)]`), `deny_promotes_to_error` (`#[deny(deprecated)]` routes the entry to `errors` instead of `warnings`). Negative-space: `non_deprecated_fn_no_warning` (plain `pub fn` doesn't fire), `self_referential_use_inside_deprecated_fn_emits` (non-transitivity ŌĆö deprecated ŌåÆ deprecated still warns at the inner call). Per-site coverage: `deprecated_const_use_emits_warning` (Constant resolution site), `type_position_use_emits_warning` (`lower_path_type` site), `struct_literal_emits_warning` (`infer_struct_literal` site). **What slice 4 does *not* do.** No emission at method-call sites ŌĆö the typechecker's method-dispatch path doesn't yet thread the resolved symbol's deprecation. No emission at variant-constructor sites ŌĆö variant resolution lives in `resolve_identifier_type`'s variant fallback (the helper is reachable from there but variant names hit the resolver's variant scope, not the symbol-table direct lookup). No emission at pattern reference sites (struct / variant patterns). No emission at trait-bound references in `where` clauses. No emission at impl-method dispatch (`x.old_method()`). All are concrete follow-up sites that would call the same `check_deprecated_use_at` helper at the right point in their respective resolution paths. **Defining-package note** ("when the deprecated item is `pub`") from the spec is also a follow-up ŌĆö today the message doesn't distinguish; the `dep` payload doesn't carry the defining `is_pub` flag through the slice-3b sidecar (it could be added by extending `Deprecation` or by joining with the symbol's `is_pub`). Phase target: 5.2 (Language Features).

- [~] **Lint level attributes `#[allow]` / `#[warn]` / `#[deny]` / `#[expect]`.** Parser + AST + central lint registry (slices 1+2+3a) + `unsafe_op_in_unsafe_fn` hard-rule rejection on the four attributes (slice 6) + broader per-item `lint_overrides` attachment beyond `Function` (slice 4a) + minimal scope cascade with `type_lint_warning` emission integration (slice 4b core) + lint-name carry-through into structured diagnostics (slice 7) + `unknown_lint` warning synthesis + spec-correct `Expect ŌåÆ suppress` semantics (slice 4b follow-up) shipped 2026-05-17; CLI build-wide defaults (`-A` / `-W` / `-D` / `-F`) + forbid mode rejection of inner `#[allow]` (slice 4b polish), broader lint-module integration with the cascade (slice 4b cross-cutting), and `#[expect]` fulfilment tracking ŌĆö emitting `unfulfilled_lint_expectation` when the lint did NOT fire (slice 5) ŌĆö remain.

  - [x] **Slices 1+2+3a ŌĆö parser, AST, central registry shipped 2026-05-17.** Spec sentence honoured for slice 1: *"Attribute parser ŌĆö recognise the four attributes uniformly; each accepts a comma-separated list of lint names (`#[allow(deprecated, rc_fallback)]`); duplicate-lint-name within a single attribute is `error[E_DUPLICATE_LINT_LEVEL]`; unknown lint names produce the `unknown_lint` warning (suppressible)"* + slice 2 AST data type + slice 3 registry. **New `src/lints.rs` module** holds three types ŌĆö `LintLevel { Allow, Warn, Deny, Expect }`, `LintLevelOverride { span, level, lint }`, `LintInfo { name, default_level, description }` ŌĆö plus the central `STARTER_LINTS: &[LintInfo]` array enumerating the 15 v1 lint names from the design.md spec (the 14 listed in the parent-entry plus `malformed_diagnostic_attribute` which the spec calls out separately under `#[diagnostic::*]`). `unsafe_op_in_unsafe_fn` is intentionally absent from the registry ŌĆö per the spec it is a hard rule, not a lint, and the four lint-level attributes are rejected on it (slice 6 enforcement). The `lint_by_name` lookup powers parser-side validation; three module-local tests pin (a) no duplicate registry names, (b) every spec-listed name is present, (c) `LintLevel::from_attr_name` Ōåö `as_attr_name` round-trips. **AST extension** in `src/ast/items.rs`: `Function.lint_overrides: Vec<LintLevelOverride>`, defaulted to empty at every construction site (parser sets from attribute scan; `prelude.rs`'s stub, `typechecker/items.rs`'s synthesized trait-method stub, `effectchecker.rs` + `effectchecker/bounds.rs` synthesized trait-method stubs all default empty). Attachment beyond `Function` is deferred ŌĆö the spec wants overrides on every item / expression-block / statement node that supports attributes, but most of those nodes don't yet carry an `attributes: Vec<Attribute>` field; the broader attachment is bundled with slice 4 (scope cascade) since that's the consumer that needs to walk outward through statement and block scopes. **Parser wiring** in `src/parser/items.rs`: new `scan_lint_level_attrs(&attributes) -> Vec<LintLevelOverride>` helper dispatches on attribute name via `LintLevel::from_attr_name`, extracts lint identifiers from each attribute's positional args (`#[allow(deprecated)]` produces an `AttrArg { name: None, value: Some(Identifier("deprecated")) }` shape; the helper deconstructs this), and emits three parse-time diagnostics: `E_DUPLICATE_LINT_LEVEL` (the same lint name appears twice in one attribute ŌĆö per-attribute scope only; cross-attribute duplicates are accepted because slice 4 will define last-writer-wins semantics), `E_LINT_LEVEL_NON_IDENT_ARG` (the arg is a string literal, key=value pair, or non-identifier expression ŌĆö the spec requires bare identifiers), `E_LINT_LEVEL_NO_ARGS` (the attribute has zero lint names ŌĆö `#[allow]` or `#[allow()]`). The helper is called from `parse_function` and the result threaded into the `Function` constructor. **Unknown lint names are silently accepted at this slice** ŌĆö per the design.md "Naming" rule ("code with `#[allow(removed_lint)]` continues to compile (the attribute targets an unknown lint, which is itself the `unknown_lint` warning, suppressible)"), an unknown name must NOT break the build. Silencing today is the safe default; the `unknown_lint` warning emission lands with slice 4's lint emission infrastructure (parser-side warnings don't have an emission channel yet). **Test surface (3 unit tests in `src/lints.rs` + 13 parser integration tests in `tests/parser.rs`).** Unit: registry well-formedness pins. Parser: `lint_attrs_slice1_allow_single_lint_captures_override` (basic ŌĆö `#[allow(deprecated)]` populates the override); `lint_attrs_slice1_all_four_attribute_names_recognized` (all four levels round-trip); `lint_attrs_slice1_comma_separated_list_produces_multiple_overrides` (`#[allow(a, b, c)]` produces three overrides); `lint_attrs_slice1_function_without_attribute_has_empty_overrides` (regression pin); `lint_attrs_slice1_unknown_lint_silently_accepted` (the spec's forward-compat pin); `lint_attrs_slice1_duplicate_lint_in_single_attribute_rejected` (E_DUPLICATE_LINT_LEVEL); `lint_attrs_slice1_duplicate_in_separate_attrs_currently_allowed` (cross-attribute duplicates accepted ŌĆö pin for the scope-cascade decision); `lint_attrs_slice1_empty_arg_list_rejected` (`#[allow()]` ŌåÆ E_LINT_LEVEL_NO_ARGS); `lint_attrs_slice1_bare_form_with_no_args_rejected` (bare `#[allow]` same diagnostic family); `lint_attrs_slice1_string_value_rejected` (`#[allow = "..."]` ŌåÆ E_LINT_LEVEL_NON_IDENT_ARG); `lint_attrs_slice1_key_value_arg_rejected` (`#[allow(deprecated = "oops")]` same diagnostic); `lint_attrs_slice1_spans_point_at_lint_name` (override span localises the name, not the whole attribute); `lint_attrs_slice1_attribute_coexists_with_other_attributes` (`#[allow]` next to `#[track_caller]` + `#[deprecated]` doesn't conflict). **What slices 1+2+3a do *not* do.** (a) Attachment beyond `Function` ŌĆö no `lint_overrides` on `StructDef`, `EnumDef`, `TraitDef`, statement nodes, or expression blocks (slice 4 bundles broader attachment with the cascade). (b) No `unknown_lint` warning ŌĆö silently accepts unknown names (slice 4 emission infrastructure). (c) No cascade ŌĆö the overrides are structurally captured but no existing warning consults them yet. (d) No `#[expect]` fulfilment tracking (slice 5). (e) No `unsafe_op_in_unsafe_fn` hard-rule rejection on `#[warn]` / `#[deny]` / `#[expect]` (slice 6 ŌĆö today only `#[allow(unsafe_op_in_unsafe_fn)]` is rejected via the older one-rule guard in `parse_attribute`). **[Resolved by slice 6 below.]** (f) No lint-name field on structured diagnostics (slice 7). Slices 1+2+3a are the foundation: with the registry + AST data type + parser surface in place, slice 4 reads `lint_overrides`, walks outward through scopes, and decides effective level per emission. (4) Scope cascade ŌĆö when emitting a lint, walk outward from the current scope to find the nearest `#[allow]` / `#[warn]` / `#[deny]` / `#[expect]` for the named lint; the innermost match wins. CLI flags (`-A NAME` / `-W NAME` / `-D NAME` / `-F NAME`) set the build-wide default that the cascade falls through to; the existing `-D warnings` flag is the canonical "treat all warnings as errors" form and works by promoting every lint's effective level to `Deny`. The `-F` (forbid) flag, like Rust's `#![forbid]`, additionally disallows inner `#[allow]` overrides ŌĆö an inner `#[allow]` of a forbidden lint produces `error[E_FORBIDDEN_LINT_ALLOW]`. (5) `#[expect]` semantics ŌĆö track per-attribute whether the named lint fired anywhere within the attributed scope (an "expectation fulfilled" bit). At end-of-typecheck, every `#[expect]` whose bit is unset emits `unfulfilled_lint_expectation` pointing at the attribute itself. Reject `#[expect(unfulfilled_lint_expectation)]` with `error[E_EXPECT_ON_UNFULFILLED]` (would be circular). The `unfulfilled_lint_expectation` lint is itself suppressible with `#[allow(unfulfilled_lint_expectation)]`. (6) `unsafe_op_in_unsafe_fn` exception ŌĆö this is a hard rule, not a lint; the four lint-level attributes are rejected on it (`error[E_LINT_LEVEL_ON_HARD_RULE]`). (7) Diagnostics ŌĆö every warning emitted by the compiler must record the lint name in the structured diagnostic so `karac explain --json` consumers can route, group, and filter by lint. Test coverage: `#[allow(deprecated)]` suppresses one warning; nested `#[warn(deprecated)]` overrides outer `#[allow]` for inner code only; `#[expect(rc_fallback)]` on a fn that triggers the lint is silent; the same `#[expect]` on a fn that doesn't trigger the lint emits `unfulfilled_lint_expectation`; multiple lints in one attribute (`#[allow(rc_fallback, implicit_clone)]`) work; `#[deny(deprecated)]` promotes the lint to a build error; `-D warnings` CLI flag treats every warning as an error; `-F deprecated` rejects an inner `#[allow(deprecated)]`; unknown lint name (`#[allow(no_such_lint)]`) emits `unknown_lint` warning suppressible with `#[allow(unknown_lint)]`; `#[expect]` cannot wrap `unfulfilled_lint_expectation`; lint level attributes on `unsafe_op_in_unsafe_fn` rejected. Phase target: 5.2 (Language Features). Cross-reference: design.md ┬¦ Lint Level Attributes for the surface, `#[deprecated]` entry above for the canonical first user.

  - [x] **Slice 6 ŌĆö `unsafe_op_in_unsafe_fn` hard-rule rejection on all four lint-level attributes shipped 2026-05-17.** Spec sentence honoured: *"`unsafe_op_in_unsafe_fn` exception ŌĆö this is a hard rule, not a lint; the four lint-level attributes are rejected on it (`error[E_LINT_LEVEL_ON_HARD_RULE]`)."* **Generalised the existing one-rule guard** in `src/parser/attributes.rs::parse_attribute` (the slice-5 `unsafe_op_in_unsafe_fn`-epic guard at lines ~142-173) from `name == "allow"` to `matches!(name.as_str(), "allow" | "warn" | "deny" | "expect")`. Same `iter().any(...)` arg-shape check (positional `IDENT` and the theoretical named `name = IDENT` form, both routed through `ExprKind::Identifier` matching). The diagnostic string now carries the symbolic `error[E_LINT_LEVEL_ON_HARD_RULE]:` prefix (was the bare slice-5 phrasing) and quotes the offending attribute's literal form back to the author so the source-line and the diagnostic stay grepably aligned; the redirect to `unsafe { ... }` + `// Safety:` comment is preserved verbatim from slice 5. **Why a stringy match instead of `LintLevel::from_attr_name`.** `src/parser/attributes.rs` lives at the AST-walk layer; calling into `crate::lints` from there would introduce a parserŌåÆlints dependency for one boolean. The four attribute names are a fixed v1 surface per the spec ("each accepts a comma-separated list of lint names"), and the slice-1+2+3a tests already pin the round-trip with the registry ŌĆö a string-list mismatch would surface there first. **Per-arg scope.** If `unsafe_op_in_unsafe_fn` appears anywhere inside one of the four attribute's args (alone or in a multi-name list like `#[warn(undocumented_unsafe, unsafe_op_in_unsafe_fn)]`), the whole attribute is rejected via `iter().any()`. **No other lint name is touched** ŌĆö `#[warn(deprecated)]` / `#[deny(rc_fallback)]` / `#[expect(implicit_clone)]` continue to parse cleanly; the slice-4 cascade reads them. **Test surface (4 new + 2 retitled + 1 amended in `tests/parser.rs`).** New tests covering the three previously-accepted attribute names: `test_lint_level_on_hard_rule_rejects_warn`, `test_lint_level_on_hard_rule_rejects_deny` (replaces the prior `test_deny_unsafe_op_in_unsafe_fn_still_accepted` regression pin, which deliberately pinned the slice-5 scoping decision that slice 6 now flips), `test_lint_level_on_hard_rule_rejects_expect`, `test_lint_level_on_hard_rule_rejects_warn_in_multi_lint_list` (iter-any branch on the new attribute names). Positive pin: `test_lint_level_attrs_with_other_lint_names_still_accepted` ensures the rejection is scoped to `unsafe_op_in_unsafe_fn` only ŌĆö `#[warn(deprecated)]` + `#[deny(rc_fallback)]` + `#[expect(implicit_clone)]` on the same fn parse cleanly. The existing `test_allow_unsafe_op_in_unsafe_fn_rejected_with_focused_diagnostic` is amended to assert the `E_LINT_LEVEL_ON_HARD_RULE` symbolic code in the diagnostic body and to spell "hard rule" instead of "hard error" (the latter wording was specific to the slice-5 framing). The slice-5 section header in `tests/parser.rs` is retitled to point at slice 6 of the lint-level-attributes entry, since the rejection is now centrally owned by lint-level slice 6 rather than the `unsafe_op_in_unsafe_fn` epic. **What slice 6 does *not* do.** No cascade integration (slice 4) ŌĆö slice 6 fires at parse time, before any scope cascade exists; the cascade can't suppress a parse-time error in any case (the rule is hard, not a lint). No `#[expect]` fulfilment tracking (slice 5) ŌĆö the `#[expect(unsafe_op_in_unsafe_fn)]` rejection here predates the fulfilment machinery; when slice 5 lands, the `unsafe_op_in_unsafe_fn` name will already have been rejected at parse, so the fulfilment pass never sees it. No lint-name field on the structured diagnostic (slice 7) ŌĆö the diagnostic is a parser error, not a lint emission; slice 7 covers lints. Phase target: 5.2 (Language Features).

  - [x] **Slice 4a ŌĆö broader `lint_overrides` attachment beyond `Function` shipped 2026-05-17.** The slice-1+2+3a ship note flagged attachment as "deferred ŌĆö most nodes don't yet carry an `attributes: Vec<Attribute>` field; the broader attachment is bundled with slice 4". The AST-enabling changes at line 437 / 439 (`Variant` + `TraitMethod` + `ConstDecl` + `TypeAliasDef`) closed the field-existence gap; this slice ships the broader `lint_overrides: Vec<LintLevelOverride>` attachment that the cascade (slice 4b) will read. **AST extension** in `src/ast/items.rs`: `StructDef`, `EnumDef`, `TraitDef`, `TraitAliasDef`, `MarkerTraitDef`, `DistinctTypeDef`, `ConstDecl`, `TypeAliasDef`, `ImplBlock` all gain a `lint_overrides: Vec<LintLevelOverride>` field, mirroring the `Function` shape. **Parser wiring** in `src/parser/items.rs` + `src/parser/items_trait.rs`: every `parse_*` site that constructs one of the nine extended item kinds calls `self.scan_lint_level_attrs(&attributes)` and threads the result into the constructor. `scan_lint_level_attrs` is the existing helper from slice 1; same diagnostic surface (`E_DUPLICATE_LINT_LEVEL` / `E_LINT_LEVEL_NON_IDENT_ARG` / `E_LINT_LEVEL_NO_ARGS`) carried forward unchanged ŌĆö slice 4a is structurally a field addition, not a parser-behaviour change. **Prelude stubs** in `src/prelude.rs::stub_struct` / `stub_trait` default to `lint_overrides: Vec::new()` (synthetic stubs never carry user-authored attributes; the field is structurally present so the AST shape is uniform). **No semantic effect today.** The cascade reader is slice 4b; without it, the attached overrides are inert (the existing emission sites in `must_use_lint`, `unsafe_lint`, etc. don't yet consult `lint_overrides` from the surrounding scope chain). Slice 4a is the foundation that lets slice 4b walk outward from a diagnostic-emit site through `Function ŌåÆ ImplBlock ŌåÆ containing TraitDef/EnumDef/StructDef ŌåÆ module-level CLI flags` and pick the innermost matching `#[allow]` / `#[warn]` / `#[deny]` / `#[expect]`. **Test surface (11 parser tests in `tests/parser.rs::lint_attrs_slice4a_*`).** One round-trip pin per attachment site: struct (`#[allow(deprecated)]` captures), struct-without-attribute (regression pin ŌĆö empty), enum, trait, trait alias, marker trait, distinct type, module const, type alias, impl block. Multi-lint-list pin (`#[allow(deprecated, rc_fallback, implicit_clone)]` on a struct captures three overrides ŌĆö exercises the `scan_lint_level_attrs` iteration on the new item kinds). The diagnostic surface (duplicates, non-ident args, empty lists) is already pinned by slice 1's tests on `Function`; slice 4a relies on the helper's centrality to skip re-testing each negative form per-item-kind. **What slice 4a does *not* do.** No cascade ŌĆö emission sites still don't consult `lint_overrides`. No `unknown_lint` emission. No `#[expect]` fulfilment tracking. No CLI flag (`-A` / `-W` / `-D` / `-F`). All of those bundle into slice 4b alongside the actual cascade walker. Phase target: 5.2 (Language Features). **Unblocks slice 4b** (the cascade reader has fields to read), **slice 5** (`#[expect]` fulfilment will key off the same data), and **slice 7** (per-lint diagnostic routing reads from the same overrides). **[Slice 7 ŌĆö see below ŌĆö shipped on the same date.]**

  - [x] **Slice 7 ŌĆö lint-name carry-through into structured diagnostics shipped 2026-05-17.** Spec sentence honoured: *"every warning emitted by the compiler must record the lint name in the structured diagnostic so `karac explain --json` consumers can route, group, and filter by lint."* **`TypeError` extension** in `src/typechecker.rs`: new `lint_name: Option<String>` field on the unified error/warning carrier (the same struct is reused for `errors` and `warnings` vectors). Defaulted to `None` at every existing construction site; populated only at lint-style emission points. **New helper `type_lint_warning(msg, span, kind, lint_name: &'static str)`** in `src/typechecker.rs` replaces `type_warning` for any lint-routed warning. The original `type_warning` (lint-name-less) has been removed ŌĆö the spec mandates every warning carry a lint name, so a name-less helper is a footgun; future warning emitters call `type_lint_warning` directly. **Wiring at the existing emission site** (`src/typechecker/patterns.rs::check_exhaustiveness`): the `UnreachableArm` warning now routes through `type_lint_warning` with `"unreachable_arm"` as the lint name. **Registry extension** in `src/lints.rs`: `STARTER_LINTS` gains an `unreachable_arm` entry with `default_level: LintLevel::Warn` so the slice-4b cascade reader can look up the default. The spec-list completeness pin (`starter_set_covers_spec_listed_lints`) is unaffected ŌĆö `unreachable_arm` isn't on the spec's original 15-name v1 starter list, and the pin's `required` array stays a strict subset. **JSON output extension** in `src/cli.rs`: `DiagEntry` gains a `lint_name: Option<&str>` field that serializes as `"lint_name":"..."` in the JSON output (positioned between `hints` and `extra_json` in the entry shape so existing field-position assumptions stay stable). All 10 `DiagEntry` construction sites updated ŌĆö 9 set `lint_name: None` (hard errors and warnings that haven't migrated to a registered lint yet), one passes through `warn.lint_name.as_deref()` for the typechecker warning channel. **Test surface (4 typechecker tests in `tests/typechecker.rs::lint_attrs_slice7_*`).** `unreachable_arm_warning_carries_lint_name` (headline ŌĆö the `UnreachableArm` warning's `lint_name` field is `Some("unreachable_arm")`); `clean_match_has_no_warnings_with_lint_name` (regression ŌĆö clean code emits no warnings; lint_name only populates on fire); `unreachable_arm_lint_is_registered` (pins the registry contains the name so the cascade reader's `lint_by_name` lookup will succeed); `error_kinds_have_lint_name_none` (pin that hard errors stay `lint_name: None` ŌĆö a future drift that auto-populates would silence the slice-7 surface). **What slice 7 does *not* do.** No cascade integration ŌĆö the field is populated, but `#[allow(unreachable_arm)]` doesn't yet suppress the warning (slice 4b reads `lint_overrides` + the cascade walker to decide). No JSON pre-existing-warning migration ŌĆö lint-module warnings (`unsafe_lint`, `must_use_lint`, etc.) currently render to stderr only, not through `DiagEntry`'s JSON channel; routing them through is a separate plumbing step. No CLI text-format change ŌĆö the rustc-style `warning[name]:` prefix on stderr renders unchanged today. Phase target: 5.2 (Language Features). **Unblocks the slice-4b cascade** which now has a `lint_name`-aware warning channel to consult; slice 4b walks outward from the warning's span, finds the innermost matching `lint_overrides` entry for the named lint, and either suppresses / promotes / records expectation fulfilment. **[Slice 4b core ŌĆö see below ŌĆö shipped on the same date.]**

  - [~] **Slice 4b core ŌĆö minimal scope cascade with emission integration shipped 2026-05-17.** Closes the slice-7 carry-forward ŌĆö `lint_overrides` are now consulted at emission time, not just structurally captured. Spec sentence honoured: *"Scope cascade ŌĆö when emitting a lint, walk outward from the current scope to find the nearest `#[allow]` / `#[warn]` / `#[deny]` / `#[expect]` for the named lint; the innermost match wins."* CLI flags (`-A NAME` / `-W NAME` / `-D NAME` / `-F NAME`), forbid-mode rejection of inner `#[allow]`, and `unknown_lint` warning emission are slice-4b polish that lands when there's a use case (today no warning-channel consumer routes through the cascade besides `type_lint_warning`). **`lint_override_stack: Vec<Vec<LintLevelOverride>>`** on `TypeChecker` ŌĆö pushed at every item-walk entry, popped on exit. Wired at `check_function` (line 800 ŌĆö after `current_fn_stdlib_origin` save/restore), `check_impl_block` (line ~980 ŌĆö after `enclosing_bounds` save), and `check_trait_def` (line 91 ŌĆö after `enclosing_trait` save). Push/pop pairs are symmetric with the existing `current_return_type` / `enclosing_bounds` save/restore patterns; the stack invariant is "innermost frame at the top, popped on item exit". **`effective_lint_level(&self, lint_name: &str) -> LintLevel`** at `src/typechecker.rs:~1010` ŌĆö walks `lint_override_stack` innermost-first (outer Vec, then innermost-to-outermost within the frame), returns the first matching `LintLevelOverride.level`. Falls through to `crate::lints::lint_by_name(lint_name).default_level` on miss; unknown lint names fall through to `LintLevel::Warn` (matches the design.md "Naming" rule of "unknown lint names continue to compile"). **`type_lint_warning` integration** at `src/typechecker.rs:~975` ŌĆö consults `effective_lint_level` before deciding where to push the entry: `Allow` ŌåÆ suppressed silently; `Warn` / `Expect` ŌåÆ pushed to `warnings`; `Deny` ŌåÆ pushed to `errors` (the message is reused unchanged ŌĆö the cascade only changes the severity). `Expect` behaves like `Warn` today; slice 5's fulfilment tracking will record whether the expected lint actually fired. **Test surface (7 typechecker tests in `tests/typechecker.rs::lint_attrs_slice4b_*`).** `allow_suppresses_unreachable_arm_warning` (headline ŌĆö `#[allow(unreachable_arm)]` on a fn silences the warning); `deny_promotes_unreachable_arm_to_error` (`#[deny]` routes to errors, not warnings ŌĆö pins the asymmetry); `warn_explicit_keeps_warning_behavior` (no-op `#[warn]` on default-warn-level lint still emits); `unrelated_allow_does_not_suppress` (cascade matches on lint name ŌĆö `#[allow(deprecated)]` doesn't silence `unreachable_arm`); `default_behavior_unchanged_without_override` (regression ŌĆö un-annotated code keeps the existing Warn behavior; the lint_name field stays populated); `impl_block_allow_propagates_to_methods` (cascade walks outward ŌĆö an `#[allow]` on the impl block silences a warning fired inside a method body; pins push/pop on `check_impl_block`); `inner_warn_overrides_outer_allow` (the cascade rule ŌĆö innermost wins; inner `#[warn]` re-enables a warning that outer `#[allow]` would have silenced). **What slice 4b core does *not* do.** No CLI build-wide flags. No forbid-mode rejection of inner `#[allow]` (slice 4b polish). No `unknown_lint` warning emission (would need a separate emission site walking each captured override). No integration with `unsafe_lint` / `must_use_lint` / `missing_must_use_lint` / `logical_lint` ŌĆö those modules emit through their own `LintDiagnostic` channels and don't yet consult the cascade. Migration is per-module (each lint walks its own AST and would push frames the same way `check_function` does); deferred until a concrete need arises. No `#[expect]` fulfilment tracking (slice 5). No module-level / file-level `#![allow(...)]` (K─üra has no current equivalent to Rust's inner attributes). Phase target: 5.2 (Language Features). **Unblocks** lint-style suppression on every existing typechecker warning that migrates to `type_lint_warning`, and the slice-5 fulfilment tracking which keys off the same `effective_lint_level` channel.

  - [x] **Slice 4b follow-up ŌĆö `unknown_lint` synthesis + `Expect` suppression shipped 2026-05-17.** Closes two of slice 4b core's deferred items in a single focused commit on top of the slice 4b core push/pop cascade. **`unknown_lint` synthesis** (`src/typechecker.rs::emit_unknown_lint_warnings`): a pre-pass in `TypeChecker::check()` (invoked between `check_signature_visibility` and `check_items`, so the cascade-aware emission path is wired before any per-item walk runs) collects every item's `lint_overrides` and, for each override whose `lint` name is not in `crate::lints::STARTER_LINTS`, pushes the item's frame (and the surrounding impl-block frame for impl methods) onto `lint_override_stack`, then emits an `unknown_lint` warning via `type_lint_warning`. Cascade self-suppression works because the item's own overrides are the innermost frame at emission time ŌĆö `#[allow(unknown_lint, removed_lint)]` resolves to `Allow` and drops the warning. The synthesizer walks every item kind that carries `lint_overrides` post-slice-4a (`Function`, `StructDef`, `EnumDef`, `TraitDef`, `TraitAlias`, `MarkerTrait`, `ImplBlock`, `ConstDecl`, `TypeAlias`, `DistinctType`); impl-block methods get their own frame on top of the impl block's. The free helper `has_unknown_lint(&[LintLevelOverride])` short-circuits the per-item work when no unregistered name appears. **`TypeErrorKind::UnknownLint`** new variant, mapped to `W0244` in both the error-loop and warning-loop code tables in `src/cli.rs` (so a `#[deny(unknown_lint)]` Deny-promotion surfaces with the same symbolic code on the error side). The error-loop `DiagEntry` construction in `cli.rs` now propagates `err.lint_name.as_deref()` instead of `None` so consumers see *which lint* drove a warning-promoted-to-error through the JSON output. **`Expect ŌåÆ suppress` semantics** (`src/typechecker.rs::type_lint_warning`): the slice 4b core's `LintLevel::Warn | LintLevel::Expect ŌåÆ push to warnings` arm split into `Warn ŌåÆ push` and `Expect ŌåÆ suppress`. Per design.md ┬¦ Lint Level Attributes, *"`#[expect(NAME)]` on a fn that triggers the lint is silent"* ŌĆö the user has acknowledged the lint by writing `#[expect]` and the firing is silent. Slice 5 will additionally track fulfilment and emit `unfulfilled_lint_expectation` when the named lint did NOT fire in the attributed scope (the un-fired case). **Test surface (5 typechecker tests in `tests/typechecker.rs::lint_attrs_slice4b_*` on top of slice 4b core's 7).** `expect_suppresses_like_allow` (headline ŌĆö `#[expect(unreachable_arm)]` on a fn whose match has an unreachable arm produces no warning); `inner_allow_overrides_outer_deny` (cascade rule mirror ŌĆö innermost `#[allow]` overrides an outer `#[deny]`, so the warning is suppressed not promoted; pins the cascade walks past the impl-block frame); `unknown_lint_emits_warning` (synthesis pin ŌĆö `#[allow(no_such_lint)]` fires an `UnknownLint` warning with `lint_name = Some("unknown_lint")`); `unknown_lint_is_suppressible` (self-suppression ŌĆö `#[allow(unknown_lint, no_such_lint)]` silences itself); `multiple_lints_in_one_attribute` (`#[allow(deprecated, unreachable_arm)]` exercises the per-name lookup on a multi-arg attribute). All 7 slice 4b core tests + the slice 7 lint-name carry-through tests + the 1000+ pre-existing typechecker tests continue to pass. **What the follow-up does *not* do.** No CLI build-wide flags (`-A` / `-W` / `-D NAME` / `-F NAME`) ŌĆö slice 4b polish. No `-F`-driven inner-`#[allow]` rejection (`E_FORBIDDEN_LINT_ALLOW`) ŌĆö slice 4b polish. No statement / expression-block level overrides ŌĆö those AST nodes don't carry `lint_overrides`. No migration of other-phase warning emitters (`unsafe_lint`, `must_use_lint`, `ffi_lint`, `logical_lint`) into the cascade ŌĆö each module would need to push frames the way `check_function` does, or route through `type_lint_warning`; that is the slice 4b cross-cutting work which lands per-module as concrete use cases appear. No `#[expect]` fulfilment tracking (slice 5). Phase target: 5.2.

- [ ] **`#[diagnostic::*]` attribute namespace ŌĆö `on_unimplemented` and `do_not_recommend`.** Spec at `design.md ┬¦ Diagnostic Namespace Attributes` (v60 item 36). Slices: (1) Lexer / parser ŌĆö extend the attribute path grammar to accept `IDENT { "::" IDENT }` per syntax.md ┬¦8 (a single-segment path is the existing case; multi-segment paths are new). AST: `Attribute { path: Vec<String>, ... }` replaces the existing single-name field; downstream consumers that look up the name now read `path[-1]` with namespace context. (2) Namespace dispatch ŌĆö central `KnownAttributeNamespace` registry in the attribute checker recognises `diagnostic::*` (and, eventually, the tool namespaces from item 37) as **silent-on-unknown** namespaces. The default behavior for an unrecognized bare-name attribute is `error[E_UNKNOWN_ATTRIBUTE]`; the default for an unrecognized member of a silent-on-unknown namespace is **accept silently, no warning**. Malformed members (recognized name, wrong shape) emit the `malformed_diagnostic_attribute` lint (warn-by-default). (3) `#[diagnostic::on_unimplemented]` ŌĆö recognise on `trait` declarations only; off-target produces the malformed-diagnostic warning. Argument shape is three optional named fields: `message: STRING_LITERAL`, `label: STRING_LITERAL`, `note: STRING_LITERAL`. Template placeholders `{Self}`, `{T0}`, `{T1}`, ... are recognised and substituted at diagnostic emit time using the failed-bound's solved metavariable map; unknown placeholders render literally and emit a build-time warning at the trait declaration site. (4) `#[diagnostic::do_not_recommend]` ŌĆö recognise on `impl` blocks only (inherent and trait); off-target produces the malformed-diagnostic warning. Captured as a flag on the impl's symbol-table entry; consulted by the failed-bound diagnostic builder when iterating candidate impls for the "trait is implemented by ..." note (skip flagged impls). Has no effect on coherence, lookup, or trait resolution ŌĆö purely diagnostic. (5) Lint registry ŌĆö register `malformed_diagnostic_attribute` in the central lint registry from item 35's lint-level-attributes entry (warn-by-default; suppressible with `#[allow(malformed_diagnostic_attribute)]`). (6) Integration with the existing failed-bound diagnostic ŌĆö when typechecker emits `error[E_UNSATISFIED_BOUND]` for a `T: SomeTrait` failure, consult the trait's `on_unimplemented` payload (if any), substitute placeholders against the resolved metavariable map, and use the result as the diagnostic's headline / span label / note in place of the default phrasing. Identical behavior whether the trait is local or imported. (7) Testing strategy ŌĆö covers both the namespace machinery and the two adopted members. Test coverage: positive ŌĆö `#[diagnostic::on_unimplemented(message: "...")]` on a trait surfaces the custom message at a failed-bound site; `{Self}` placeholder substitutes the failing type; multiple fields all surface in the right slots; unknown member `#[diagnostic::polish_my_error_pretty]` is silently accepted with no warning at the use site; `#[diagnostic::do_not_recommend]` on a blanket impl removes that impl from the "implemented by" note while still allowing the impl to satisfy bounds. Negative ŌĆö `#[diagnostic::on_unimplemented]` on a function emits `malformed_diagnostic_attribute`; misspelled field name (`#[diagnostic::on_unimplemented(messsage: "...")]`) emits the same lint; multiple `#[diagnostic::on_unimplemented]` on one trait emits warning and uses the first; unknown placeholder `{NotAParam}` emits build-time warning at the trait decl and renders literally; `#[diagnostic::do_not_recommend]` on a function or struct emits the malformed lint and is ignored; an unknown bare-name attribute `#[no_such_thing]` is still `error[E_UNKNOWN_ATTRIBUTE]` (silent-on-unknown applies only to namespaced paths). Phase target: 5.2 (Language Features). Cross-reference: design.md ┬¦ Diagnostic Namespace Attributes; implementation_checklist/ item 35 lint-level-attributes entry (for the lint registry the new `malformed_diagnostic_attribute` lint plugs into); item 37's tool-namespaced attributes share the same path-form lexer/parser change.

- [ ] **Tool-namespaced attributes `#[TOOL::NAME(...)]`.** Spec at `design.md ┬¦ Tool-Namespaced Attributes` (v60 item 37). Slices: (1) Attribute checker discriminator ŌĆö extend the namespace dispatch from item 36 (`KnownAttributeNamespace`) to recognize the *first segment* of every multi-segment attribute path: if the segment matches a compiler-reserved namespace (currently only `diagnostic`), validate per the corresponding spec (item 36); otherwise treat as a tool namespace and accept silently. A bare-name attribute (single-segment path) that doesn't match a known compiler attribute remains `error[E_UNKNOWN_ATTRIBUTE]` ŌĆö the silent-on-unknown rule applies *only* to multi-segment paths, never to bare names. (2) AST representation ŌĆö the existing `Attribute { path: Vec<String>, args: Vec<AttrArg>, span: Span }` shape from item 36 already covers tool-namespaced attributes; no new variant needed. The arguments are stored verbatim (parsed, not validated). Tools are responsible for their own argument-shape validation. (3) `karac query attributes [--tool PREFIX]` subcommand ŌĆö new query command emitting a JSON list of every multi-segment attribute on every item, filtered by tool-name prefix when `--tool` is provided. Output shape: one record per attribute with `path` (the full path), `args` (the parsed arg list as JSON), `attached_to` (item kind + qualified name), `span` (file/line/col). The `--tool` filter is a first-segment match (`--tool karafmt` returns every `#[karafmt::*]`); without `--tool`, returns every multi-segment attribute. (4) Language-server integration ŌĆö the existing LSP surfaces item-level attributes through workspace-symbol responses; extend it to include tool attributes when the LSP client requests them by namespace prefix. The compile-as-library API exposes the same `Attribute` structure. (5) v1-reserved name-claim ŌĆö document `karafmt::*`, `karalint::*`, `karadoc::*` as reserved for the canonical first-party tools that will ship post-v1; user attributes against these names parse and store like any other tool attribute, but the names cannot be claimed by other tools. The reservation is documentary (in design.md and the attribute reference book appendix) ŌĆö there is no compiler-side enforcement that another tool cannot collide with these names; the social authority is "first reserved, first served." (6) No `#[register_tool(name)]` mechanism at v1 ŌĆö open namespace rule applies; per-project tool registration is a deferred feature (post-v1 quality-of-life addition for typo detection). Test coverage: positive ŌĆö `#[karafmt::skip]` on a function parses, stores, emits no diagnostic, appears in `karac query attributes --tool karafmt` output; `#[arbitrary_tool::custom_thing(arg1: 1, arg2: "x")]` likewise ŌĆö fully open namespace; multi-arg tool attributes parse with full `IDENT ":" EXPR` arg shape; tool attribute on every item kind (function, struct, enum, trait, impl, module-const) accepted; attribute attached to a stmt/block accepted with no diagnostic but documented as exotic. Negative ŌĆö bare-name unknown attribute `#[no_such_thing]` still rejected with `E_UNKNOWN_ATTRIBUTE` (silent-on-unknown applies only to multi-segment paths); compiler-reserved namespace member with malformed args still emits `malformed_diagnostic_attribute` warn (item 36 rule, not subsumed by tool-namespace silence). Phase target: 5.2 (Language Features). Cross-reference: design.md ┬¦ Tool-Namespaced Attributes; item 36 attribute-namespace dispatch (shares the same `KnownAttributeNamespace` machinery ŌĆö item 36 lands the `diagnostic::*` arm, this entry lands the catch-all tool-namespace arm); `karac query attributes` command lands together with this entry as the tool-facing read surface.

- [~] **`#[track_caller]` for stdlib panic-emitters ŌĆö caller-location redirection.** Parser flag + resolver placement validation (slice 1) shipped 2026-05-16; resolver/typechecker pass-through (slice 3) is a no-op the slice 1 wiring already preserves; codegen call-lowering with hidden caller-location parameter (slice 4), panic runtime integration (slice 5), stdlib annotations (slice 6), and `missing_track_caller` lint (slice 7, depends on lint registry at line 383) remain. Sub-open: **trait method declarations don't carry attributes today** ŌĆö `TraitMethod` has no `attributes` field at the AST level, so the spec's "trait method declarations are accepted; the attribute applies to every impl unless an impl explicitly drops it" rule needs a separate enabling change before the slice-1 parser/resolver path can extend to trait methods. Implement the spec in `design.md ┬¦ Error Handling > Stdlib panic-emitters report the caller's source location` and the cross-reference at `design.md ┬¦ Crash Report Format > Panic site`.

  - [x] **Slice 1 ŌĆö parser flag + resolver placement validation shipped 2026-05-16.** Spec sentences honoured: *"Attribute parser ŌĆö recognize `#[track_caller]` as a function-level attribute; reject on items that aren't `fn` declarations ...; reject arguments ŌĆö the attribute takes none"* and *"AST ŌĆö capture as a boolean `is_track_caller: bool` field on the existing `Function` node."* Bundles spec slices 1 + 2 because (per the `#[non_exhaustive]` precedent shipped earlier this session) the AST field is the parser's storage shape ŌĆö splitting them lands an unused field for one commit. **AST extension** in `src/ast/items.rs`: `Function.is_track_caller: bool`, defaulted to `false` at every construction site (parser sets the flag from attribute presence; `prelude.rs`'s `stub_function`, `typechecker/items.rs`'s trait-method synthesized stub, `effectchecker.rs`'s trait-method synthesized stub, `effectchecker/bounds.rs`'s trait-method scan stub all default `false` ŌĆö none of those synthesized stubs represent a user-authored function so the flag is structurally `false`). **Parser wiring** in `src/parser/items.rs`: `parse_function` calls a new `scan_track_caller_attr(&attributes)` helper that returns the flag and emits `E_TRACK_CALLER_ARGS_NOT_PERMITTED` for any occurrence carrying args (`#[track_caller(extra)]`) or a string value (`#[track_caller = "..."]`); the diagnostic is anchored at the attribute's own span. Duplicates are accepted silently ŌĆö bare `#[track_caller]` is idempotent, and a "duplicate attribute" lint belongs to the lint registry (line 383) once it lands. **Resolver placement validation** in `src/resolver/collect.rs`: new `reject_track_caller_attr(attrs, target_kind)` helper emits one `E_TRACK_CALLER_INVALID_TARGET` diagnostic per occurrence on a disallowed item, naming the target kind in the message (`"struct"`, `"enum"`, `"trait"`, `"marker trait"`, `"trait alias"`, `"impl block"`, `"struct field"`). Wired into every non-`fn` `collect_*` site: `collect_struct` (block + each field), `collect_enum`, `collect_trait`, `collect_trait_alias`, `collect_marker_trait`, `collect_impl` (block only ŌĆö impl methods are `fn`s and skip the helper). `collect_function` and impl-method walks don't call the helper because the attribute is legal there. **New `ResolveErrorKind::TrackCallerInvalidTarget`** in `src/resolver.rs`; mapped to `E0240` in both `src/cli.rs` error-code tables (the diagnostic-emit path at line 706 and the legacy `resolve_error_code` map at line 2711 ŌĆö both must stay in sync). **Test surface (7 parser tests in `tests/parser.rs`)**: `track_caller_slice1_sets_flag_on_function` (basic ŌĆö attribute presence sets flag); `track_caller_slice1_function_without_attribute_has_flag_false` (regression pin); `track_caller_slice1_coexists_with_other_attributes` (the flag is set when the attribute appears alongside others like `#[must_use = "..."]`); `track_caller_slice1_rejects_paren_args` (negative pin ŌĆö `#[track_caller(extra)]` produces `E_TRACK_CALLER_ARGS_NOT_PERMITTED`); `track_caller_slice1_rejects_string_value` (negative pin ŌĆö `#[track_caller = "oops"]` same diagnostic); `track_caller_slice1_duplicate_attribute_is_idempotent` (two bare copies are silently idempotent at parse ŌĆö pin for the no-duplicate-lint posture); `track_caller_slice1_set_on_non_fn_item_parser_does_not_reject` (the parser captures the attribute on a struct without diagnostic; placement rejection is the resolver's job). **Test surface (10 resolver tests in `tests/resolver.rs`)**: `track_caller_slice1_accepted_on_function` / `..._on_impl_method` (positive pins ŌĆö no diagnostic on the legal `fn` and impl-method placements); `track_caller_slice1_rejected_on_struct` / `..._enum` / `..._trait` / `..._marker_trait` / `..._trait_alias` / `..._impl_block` / `..._struct_field` (rejection at each disallowed site, asserting the kind name appears in the diagnostic so the role is unambiguous); `track_caller_slice1_rejection_uses_dedicated_error_kind` (pin that the new `ResolveErrorKind::TrackCallerInvalidTarget` discriminant is used rather than overloading existing kinds, AND that the message carries the symbolic `E_TRACK_CALLER_INVALID_TARGET` prefix for CLI/IDE consumers). **What slice 1 does *not* do.** No call-site lowering ŌĆö the codegen pass does not yet inject the hidden caller-location argument (slice 4); no panic runtime integration ŌĆö `PanicRecord` doesn't yet read the caller-location parameter (slice 5); no stdlib annotations ŌĆö `Option::unwrap` / `Result::unwrap` / `Vec::index` etc. don't yet carry the attribute (slice 6);
