no `missing_track_caller` lint (slice 7, blocked on lint registry at line 383). **Trait-method support** is a sub-open: the spec accepts the attribute on trait method declarations with last-writer-wins propagation to impls, but `TraitMethod` has no `attributes` field at the AST level yet ŌĆö adding attribute support to trait methods is a separate enabling change that unblocks (a) `#[track_caller]` on trait method declarations, (b) `#[deprecated]` on trait method declarations once that lands (line 381), and (c) the broader `#[diagnostic::*]` / tool-namespaced attribute work (lines 385, 387). The slice-1 parser flag is structurally complete for the function and impl-method cases that cover the spec's stdlib-annotation slice 6. (3) Resolver / typechecker ŌĆö pass through unchanged; the attribute does not affect types, effects, or generic instantiation. (4) Codegen / call lowering ŌĆö for every call site whose callee is `#[track_caller]`, insert a hidden caller-location argument carrying the call site's `(file, line, col)`; if the **enclosing** function is itself `#[track_caller]`, forward its received caller-location parameter instead of the literal call site (transitivity rule); the parameter is ABI-stable within the language but never user-visible. (5) Panic runtime (`std.panic`) ŌĆö when constructing a `PanicRecord`, read the caller-location parameter (if the panicking frame is `#[track_caller]`) and store it as the `site.file`/`site.line`/`site.col` triple of the Crash Report Format Field 1; the demangled function name and instruction pointer continue to identify the actual emitting frame. (6) Stdlib annotations ŌĆö apply `#[track_caller]` to: `Option::unwrap`, `Option::expect`, `Result::unwrap`, `Result::expect`, `Result::unwrap_err`, `Result::expect_err`, `Vec::index` / `Slice::index` / `Array::index` and their `_mut` variants (the bare `[i]` operator desugars onto these), `Vec::first` / `Vec::last` (the panicking variants ŌĆö the `.get()` / `.first_opt()` / `.last_opt()` Option-returning forms do not carry the attribute), the trapping arithmetic helpers (`i64::unchecked_div`, `i64::unchecked_rem`, the `embedded`-profile overflow-trapping named methods), the assertion macros once macros land (`assert!`, `assert_eq!`, `assert_ne!` ŌĆö for v1 the assertion intrinsics in stdlib carry the attribute directly), and the diverging primitives `todo()` / `unreachable()` / `panic()`. (7) Stdlib hygiene lint ŌĆö new `missing_track_caller` lint that fires on any `pub fn` in a `lib.kara` of the standard library whose declared or inferred effect set contains `panics` and which lacks `#[track_caller]`; lint level `deny` for stdlib crates, `allow` for user code. The lint is opt-in for user code (a regular `pub fn foo() with panics` does *not* require the attribute ŌĆö only stdlib panic-emitters do). (8) Built-in operator panics (`a + b` overflow trap under `app`/`lib`, `a / b` div-by-zero trap, exhaustiveness violations the compiler did not statically rule out) already point at the operator's own source location ŌĆö no attribute or codegen change is needed for them; this entry is exclusively about stdlib **function** panic-emitters. Test coverage: `vec.get(99).unwrap()` reports the user's `unwrap()` site as Field 1, not a frame inside `Option::unwrap`; same for `Result::expect("...")`, `Vec[i]` OOB, `i64::unchecked_div(0)`, `panic("msg")`, `todo()`, `unreachable()`; transitivity ŌĆö a user `#[track_caller] fn must_be_pos(x: i32) -> u32 { if x >= 0 { x as u32 } else { panic!(...) } }` called from `caller_fn` reports `caller_fn`'s site, not `must_be_pos`'s; a `#[track_caller]` user fn that calls a `#[track_caller]` stdlib fn reports the *user fn's* caller; a non-`#[track_caller]` fn that calls a `#[track_caller]` stdlib fn reports the call site inside the wrapper (no transitivity); attribute on a non-`fn` item is rejected; attribute with arguments is rejected; trait-method `#[track_caller]` declaration is honoured by impls that don't explicitly drop it; `missing_track_caller` lint fires on a stdlib `pub fn` with `panics` effect that lacks the attribute; the lint does not fire on user-code `pub fn` with `panics`. Phase target: 5.2 (Language Features).

- [x] **AST enabling change ŌĆö attributes on `TraitMethod` + `Variant` nodes shipped 2026-05-17.** Resolves the trait-method-support sub-open flagged in the `#[track_caller]` slice 1 entry (line 391) and the variant/trait-method sub-open flagged in the `#[deprecated]` slices 1+2+3a entry (line 381). Two AST surface extensions in `src/ast/items.rs`: (1) `Variant` gains `attributes: Vec<Attribute>` (defaulted to empty in any synthesized construction) and `deprecation: Option<Deprecation>` ŌĆö the spec's variant-level `#[deprecated]` target now has a place to attach. (2) `TraitMethod` gains `attributes: Vec<Attribute>`, `doc_comment: Option<String>`, `deprecation: Option<Deprecation>`, and `is_track_caller: bool` ŌĆö covering the spec's last-writer-wins propagation rule (the impl-level `Function.is_track_caller` overrides this when set; the codegen slice consults both). **Parser wiring** in `src/parser/items.rs` (`parse_variant` now calls `parse_attributes` after collecting doc comments and threads them through; `scan_deprecated_attr` produces the payload) and `src/parser/items_trait.rs` (`parse_trait_def_tail` now collects per-item attributes before dispatching to `parse_trait_method`; `parse_trait_method` takes `attributes: Vec<Attribute>` as an arg and calls both `scan_track_caller_attr` + `scan_deprecated_attr`). **Visibility change**: `Parser::scan_track_caller_attr` was promoted from `fn` to `pub(crate) fn` so the trait-method parser in the sibling impl block can call it. **Attributes on associated-type declarations** are rejected with the new `E_ATTR_ON_ASSOC_TYPE_DECL` diagnostic ŌĆö `AssocTypeDecl` has no `attributes` field today and the v1 surface explicitly doesn't include them; silently dropping attributes attached to `type Item;` inside a trait body would mask user intent. **Resolver placement-rejection extensions** in `src/resolver/collect.rs`: `collect_enum` now walks `e.variants` and rejects `#[track_caller]` and `#[non_exhaustive]` at each variant (both type-level-only per spec). `collect_trait` walks `t.items` and rejects `#[non_exhaustive]` on each `TraitItem::Method`; `#[track_caller]` and `#[deprecated]` are accepted on trait methods (both legal targets per spec). **Test surface (9 parser tests in `tests/parser.rs`)**: `enabling_change_variant_captures_attributes` (basic positive ŌĆö `#[deprecated]` on a variant attaches and populates the payload); `enabling_change_variant_bare_deprecated_attaches`; `enabling_change_trait_method_captures_attributes`; `enabling_change_trait_method_track_caller_attaches` (the headline ŌĆö `#[track_caller]` on a trait method declaration now sets `is_track_caller = true`); `enabling_change_trait_method_doc_comment_captured` (regression pin ŌĆö doc comments before a trait method now attach); `enabling_change_attr_on_assoc_type_decl_rejected` (E_ATTR_ON_ASSOC_TYPE_DECL negative pin); `enabling_change_unsafe_fn_in_trait_with_attribute` (the `unsafe fn` dispatch in the trait body must thread attributes through, not lose them); `enabling_change_attr_on_tuple_variant` / `..._struct_variant` (the attribute attaches to every variant kind, not just unit variants). **Test surface (6 resolver tests in `tests/resolver.rs`)**: `enabling_change_track_caller_on_enum_variant_rejected`; `enabling_change_non_exhaustive_on_enum_variant_rejected`; `enabling_change_non_exhaustive_on_trait_method_rejected`; `enabling_change_track_caller_on_trait_method_accepted` (the spec's "trait method declarations are accepted" positive pin); `enabling_change_deprecated_on_enum_variant_accepted` (the spec's variant-level deprecation positive pin); `enabling_change_deprecated_on_trait_method_accepted`. **What this entry does *not* do.** No codegen ŌĆö the `is_track_caller` flag on `TraitMethod` is structurally captured but the codegen pass doesn't yet propagate it to impl methods at synthesis time (that's slice 4 of the `#[track_caller]` entry at line 391). Those AST nodes are smaller surface than `Variant`/`TraitMethod` (no nested items to walk) but still touch every existing pass that walks them; tracked as a follow-up.

Both functions call `scan_deprecated_attr` and store the payload on the AST node. **Resolver placement validation** in `src/resolver/collect.rs`: `collect_const` and `collect_type_alias` both call `reject_non_exhaustive_attr(attrs, "module const" / "type alias")` and `reject_track_caller_attr(attrs, ...)` ŌĆö neither attribute is legal on these item kinds (`#[non_exhaustive]` is type-level only on `pub struct` / `pub enum`; `#[track_caller]` is fn-only). `#[deprecated]` is accepted on both (spec-listed targets); no rejection helper is called for it. **Test surface (5 parser tests + 6 resolver tests)** covering positive payload capture, regression pins (no attribute ŌåÆ empty field), the long-form deprecation shape, and the four cross-product rejection sites. **What this entry does *not* do.** No use-site `#[deprecated]` warning emission on consts / type aliases (still blocked on lint emission infrastructure ŌĆö slice 4 of the lint-level-attributes entry at line 385). The parser-captured `deprecation` field is structurally complete; the warning emission will read it once the cascade infrastructure lands.

- [x] **Identifier case-class enforcement.** Enforce the case-class rule specified in `design.md ┬¦ Identifiers and Naming`. Lexer classifies each `Ident` token as Type / Const / Value by its character pattern (see `syntax.md ┬¦1.5`). Parser checks the class at every declaration site ŌĆö `struct` / `enum` / `trait` / `type` / `distinct` / generic param / const generic param / associated type / `effect resource` require Type-class; `fn` / function-body `let` / param / field / `mod` / `layout` / effect group / effect verb require Value-class; `const` requires Const-class. Mismatch emits a structured diagnostic with position-aware wording and a suggested rename. `#[kara_name = "..."]` attribute on `extern` items provides the FFI escape hatch (CN-7). Non-ASCII identifiers remain a parse error (Unicode deferred). No-op for existing codebase ŌĆö all current K─üra source already follows the convention. Test coverage for every site in `tests/parser.rs` (snake_case struct/enum/variant/trait/type-alias rejected, PascalCase fn/param/field/extern-fn rejected, snake_case const-generic/assoc-type/generic-param rejected, PascalCase layout name rejected, single-upper Type-class accepted, leading-underscore Value-class accepted, `#[kara_name]` skip-check accepted, let-binding deferred to resolver).

- [ ] **`#[profile(P1, P2, ...)]` attribute.** Function/module attribute asserting compatibility with a specific set of project profiles. Compile error if the function's transitive effect set isn't compatible with the *intersection* of the listed profiles' constraints (function must satisfy the strictest constraint from any listed profile). Parser: recognize `#[profile(...)]` with comma-separated profile name list. Resolver: validate names against profiles defined in `kara.toml`; unknown names are a parse-level diagnostic. Effect checker: per-call enforcement of the intersected constraint set. Not viral ŌĆö effects already propagate transitively through inference, so the local check is sufficient. Stdlib `core` layer is the first major user; portability marking becomes structural rather than convention-based. The attribute name `profile` is chosen over `profile_compatible` for consistency with `kara.toml`'s `profiles = [...]` vocabulary.

- [x] **C-string literals `c"..."` ŌĆö lex acceptance.** Spec lives at design.md ┬¦ C-String Literals (v60 item 18). Today the lexer rejects `c"..."` with a focused diagnostic that points at the spec ("specced for v1 but lex acceptance lands in Phase 5.2"); the work here is to graduate the prefix from rejected to recognized. Sub-steps: (1) `Token::CStringLiteral { bytes: Vec<u8>, source_len: i64 }` variant in `src/token.rs` ŌĆö `bytes` excludes the trailing NUL (the codegen layer appends it); `source_len` records the textual length for `len()` / `as_bytes()` introspection without re-walking. (2) Lexer dispatch arm ŌĆö add `b'c' if self.peek() == b'"' => self.c_string()` between the existing `f"`-arm and the reserved-prefix catch-all. (3) `c_string()` method ŌĆö body parsing identical to `string()` plus the `\xHH` hex-byte escape (already implemented for byte-literals, lift the helper); `\u{...}` Unicode escapes encode to UTF-8 bytes. (4) Interior-NUL guard ŌĆö any escape that produces a `0x00` byte (`\0`, `\x00`, `\u{0}`) is a lex error `error[E_INTERIOR_NUL_IN_C_STRING]` with the message from design.md, pointing at the offending escape. (5) Update the existing `test_v60_reserved_string_prefix_diagnostic` in `tests/lexer.rs` to drop the Phase-5.2-gating diagnostic and add positive lex tests for the new token shape (empty, ASCII, escape sequences, Unicode escapes producing multi-byte UTF-8). Parser handling and the stdlib `CStr` / `CString` types ship in Phase 8 (see follow-up entry below); this Phase 5.2 entry is lex-level only. (Phase 5.2 ŌĆö items 3, 18, 22 land together as the FFI-tightening cluster.)

- [ ] **Field offsets `offset_of[T](field)` + `ptr.container_of` / `ptr.container_of_mut`.** Spec lives at design.md ┬¦ Field Offsets (v60 item 25). Sub-steps: (1) Parser/typechecker ŌĆö recognise `offset_of` followed by `[TYPE](FIELD_PATH)` as a special call form during expression-call lowering, where `FIELD_PATH = IDENT ("." IDENT)*`. The argument is parsed as a dotted identifier sequence, NOT as an expression ŌĆö expression forms (indexing, method calls, dereferences) inside the parens are rejected at parse with `error[E_OFFSET_OF_INVALID_PATH]`. The typechecker resolves the path against `T`'s field namespace segment by segment, descending into struct field types. The result type is `usize`. (2) Field-resolution rules ŌĆö unknown field at any segment produces `error[E_OFFSET_OF_UNKNOWN_FIELD]` with the offending segment underlined and the available fields enumerated; private field accessed from outside the defining module produces `error[E_OFFSET_OF_PRIVATE_FIELD]`; non-struct target (enum variant, opaque foreign type, generic type parameter without concrete instantiation) produces a focused diagnostic per kind (`E_OFFSET_OF_ENUM_VARIANT`, `E_OFFSET_OF_OPAQUE_TYPE`, `E_OFFSET_OF_GENERIC_PARAM`); union field produces `warning[W_OFFSET_OF_UNION_FIELD]` (call accepted, returns 0). (3) Const-evaluator ŌĆö when `T` and the field path are statically resolvable, the call is a compile-time constant computed from the existing layout machinery (the same code path that powers `size_of` / `align_of`); the result is usable in const-generic argument position, `static` initializers, and match-arm guards. (4) Layout-block interaction ŌĆö for structs carrying a `layout` block with SoA transformation, the returned offset is the *runtime* (post-transformation) offset, not the logical pre-transformation offset; for `#[repr(C)]` structs (where SoA is disabled), logical and physical layouts coincide. (5) Stdlib `ptr.container_of` / `ptr.container_of_mut` ŌĆö generic functions in the prelude `ptr` module: `unsafe fn container_of[T, F](field_ptr: *const F, field: <field-path>) -> *const T` (and the `_mut` variant). The `field` argument uses the same special-form field-path syntax as `offset_of`. Implementation lowers to `field_ptr.with_addr(field_ptr.addr() - offset_of[T](field))`, leveraging the strict-provenance APIs from item 20 to keep the address arithmetic provenance-preserving. The `unsafe` marker carries the precondition "field_ptr actually points at the named field of an enclosing T". (6) Codegen ŌĆö offset_of compiles to a literal const usize at every call site; no runtime arithmetic is emitted. The container_of helpers compile to the same LLVM IR sequence the strict-provenance APIs already emit. Test plan: positive ŌĆö `offset_of[UsbDescriptor](descriptor_type)` returns 1 with `#[repr(C)]` padding rules; nested path `offset_of[Outer](inner.y)` resolves through two struct layers; const-eval round-trip into `Array[u8, offset_of[Frame](payload)]`; layout-block-transformed struct returns the runtime offset; container_of round-trip recovers the enclosing struct pointer; transparent carrier returns 0; private-field rejection from outside the defining module. Negative ŌĆö unknown field rejected; expression-form arg `offset_of[T](field[0])` parser-rejected; opaque foreign type rejected; bare generic type param `T` rejected; enum variant `offset_of[E.V](field)` parser-rejected. (Phase 5.2 ŌĆö typechecker work; depends on the layout-resolution pipeline already used by `size_of` / `align_of`.)

- [ ] **Strict-provenance pointer APIs `ptr.addr` / `ptr.with_addr` / `ptr.expose` / `ptr.from_exposed`.** Spec lives at design.md ┬¦ Pointer Provenance (v60 item 20). Sub-steps: (1) Stdlib `ptr` module ŌĆö generic functions `addr[T](p: *const T) -> usize`, `with_addr[T](p: *const T, addr: usize) -> *const T`, `with_addr_mut[T](p: *mut T, addr: usize) -> *mut T`, `expose[T](p: *const T) -> usize`, `expose_mut[T](p: *mut T) -> usize`, plus the unsafe `from_exposed[T](addr: usize) -> *const T` and `from_exposed_mut[T](addr: usize) -> *mut T`. No special parsing ŌĆö these are ordinary `ptr`-module method calls; only `ptr.const` / `ptr.mut` are place-form special cases. (2) Cast-rejection ŌĆö extend the existing `as`-cast typechecker (sibling to the `&T ŌåÆ *const T` rejection) to reject all four `ptr Ōåö usize` casts: `*const T as usize` / `*mut T as usize` produce `error[E_PTR_TO_INT_CAST_FORBIDDEN]` with a suggested-fix span offering `ptr.addr(p)` (the safer default ŌĆö the diagnostic message also names `ptr.expose` for the round-trip case); `usize as *const T` / `usize as *mut T` produce `error[E_INT_TO_PTR_CAST_FORBIDDEN]` with no auto-suggested-fix (the choice between `ptr.with_addr` and `ptr.from_exposed` depends on whether a base pointer is in scope). (3) Codegen ŌĆö `addr` and `with_addr` lower to LLVM `ptrtoint` / `inttoptr` with provenance-preserving metadata (specifically `!provenance.preserve` markers when LLVM IR supports them; otherwise plain `inttoptr` with the existing alias-analysis annotations); `expose` and `from_exposed` lower to the same instructions but mark the source pointer as having escaped via `noalias` invalidation. The unsafe marker on `from_exposed` is a typecheck-only check (parser/typechecker enforces the `unsafe { }` requirement); codegen treats both equally. Test plan: positive ŌĆö read-back via `addr` matches the original pointer's address bits; `with_addr(p, addr(p) | 1)` produces a tagged pointer that round-trips through `with_addr(_, _ & !1)`; `expose` followed by `from_exposed` round-trips a stored address; the `from_exposed` call must sit inside `unsafe { }` (parser/typechecker rejects bare-call form). Negative ŌĆö the four forbidden casts each produce their respective focused diagnostic; raw-to-raw casts (`*const T as *mut T`) and integer-to-integer casts (`usize as i64`) remain unaffected; `addr` and `expose` are accepted in safe code; `from_exposed` is rejected in safe code with `error[E_UNSAFE_OUTSIDE_UNSAFE_BLOCK]`. (Phase 5.2 ŌĆö typechecker work; codegen substrate ships with Phase 7.)

- [ ] **Opaque foreign types ŌĆö `extern "C" { type Foo; }`.** Spec lives at design.md ┬¦ Opaque Foreign Types (v60 item 24). Sub-steps: (1) Parser ŌĆö extend the `unsafe extern "ABI" { ... }` block grammar so each item may be either a foreign-function declaration (existing) or an opaque-type declaration `type IDENT ;` (new). Reject generic forms `type Foo[T];` at parse with `error[E_OPAQUE_TYPE_GENERIC_FORBIDDEN]`. AST: new `ExternItem::OpaqueType { name, attrs, vis, span }`. (2) Resolver ŌĆö register the opaque type name in the type namespace at the enclosing module's level (visibility from the declaration). Multiple declarations of the same opaque-type name across blocks/files emit `warning[W_OPAQUE_TYPE_REDECLARED]` rather than an error ŌĆö the C side has the final word; duplicate declarations are noisy but not unsound. (3) Typechecker ŌĆö model opaque types as a new `Type::OpaqueExtern { name, ... }` variant with sizing flag `Sized = false`. The pointer-only constraint is enforced at every use site: a place or value of opaque-extern type that is *not* behind `*const T` / `*mut T` / `ref T` / `mut ref T` is rejected with `error[E_OPAQUE_TYPE_REQUIRES_INDIRECTION]` (covers by-value lets, by-value parameters, by-value returns, struct fields, array element types, and any other non-indirect occurrence). Field access and method calls on a value of opaque-extern type are rejected with `error[E_OPAQUE_TYPE_NO_FIELDS]` / `error[E_OPAQUE_TYPE_NO_METHODS]`. `size_of[Foo]()` and `align_of[Foo]()` are rejected with `error[E_OPAQUE_TYPE_NO_KNOWN_SIZE]`. `impl ... for Foo` (inherent or trait) blocks are rejected with `error[E_OPAQUE_TYPE_NO_INHERENT_OR_TRAIT_IMPLS]` ŌĆö the wrapper-type pattern (`distinct type SafeFile = *mut FILE; impl Drop for SafeFile { ... }`) is the supported alternative. `#[derive(...)]` is rejected with the same diagnostic family. `ptr.const(...)` / `ptr.mut(...)` on an opaque-type place fails the place-validator with the standard E_PTR_CONST_REQUIRES_PLACE diagnostic ŌĆö a place of opaque type cannot exist in the first place because by-value bindings are forbidden. (4) Codegen ŌĆö opaque-extern types lower to LLVM's incomplete struct type (`%struct.Foo = type opaque`), used only as the pointee in `*const T` / `*mut T` types; no allocation or memory operation is ever emitted on an opaque type directly. (5) Effect integration ŌĆö opaque type declarations contribute no effects; functions in the same `unsafe extern { }` block that take or return pointers to the opaque type follow the standard FFI effect-declaration rules. (6) Linker integration ŌĆö opaque-type declarations emit no linker symbols (the type is the C side's; only function bindings produce import symbols). Test plan: positive ŌĆö `extern "C" { type FILE; }` plus `fopen`/`fclose` signatures parse, type-check, and round-trip a `*mut FILE` through K─üra code; the `SafeFile` wrapper-type pattern compiles; the same opaque type declared twice (different files) emits the redeclare warning and resolves to one type. Negative ŌĆö by-value `let f: FILE = ...` rejected; by-value parameter `fn f(x: FILE)` rejected; field-of-struct `struct S { f: FILE }` rejected; field access `(*ptr).x` where ptr: *mut FILE is rejected (no fields known); `size_of[FILE]()` rejected; `impl Display for FILE` rejected; `extern "C" { type Foo[T]; }` parser-rejected; `#[derive(Debug)] type FILE` rejected. (Phase 5.2 ŌĆö typechecker work; lexer/parser change lands together. Items 3, 18, 22, 24 cluster together as the FFI-tightening cluster.)

- [ ] **FFI unions ŌĆö `union Foo { ... }`.** Spec lives at design.md ┬¦ FFI Unions (v60 item 22). Sub-steps: (1) Lexer ŌĆö add `union` to the keyword arm in `src/lexer.rs` (currently a free identifier). The keyword token kind is unconditional; there is no contextual-keyword treatment because every legitimate use is at item position. (2) Parser ŌĆö accept `UNION_DEF` per syntax.md ┬¦ 3.3a alongside `STRUCT_DEF` and `ENUM_DEF`. AST: new `Item::Union { name, attrs, vis, fields, span }` variant carrying a `Vec<UnionField { name, ty, vis, span }>`. Reject empty fields-list at parse with `error[E_EMPTY_UNION]`. Reject tuple-style (`union Foo(T, U)`) and generic (`union Foo[T] { ... }`) forms at parse ŌĆö neither has a v1 use case. (3) Resolver ŌĆö register `Foo` in the type namespace; resolve field types in the enclosing scope. (4) Typechecker ŌĆö required-`#[repr(C)]` check at union-decl time produces `error[E_UNION_REQUIRES_REPR]` if absent (also accepts `#[repr(C, packed)]`). Per-field `Copy`/`Pod` bound check produces `error[E_UNION_FIELD_NOT_COPY]` naming the offending field's type. Reject `impl Drop for Foo` on a union type (`error[E_UNION_DROP_FORBIDDEN]`). Reject `#[derive(...)]` on a union (`error[E_UNION_DERIVE_FORBIDDEN]` ŌĆö the diagnostic enumerates the rejected derives). Reject `#[non_exhaustive]` (`error[E_UNION_NON_EXHAUSTIVE_FORBIDDEN]`). Construction-literal check: exactly one field name in the literal (`error[E_UNION_LITERAL_REQUIRES_ONE_FIELD]` for zero or multiple). Field-access check: a union field read or pattern-bind requires `unsafe { }` (`error[E_UNION_READ_REQUIRES_UNSAFE]`); a `&u.field` / `&mut u.field` borrow likewise (`error[E_UNION_BORROW_REQUIRES_UNSAFE]`); a field assignment is unconditionally safe; `ptr.const(u.field)` / `ptr.mut(u.field)` are safe (they don't read the bytes ŌĆö the place-expression validator already permits union field paths). (5) Layout ŌĆö codegen lowers a `#[repr(C)] union Foo { ... }` to LLVM's storage with `size = max(field_sizes)`, `align = max(field_aligns)`, size rounded up to a multiple of `align`. The field-`Copy` constraint means no destructors are emitted for unions; layout-block syntax is rejected on union types (no SoA transformation makes sense). (6) Effect integration ŌĆö union field reads contribute no effects to the enclosing function's inferred set; the surrounding `unsafe { }` block carries the language-level safety load. If a hardware effect is in play (volatile MMIO read interpreted as a union field), the effect is captured by the existing `volatile_read` / `reads(Hardware)` machinery, not by union semantics. (7) Cross-`extern` use ŌĆö no special handling beyond what `#[repr(C) struct]` already does; `extern "C"` signatures may name union types as parameters, returns, or struct fields. Test plan: positive ŌĆö `#[repr(C)] union FloatBits { f: f32, bits: u32 }` parses, type-checks, and round-trips bit-pattern reads/writes; `epoll_data` example from design.md compiles in a stub `unsafe extern "C" { }` block; `size_of[FloatBits]()` reports the larger field's size; `align_of[FloatBits]()` reports the larger field's alignment. Negative ŌĆö bare `union Foo { ... }` without `#[repr]` is rejected; `union Foo { v: Vec[i32] }` (Vec is not Copy) is rejected; `impl Drop for FloatBits` is rejected; `#[derive(Eq)] union Foo { ... }` is rejected; safe-context `let v = u.bits;` is rejected; `let FloatBits { bits } = u;` outside `unsafe { }` is rejected; literal `FloatBits { f: 1.0, bits: 1 }` is rejected; literal `FloatBits {}` is rejected. (Phase 5.2 ŌĆö typechecker work; depends on `#[repr]` and Pod/Copy bound infrastructure being stable. Lexer change lands together. Items 3, 18, 22 cluster together as the FFI-tightening cluster.)

- [ ] **Raw pointer construction `ptr.const` / `ptr.mut`.** Spec lives at design.md ┬¦ Raw Pointer Construction (v60 item 19). Sub-steps: (1) Parser/typechecker ŌĆö recognise `ptr` `.const` `(...)` and `ptr` `.mut` `(...)` as a special call form during expression-call lowering; the argument is parsed as an ordinary expression but routed through a *place-expression* validator at typecheck time rather than the value-expression typecheck. Place-expression validity matches the existing borrow-rooting rules (binding, field access, index, deref, projection chains over those); a non-place argument produces `error[E_PTR_CONST_REQUIRES_PLACE]` / `error[E_PTR_MUT_REQUIRES_PLACE]`. The `mut` form additionally checks that the place is mutably reachable using the same logic as `mut ref` borrow checking; failure produces `error[E_PTR_MUT_REQUIRES_MUTABLE_PLACE]`. The result type is `*const T` / `*mut T` where `T` is the place's type. (2) Cast-rejection ŌĆö extend the existing `as`-cast typechecker to reject `&T as *const U` and `&mut T as *mut U` with `error[E_REF_TO_RAW_PTR_CAST_FORBIDDEN]`; the diagnostic includes a suggested-fix span replacing the cast with `ptr.const(...)` / `ptr.mut(...)` and points at the `as` operator. Casts between raw-pointer types (`*const T as *mut T`, etc.) remain unaffected ŌĆö only the `&T ŌåÆ *_ T` origin cast is forbidden. (3) Stdlib `ptr` module ŌĆö generic functions `null[T]() -> *const T`, `null_mut[T]() -> *mut T`, `dangling[T]() -> *const T`, `dangling_mut[T]() -> *mut T`, `is_null[T](p: *const T) -> bool`. These are ordinary stdlib items with no special parsing ŌĆö only `ptr.const` / `ptr.mut` are place-form special cases. (4) Local-binding shadowing ŌĆö a local binding named `ptr` shadows the prelude module within its scope; in that case `ptr.const(...)` parses as a method call on the local, and the special-form recognition does *not* fire. The standard prelude-shadow lint (warn-by-default) flags the shadow. Test plan: positive `ptr.const(local_binding)`, `ptr.const(struct_field)`, `ptr.mut(arr[i])`, `ptr.const(*ref_binding)`; rejection on value expressions (`ptr.const(x + 1)` ŌĆö not a place); rejection on immutable place under `ptr.mut`; rejection of `&v as *const T`; passthrough of `*const T as *mut T`. Construction is *safe* ŌĆö no `unsafe { }` block required for `ptr.const(...)` itself; only dereference, arithmetic, unaligned/volatile, and pointee-changing casts trip the unsafe rule. (Phase 5.2 ŌĆö typechecker work; depends on the existing borrow-rooting / mutable-place infrastructure being stable.)

- [ ] **C-string literals ŌĆö parser + stdlib `CStr` / `CString` types.** Follow-up to the Phase 5.2 lex-acceptance entry above. Sub-steps: (1) Parser ŌĆö accept `Token::CStringLiteral` in expression position, lower to a literal AST node carrying the bytes and source length. (2) Typechecker ŌĆö assign type `ref CStr` with `'static` lifetime to the literal expression; `CStr` resolves to a stdlib type (Phase 8). (3) Stdlib `CStr` ŌĆö unsized type `[u8]`-shaped with the trailing-NUL invariant; methods `as_ptr(ref self) -> *const u8`, `len(ref self) -> i64`, `is_empty(ref self) -> bool`, `as_bytes(ref self) -> Slice[u8]`, `to_string_slice(ref self) -> Result[StringSlice, Utf8Error]`, `to_string(ref self) -> Result[String, Utf8Error]`. (4) Stdlib `CString` ŌĆö owning heap-allocated counterpart; constructed via `String.to_cstring(ref self) -> Result[CString, NulError]` and `Slice[u8].to_cstring(ref self) -> Result[CString, NulError]`; `as_ptr` / `len` / `is_empty` / `as_bytes` mirror `CStr`. (5) `unsafe`-only constructor `CStr.from_raw(ptr: *const u8) -> ref CStr` for runtime-borrowed C strings (walks to terminating NUL at `O(N)` per the spec). Test plan: round-trip via FFI through a stub `extern "C" fn strlen(s: *const u8) -> usize`; `to_string_slice` on UTF-8 and non-UTF-8 inputs; `to_cstring` rejection on interior-NUL `String`. Depends on the Phase 7.2 stdlib codegen substrate landing first. (Phase 8.)

### 5.3: Advanced Diagnostics

- [x] **`--output=jsonl` streaming mode.** Newline-delimited JSON, six event types (`build_start`, `phase_start`, `phase_complete`, `phase_skipped`, `diagnostic`, `build_complete`). Strict superset of `--output=json`. See design.md ┬¦ AI-First Compiler Interface > 1b. Streaming Phase Events.

- [x] **Error return traces.** Ring buffer (depth 64) at each `?` site. `"error_return_trace"` field in JSON output. Pushed on `Err`/`None` propagation, cleared on `Ok`/`Some`. Truncation flag set when buffer is full.

- [x] **Enhanced per-SCC effect diagnostics.** Tarjan's SCC algorithm detects mutual recursion groups. `"mutual_recursion_groups"` JSON field includes full effect resolution trace ŌĆö which call site resolved which effect through which callee. See [deferred.md ┬¦ Per-SCC Effect Diagnostics](deferred.md#per-scc-effect-diagnostics).

- [x] **`karac query` subcommands.** `karac query effects` (inferred + declared effects), `karac query ownership` (parameter modes, RC values).

- [x] **`karac query cost-summary` (static counts).** Per-function and per-module table of every silent runtime cost the compiler emitted: RC ops (Rc/Arc), Arc-provider-wraps, borrow-flag fields, partition-guard sites, auto-clone insertions. Each category aggregates into `totals` and breaks down per-function with a `derivation` array of source locations. v1 is static counts only ŌĆö runtime attribution (sampling-profiler-driven %wall-clock against a real workload) is post-v1. Closed 2026-05-01 ŌĆö see WIP block above for landed-implementation details. v1 wires `rc_ops` (per-function from the ownership pass), `arc_provider_wraps` (per-function `with_provider[R]` AST sites), and `borrow_flag_fields` (totals-only over `shared struct` `mut` fields); `partition_guard_sites` and `auto_clone_insertions` ship as `0` until parameterized resources and the REPL `--auto-clone` flag respectively land ŌĆö schema reserves the keys so post-v1 wiring is purely additive. Codegen-time wiring of additional cost sites (e.g. tighter Arc-provider-wrap accounting once Phase 7 lowering tracks per-call closure-boundary crossings) can refine the static counts; the surface stays the same.

- [x] **`ffi_float_eq` lint.** Ō£ō DONE (2026-04-27) ŌĆö `src/ffi_lint.rs`: `check_ffi_float_eq(program)` collects all `extern "C"` function names that return `f32`/`f64`, then walks for `BinOp::Eq`/`NotEq` where either operand is a direct call to one of those functions. Wired into `cmd_run` in `cli.rs`. 6 tests in `tests/ffi_lint.rs`. Indirect patterns (via let-binding) not tracked ŌĆö requires DFA.

- [x] **`undocumented_unsafe` lint.** Ō£ō DONE (2026-04-27) ŌĆö `src/unsafe_lint.rs`: `check_undocumented_unsafe(program, source)` walks the AST for `ExprKind::Unsafe` nodes; checks the line immediately before the `unsafe` keyword in the raw source text for `// Safety:` (case-insensitive). `#[allow(undocumented_unsafe)]` on the enclosing function suppresses; `#[deny(undocumented_unsafe)]` escalates to error. Wired into `cmd_run` in `cli.rs` (text output mode). 8 tests in `tests/unsafe_lint.rs`. Note: `unsafe fn` not yet a syntactic form; lint only covers `unsafe { }` blocks. ~~`unsafe fn` doc-comment `# Safety` section check and one-time doc pass deferred.~~

- [x] **Empty prefix-literal diagnostic ŌĆö `Vec[]` / `Array[]` / `Set[]` / `Map[]` without binding annotation.** Per `design.md ┬¦ Collection Literals` (line 1462), an empty prefix-literal has no element type to infer and requires a binding annotation. Today the typechecker accepts empty literals in check mode (the binding's expected type drives recovery ŌĆö see `phase-8-stdlib-floor.md ┬¦ Set[T] LLVM codegen` subtask 8 for the `Set[]` case; `Vec[]` / `Array[]` / `Map[]` follow the same pattern), but synthesis-mode use (no enclosing annotation) currently surfaces a generic `Type::Error` rather than a focused message. Slices: (1) Typechecker ŌĆö at the `infer_expr` arm for `ExprKind::PrefixCollectionLiteral { items: [] }`, detect synthesis-mode entry (no expected type threaded from `check`) and emit `error[E_EMPTY_PREFIX_LITERAL_NEEDS_ANNOTATION]` naming the literal kind. (2) Diagnostic body ŌĆö `cannot infer element type from empty 'Vec[]' literal ŌĆö add a binding annotation: 'let v: Vec[T] = Vec[]'`, with per-kind annotation skeletons (`Vec[T]`, `Array[T, 0]`, `Set[T]`, `Map[K, V]`); the fix-it offers both the annotated-literal form and the corresponding constructor (`Vec.new()` / `Set.new()` / `Map.new()`) per design.md line 1470. (3) Check-mode unchanged ŌĆö annotated binding, typed call argument, typed struct-field initializer continue to recover via the expected type with no diagnostic. Test coverage: bare `let x = Vec[];` / `Array[]` / `Set[]` / `Map[]` each rejected with the per-kind diagnostic; annotated forms continue to typecheck (regression ŌĆö `test_set_prefix_literal_empty_with_annotation` already exists for `Set`; add `Vec` / `Array` / `Map` counterparts); typed call-arg and struct-field positions with empty literals accepted. Phase target: 5.3 (typechecker diagnostic emission only; no parser / resolver / AST changes). Closes `phase-4-interpreter.md` line 10.

- [ŌåÆ P1] **`karac explain --format=json` ŌĆö structured diagnostics.** Machine-parseable diagnostic output with a finite error-class enum, typed `expected` / `got` fields, and ranked candidate patches. The MVP `karac explain` ships human-readable prose only; the JSON format adds an opt-in machine-consumable shape for LLM agents and IDE tooling. Class enum freezes once the diagnostic catalogue has matured (~20+ entries). Full design in [`docs/deferred.md` ┬¦ P1 ┬¦ Structured Diagnostics and Error Class Enum](deferred.md#structured-diagnostics-and-error-class-enum-karac-explain---formatjson).

- [ŌåÆ P1] **Signature-from-call-site stub diagnostic.** When the resolver hits an unresolved-identifier *call* inside a `_test.kara` file, enrich the existing `unresolved identifier` diagnostic with a `hints[].diff` entry that proposes a stub function in the sibling production file with parameter types inferred from the call's argument expressions, return type inferred from `assert_eq` / `==` comparison context, and a `todo()` body. Implementation picks the inference layer (resolver-time best-effort vs. post-typecheck refinement) based on quality bar; the diagnostic shape is identical at either layer. Activation gated to `_test.kara` files only ŌĆö production-file unresolved calls keep the plain diagnostic. Reuses the `karac test --init` compiling-skeleton convention for `todo()` bodies. Full design in [`docs/deferred.md` ┬¦ P1 ┬¦ Signature-from-Call-Site Stub Diagnostic](deferred.md#signature-from-call-site-stub-diagnostic).

- [ŌåÆ P1] **`karac catalog` ŌĆö public API surface index.** Subcommand that indexes every exported item (fully qualified name, kind, generic parameters with bounds, parameter modes and types, return type, declared effect row, refinement constraints, source span) and emits JSONL for downstream consumers (LLM agents, IDE plugins, doc generators). Public surface only; private items have inferred reported-tier effect rows that are not stable enough to index. Full design in [`docs/deferred.md` ┬¦ P1 ┬¦ Signature Catalog](deferred.md#signature-catalog-karac-catalog).

- [ŌåÆ P1] **`karac query affected-by` ŌĆö call-graph reach query.** New `karac query` subcommand that exposes the compiler's call graph (already computed for effect inference) as a queryable surface. Given a file:line range or fully-qualified function path, returns the transitive callers, callees, and reaching test functions as JSONL with `--tests-only` and `--direction=callees|callers|all` filters. Structural prerequisite for the test-selection flags (`--related FILE`, `--since REV`) in the `karac tdd` watch driver and the `coverage_delta` event in `karac test --coverage` ŌĆö without it, both features ship with reduced functionality. Implementation extends the existing query infrastructure (`karac query effects` / `ownership` / `concurrency` already shipped) by surfacing the existing graph traversals as a public JSONL surface; engineering well-understood (no research questions). Full design in [`docs/deferred.md` ┬¦ P1 ┬¦ karac query affected-by](deferred.md#karac-query-affected-by--call-graph-reach-query).

### 5.4: Interactive REPL and Jupyter Kernel

First-class interactive surface. **v0 ŌåÆ v1 transition:** the MVP REPL shipped 2026-04-28 on top of the tree-walk interpreter; the v62 lock (2026-05-06) moved the runtime backend to **always-JIT via LLJIT** for v1, with tree-walk retained only as a dev/debug tool. See `design.md ┬¦ Execution Model and Compilation Targets` and the LLJIT integration entry in `phase-7-codegen.md` for the migration work; the user-facing surface (meta-commands, session model, cross-cell semantics) is unchanged by the backend swap. **Delivery split:** the REPL binary and the browser playground are P0 delivery ŌĆö both optimize the frictionless first-try path that drives adoption. The Jupyter kernel is P0 priority (committed, designed, scoped) but P1 delivery ŌĆö timed to ship once the stdlib is stable enough that a first-time notebook user does not hit "function not found" on common types. Semantics (cell scope, ownership across cells, effect display) are now specified in `docs/design.md ┬¦ Interactive Evaluation Model`.

**P0 delivery ŌĆö ships in v1.**

- [~] **`karac repl` binary.** MVP shipped 2026-04-28 ŌĆö line-based REPL over the tree-walk interpreter with meta-commands `:help`, `:quit` (`/`:q`/`:exit`), `:type <expr>`, `:effects`, `:save <path>`. Items accumulate in `Session.items_source`; statement-style cells run inside a synthetic `fn main()` wrapper. New `Session::evaluate_cell_captured` test API surfaces the interpreter's `captured_output` so tests don't need to wrestle with the process's stdout fd. 13 integration tests + 7 unit tests. Open follow-ups: see the next two entries (persistent `let` bindings, cross-cell item shadowing) plus the existing standalone entries below for `--auto-clone`, the notebook-aware use-after-move diagnostic, and session export.

- [~] **`karac repl` follow-up: persistent statement-level bindings across cells.** Closed 2026-05-01 with the option-(a) source-replay model ŌĆö `Session.persistent_lets` accumulates verbatim `let` source slices, prepended to every subsequent synthetic `fn main()` body, with shadow-pruning before parse so re-binding the same name across cells works. See WIP block above for landed-implementation details. The `[~]` (vs `[x]`) marker reflects that the spec's "value persists" semantics are only approximated: RHS re-runs each cell (the side-effect caveat documented in `:help` and the module docs). Option-(b) value-snapshot semantics ŌĆö interpreter exposing an "extend session" entry point so prior `Value`s carry forward instead of being recomputed ŌĆö is the right long-term shape and still tracked, but the v1 source-replay form covers the common notebook-style `let x = literal; ŌĆ” println(x);` flow without interpreter surgery. Files: `src/repl.rs`, `tests/repl.rs`.

- [x] **`karac repl` follow-up: cross-cell item re-declaration shadowing.** Closed 2026-05-01 with `prune_shadowed_items` ŌĆö see WIP block above for landed-implementation details. The implementation took the AST-driven path (re-parse the buffer, identify each item's byte range via `item_span`, splice out names re-declared by the new cell) rather than the originally-suggested generalized `strip_main` brace-balance walk. AST-driven is more robust against attribute/visibility/doc-comment placement and handles every named item kind (`fn` / `struct` / `enum` / `trait` / `const` / `extern fn` / `type` alias / `distinct type` / `layout` / `effect resource` / `effect group` / `effect verb`) uniformly; anonymous items (`impl` blocks, `use` / `import`, `independent`, `alias`) have no shadowable name and are never pruned. The previously `#[ignore]`d `redeclaring_item_across_cells_shadows` test is now active.

- [x] **Notebook-aware use-after-move diagnostic.** Closed 2026-05-08. When the REPL detects a use-after-move spanning cells, the diagnostic renders a hint naming the consuming cell and suggesting `.clone()` at the call site ŌĆö not an auto-clone insertion. Strictness identical to `.kara` files; only the diagnostic presentation differs. See `design.md ┬¦ Interactive Evaluation Model > Ownership Across Cells`.

- [x] **`--auto-clone` opt-in mode.** Closed 2026-05-08. `karac repl --auto-clone` flag enables 2B-style ergonomics: `.clone()` inserted at the consume site when the binding is referenced in a later cell; emits `perf[auto-clone-in-repl]` note. Never silent. Inserted clones appear verbatim in session export.

- [ ] **Session export ŌĆö `.kara` fidelity.** `:save session.kara` writes the session's cell history as a single `.kara` file wrapping the history in `fn main() -> Result[Unit, Error]` with declared effects matching the session's accumulated effect set. Guarantee: the exported file compiles with `karac build` and produces identical observable behavior. If auto-clone was enabled, the inserted clones appear in the exported file unchanged.

- [ ] **Cross-cell providers ŌĆö `:provide R = expr` / `:end-provide R` meta-commands.** Open and close a long-lived `with_provider` scope spanning subsequent cells. Implementation steps: (1) parse the meta-command form (`:provide R = expr` consumes a resource ident + `=` + expr; `:end-provide R` consumes a resource ident); (2) maintain `Session.provider_stack: Vec<(ResourceId, Expr, FirstCellInScope)>` tracking active scopes in nesting order; (3) wrap each subsequent cell body inside an in-memory `with_provider[R](provider, || { cell_body })` when projecting the saved-session form, with one wrap per active stack entry; (4) at `:end-provide R`, pop the innermost matching frame and surface a structured error if `R` doesn't match the top of stack (LIFO close); (5) when a cell after `:end-provide` references a binding declared inside the closed scope, surface "cannot find value `X`" with a notebook-aware hint naming the provider scope that closed and the cell where `X` was declared (mirroring the use-after-move diagnostic shape from `Notebook-aware use-after-move diagnostic`); (6) construct the provider expr in the synthetic `:provide` cell ŌĆö if construction panics, the scope is not opened and the panic surfaces in the cell output. Closure-capture-and-escape becomes a special case of the binding-scope rule ŌĆö no separate handling. Saved-session form: each `:provide`/`:end-provide` pair compiles to one `with_provider[R](expr, || { /* cells in scope */ })` block; cell boundaries don't survive export. See `design.md ┬¦ Interactive Evaluation Model > Cross-Cell Providers` for the full contract.

- [ ] **Browser playground (`play.kara-lang.org` or equivalent).** Zero-install entry point hosting the interpreter behind a web frontend ŌĆö the adoption lever that does not require a local install. Architecture: server-side `karac repl` behind a minimal HTTP/WebSocket shim, or WASM-compiled interpreter running in the browser. Reach decision during implementation. Minimum UX: text editor, run button, output pane, share-by-URL. No stdlib fetch, no account, no persistence beyond URL sharing.

**P0 priority, P1 delivery ŌĆö ships with v1.1 alongside stable stdlib.**

- [ ] **Jupyter kernel MVP.** K─üra kernel implementing the `jupyter_client` ZMQ protocol: shell/iopub/stdin/control channels, cell execution returning `text/plain` for the last expression, stderr routing for diagnostics with **clickable source spans in JupyterLab** (diagnostic machinery already produces spans; protocol-level wiring exposes them). Ctrl+C cooperative interrupt wired to the existing cancellation mechanism. Tab completion over current-session identifiers + prelude. Packaging: `pip install karac-kernel` (precedent: `evcxr`, `IJava`) with a Python shim that locates the `karac` binary and registers the kernelspec. Kernel process itself is Rust; the Python package is only launcher + installer.

- [ ] **Jupyter `%magic` surface (MVP subset).** `%effects` (session-wide effect set + per-cell footer display), `%ownership` (current binding table with mode/RC status), `%explain <name>` (wrap `karac explain`), `%set auto-clone on|off` (toggle the opt-in ownership mode), `%provide R = expr` / `%end-provide R` (cross-cell provider scoping ŌĆö parity with the REPL meta-commands; same compilation path; see `design.md ┬¦ Cross-Cell Providers`). Per-cell effect footer renders on every cell execution automatically. `%rc` magic is **deferred to post-MVP** ŌĆö RC fallback analysis is still settling and its introspection surface is not yet stable enough to commit to.

**Stretch (P1+) ŌĆö post-MVP kernel.**

- [ ] **Rich display for structs and collections.** `text/html` table rendering for `Vec[Struct]` (one row per element, one column per field), `text/plain` pretty-printing for nested data, `image/png` for any stdlib plotting primitive that lands. Reflection-based ŌĆö uses the type registry already maintained by the type checker. Ships alongside plotting stdlib.

- [ ] **Effect-conflict timeline visualization.** Sidebar or cell-footer rendering showing per-cell effect set and cross-cell dependency arrows (e.g., "cell 3 reads `Files` written by cell 2"). Uses existing effect analysis output; purely a rendering concern in the kernel. Not a correctness concern (cells are sequential), but a teaching tool.

- [ ] **`%rc` magic.** List of RC-fallback decisions with trigger reasoning. Gated on RC-fallback diagnostic surface stabilizing.

- [ ] **Widget protocol (IPython-widgets equivalent).** Deep integration for interactive controls. v2+.

- [ ] **Provider control panel widget.** Sidebar UI showing active `with_provider` scopes (resource name, provider expr, opened-in-cell), with one-click `%end-provide` and per-cell-effect timeline annotations. Builds on the widget protocol above. Saved-session export ignores widget actions ŌĆö the underlying `:provide`/`:end-provide` log is what survives. Tracked separately because it uses the cross-cell-provider mechanism specifically and is the "data-science differentiator" UI for the v1.1+ kernel.

**Book coverage ŌĆö P0 prose (v1).**

- [ ] **"Getting Started, Part 2: Two Surfaces" chapter.** Dedicated chapter positioned right after "Getting Started / Installation." Shows the `.kara` file and `karac repl` terminal side by side on the same binary-search example, teaches the session model (cell scope, re-declaration, ownership across cells), and introduces the `:effects` / `:save` meta-commands. Browser playground gets a sidebar callout ("try without installing"). Ownership is taught honestly from day one ŌĆö the diagnostic-softening from Q2 means no retraction later when the reader graduates to compiled files. v1 surfaces only; notebook / Jupyter content lands in v1.1 either by extending this chapter to a third surface or by adding a standalone "Notebooks" chapter.

### 5.5: Package Manager (v1.1)

All entries here are v1.1 work ŌĆö v1 ships with the current parsed-but-ignored `[dependencies]` posture; this section flips it to load-bearing. Decisions are recorded in `design.md ┬¦ Package System`.

- [ ] **PubGrub resolver.** Port `pubgrub-rs` or roll a K─üra-side equivalent. Inputs: `[dependencies]` + `[dev-dependencies]` + `[target.X.dependencies]` constraints across the dependency graph; output: a concrete version per package or a structured conflict diagnostic naming the constraint chain. Conflict diagnostics show the full chain ("`A` requires `C >=1.0`; `B` requires `C >=2.0`"), not a single "no solution" message. Honors the MSRV constraint via `[package].kara-version` (see toolchain entry).

- [ ] **Lockfile (`kara.lock`) reader/writer.** Schema: package name, exact version, source URL (registry-proxy mirror or git URL), BLAKE3 content hash, resolver-output dependency tree. Single lockfile across all build targets. Writer is invoked by the resolver after a successful resolve; reader is consulted on every build to pin versions. Library-vs-binary commitment is encoded by which projects check the file in (no compiler-side enforcement).

- [ ] **`karac update` and `karac update <pkg>`.** Bare form bumps every dep to the newest version compatible with declared semver constraints; surgical form bumps a single package (and any deps newly required by its update). Both rewrite `kara.lock`.

- [ ] **Registry proxy client.** HTTP client that fetches packages through `proxy.kara-lang.org` (or equivalent configured proxy) by default. Records both the original git URL (for human readability) and the proxy mirror reference (for fetch reproducibility) into `kara.lock`. `--no-proxy` flag for direct-from-source fetches in development workflows. The proxy itself is separate infrastructure (not part of `karac`); this entry is the client side.

- [ ] **Build artifact cache (`~/.kara/cache/`).** Global cache of compiled deps keyed on `(compiler-version, package-version, edition, profile, target-triple)`. Two projects with the same dep version under the same compiler / edition / profile / target share a cached object. Per-project `dist/` is already in place. Auto-invalidate on compiler upgrade (cache key includes version); never invalidate on time.

- [x] **`karac clean` and `karac clean --global`.** Bare form removes the project `dist/`; `--global` removes the user-wide `~/.kara/cache/`. Both idempotent ŌĆö a missing directory is reported and treated as success. `--global` resolves the cache path from `$HOME` / `$USERPROFILE`. Commit `a5a516c`; tests in `tests/cli.rs` (`test_clean_bare_idempotent_when_no_dist`, `test_clean_bare_removes_existing_dist`, `test_clean_global_targets_kara_cache`).

- [ ] **`karac install <bin-spec>`.** Build a binary package and install it into `~/.kara/bin/`. Spec accepts `path = ...`, `git = ...`, or a registry-proxy reference. Useful pre-registry for path/git deps.
  - [x] Subcommand wired: parses `<bin-spec>` positional + help text; missing-spec errors; "not yet wired" diagnostic exits non-zero so CI scripts notice the gap ŌĆö commit `a5a516c`
  - [ ] Spec resolution against the manifest dependency-entry shape (`path = "..."` / `git = "..."` / bare registry-proxy reference / `name@version`)
  - [ ] Binary build through the existing build pipeline + install into `~/.kara/bin/` (depends on dep-resolution slice)

- [ ] **`karac vendor` and `karac build --offline`.** `karac vendor` copies all resolved dependencies into a `vendor/` directory at the project root. `karac build --offline` reads dependencies only from `vendor/` and refuses any network access. Air-gap workflow for regulated environments and offline CI.
  - [x] `karac vendor` subcommand wired: parses cleanly, rejects extra args, emits "not yet wired" diagnostic + non-zero exit ŌĆö commit `a5a516c`
  - [x] `--offline` flag added to existing `Build` / `BuildProject`; parses cleanly + emits "not yet wired" notice before falling through to normal behavior ŌĆö commit `a5a516c`
  - [ ] `karac vendor` actually copies resolved dependencies into `./vendor/` (depends on dep-resolution slice)
  - [ ] `karac build --offline` consults only `./vendor/` and refuses any network access (depends on dep-resolution slice + resolver hookpoint)

- [ ] **`[target.X.dependencies]` and `[target.X.profile]` parsing.** Extend `manifest.rs` to recognize per-target dependency and profile blocks. Resolver consults the active target triple (from `karac build --target X` or `[build].target` default) to merge the relevant target block into the dep graph.

- [ ] **`[dev-dependencies]` excluded from non-test builds.** Resolver and build pipeline already separate test compilation from non-test compilation; ensure `[dev-dependencies]` participate only in test-mode resolution. No new infrastructure ŌĆö wiring in the existing test/non-test split.

- [~] **`[package].kara-version` MSRV constraint.** Parser-side field capture shipped 2026-05-17; resolver enforcement against the active toolchain version (the diagnostic-emitting half) remains. The resolver enforcement is blocked on the dependency resolver landing (line 493 PubGrub) ŌĆö without a resolution pipeline there's nothing to report the constraint chain against.

  - [x] **Parser slice 1 ŌĆö `kara-version` field capture shipped 2026-05-17.** Spec sentence honoured for the parser half: *"Parser accepts the field"*. **Manifest extension** in `src/manifest.rs`: `Manifest.kara_version: Option<String>` field, populated from `[package].kara-version` in `kara.toml`. The field stores the raw version string verbatim ŌĆö no parsing-time interpretation of constraint syntax (`^1.0`, `>=1.2.3`, etc.) since the constraint comparator lives in the resolver alongside the active-toolchain lookup. `kara-version` is added to `KNOWN_PACKAGE_KEYS` so the unknown-key warning doesn't fire when the manifest declares it. **Validation at parse time:** wrong-type values (`kara-version = 1.0` ŌĆö TOML float) are rejected with `ManifestError::InvalidFieldType { key: "kara-version", expected: "a string version constraint" }`. Empty / whitespace-only strings (`kara-version = ""`, `kara-version = "   "`) are rejected with the same error kind but a more specific `expected` message ŌĆö an empty version string is more likely a mistake than an intentional "no constraint", and the no-constraint case is expressed by *omitting* the field. **Test surface (8 manifest tests in `src/manifest.rs::tests`)**: `kara_version_absent_is_none` (regression pin ŌĆö absent field stays `None`); `kara_version_captured_when_present` (positive ŌĆö basic `"1.0"` is captured verbatim with no warnings); `kara_version_accepts_semver_triple` (positive ŌĆö `"1.2.3"`); `kara_version_accepts_caret_constraint` (positive ŌĆö `"^1.0"`, pinning that the raw constraint syntax passes through unmolested for the resolver to interpret later); `kara_version_wrong_type_is_hard_error` (negative ŌĆö TOML float rejected); `kara_version_empty_string_is_hard_error` and `kara_version_whitespace_only_is_hard_error` (negative ŌĆö both flagged as InvalidFieldType); `kara_version_recognised_key_does_not_warn` (regression pin against a future refactor that drops `kara-version` from `KNOWN_PACKAGE_KEYS` ŌĆö would silently start emitting the unknown-key warning otherwise). **What slice 1 does *not* do.** No constraint-syntax parsing ŌĆö `"^1.0"` is stored as a raw string, not parsed into a structured `VersionReq`. No active-toolchain lookup ŌĆö the resolver doesn't yet read this field. No diagnostic when the constraint exceeds the active compiler version (the headline behavior the spec promises). All three land alongside the resolver work at line 493.

- [ ] **`karac-toolchain.toml` reader.** `karac` parses the file from project (or workspace) root and either delegates to `karaup` (when it exists) to switch toolchain, or ŌĆö if running standalone ŌĆö emits a diagnostic indicating the version mismatch and the recommended action. v1 schema: `version` (required), `targets` (optional list). Channels / components / install profiles deferred.

- [~] **`:dep` REPL meta-command.** Parse `:dep name = "..."` (accepting the same right-hand side shape as a `[dependencies]` entry). Mutate the session's in-memory manifest, drive the resolver against the new constraint, fetch + compile the package, and bring its surface into scope for subsequent cells. Failures (resolution conflict, network error, missing package) surface in the cell output and leave session state unchanged. State is in-memory only ŌĆö no implicit persistence. Closed 2026-05-01 *for the syntax-parsing + registry portion only*: new `Session.pending_deps: BTreeMap<String, String>` accumulates `name ŌåÆ normalized TOML value`; new `add_dep` parses the RHS by wrapping it as `[__kara_repl_dep__]\n{rest}\n` and leaning on the `toml` crate to validate the shape (bare semver string OR inline table ŌĆö `{ git = ... }` / `{ path = ... }` / `{ version = ... }`); failures surface `error: invalid \`:dep\` syntax ŌĆö ...` and leave state unchanged; success prints the recorded entry plus a v1.1 caveat note that the package's symbols are not yet in scope; `Session::pending_deps()` accessor exposed for the future package-manager wiring; `:help` updated. 9 tests in `tests/repl.rs`. The resolver / fetch / symbol-bring-into-scope plumbing is gated on the package-manager work (registry-proxy + resolver + lock-file, not yet shipped) and aligns with design.md's v1.1 tag for `:dep`.

- [ ] **`karac run <script>` script-dir manifest discovery.** Walk upward from the *script's own directory*, not cwd, looking for `kara.toml`. Implementation: factor the existing project-root walk in `cli.rs` to accept a starting path parameter; `karac run path/to/foo.kara` passes `dirname(path/to/foo.kara)` instead of cwd. `--manifest path/to/kara.toml` overrides; `--no-manifest` forces stdlib-only.

- [x] **`karac fix` CLI wrapper.** CLI subcommand that applies machine-applicable diagnostic fixes to disk. Closed 2026-05-03; rolled out across seven rounds. Initial dispatcher (2026-05-01) ŌĆö new `TextEdit { offset, length, replacement }` struct on `ResolveError` (boxed for `result_large_err` headroom), populated for E0228 (UndefinedName) and E0229 (UndefinedType); `cmd_fix` re-runs the resolver and applies edits in reverse-offset order with overlap dedupe; `--dry-run` preview; JSON envelope payload for IDE consumers. **Round 12.28** added E0225 (UnknownItemInModule). **Round 12.29** added E0223 (UnknownModule) ŌĆö required new `path_spans: Vec<Span>` on `ImportDecl` so the edit targets the misspelled prefix without disturbing the import's trailing item or `as alias` clause. **Round 12.30** wired `replacement` through the multi-file JSON / JSONL paths (`resolve_errors_json`, `resolve_errors_jsonl`); E0223 / E0225 only fire in multi-file mode, so the IDE-facing payload was previously unreachable for `karac build --output=json` / `karac test` consumers. **Round 12.31** extended `replacement` to the first non-resolver class (ownership N0507, UnusedMutCaptureNote, `mut ref` ŌåÆ `ref` rewrite over the closure prefix) ŌĆö required new `prefix_span: Option<Span>` on `ExprKind::Closure` and a `replacement` field on `OwnershipError`. **Round 12.32** swapped `cmd_fix` from a standalone resolver invocation to `Pipeline::run_all_checks()`, harvesting edits from resolver errors + ownership errors + ownership notes in one pass. The implementation diverged from the original "reads jsonl from a build invocation" sketch ŌĆö the in-process path is self-contained but emits the same JSON / JSONL payload externally. Original gating note honored (not v1.1-blocked, landed opportunistically). Remaining typechecker / effectchecker tagging tracked as a P2 entry in `deferred.md ┬¦ Machine-Applicable Replacement Metadata on Typechecker / Effectchecker Diagnostics`.
